## Question 169

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 169</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> You are planning to move from your hometown to Pittsburgh. Along the way, you stop in Columbus, Ohio to visit a relative and fall in love with the city! You decide to stay and make Columbus your new home. This is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. intervening opportunity.</li><li>B. distance decay.</li><li>C. involuntary migration.</li><li>D. push-pull factors.</li><li>E. transhumance.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>

## Question 261

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 261</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Human-induced environmental change is often referred to as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. anthropomorphic.</li><li>B. anthropocentric.</li><li>C. anthropogenic.</li><li>D. unsustainable.</li><li>E. environmental determinism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Anthropogenic, by definition, means human-induced changes on the physical environment. The other options are tricky only because they look similar to this term.</p>
</div>

## Question 262

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 262</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Conserving resources to ensure enough for future generations is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. subsistence agriculture.</li><li>B. sustainability.</li><li>C. cultural ecology.</li><li>D. environmental determinism.</li><li>E. the organic movement.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Sustainability is the idea of using Earth's resources in such a way that the needs of the current population are provided for without compromising the ability of future generations to use the same resources.</p>
</div>

## Question 263

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 263</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> ______________ argued that cultural landscapes should form the basic unit of geographic inquiry.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Ptolemy</li><li>B. George Perkins Marsh</li><li>C. Eratosthenes</li><li>D. Carl Sauer</li><li>E. W. D. Pattison</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Carl Sauer developed the notion of a cultural landscape to describe the parts of Earth's surface that have been modified by human activities. He also argued that virtually all of Earth's surface has in some way been affected by human activity and thus paved the way for environmental geography.</p>
</div>

## Question 264

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 264</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> A thematic layer is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a method used in cartography to produce mathematically accurate map projections.</li><li>B. a map portraying a particular feature that is used in a GIS.</li><li>C. used in GPS systems to provide more accurate navigational information.</li><li>D. a map used by early explorers to find particular resources in new regions of the earth.</li><li>E. used as a method to analyze thematic regions.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) The purpose of GIS is to provide a tool to understand and analyze spatial relationships between different phenomena better. This goal is accomplished by overlaying different thematic layers, or maps with different geographic information, on top of one another.</p>
</div>

## Question 265

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 265</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following is the oldest field of geography?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Cultural ecology</li><li>B. Conservation biology</li><li>C. Cartography</li><li>D. Environmental geography</li><li>E. Physical geography</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) The first geographers were primarily interested in exploration. Cartography allowed these first geographers to map the information gleaned from their expeditions.</p>
</div>

## Question 266

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 266</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> A perceptual region's boundaries are</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. determined by a set of uniform physical or cultural characteristics across a particular area.</li><li>B. drawn around the functions that occur between a particular place and the surrounding area.</li><li>C. determined by the portion of a particular area that has been modified by human activities.</li><li>D. fuzzy because they allow for individual interpretation.</li><li>E. designated by the inclusion of a particular cultural characteristic.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Perceptual regions are determined by commonly perceived characteristics of particular places on the earth's surface. Different individuals have different ideas about where these characteristics begin and end. Thus, the boundaries are necessarily fuzzy.</p>
</div>

## Question 267

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 267</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> If a geographer performs a study on people's perceptions of the Deep South using interviews as the primary data source, the geographer's method is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. quantitative.</li><li>B. systematic.</li><li>C. anthropogenic.</li><li>D. qualitative.</li><li>E. idiographic.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Qualitative data are more humanistic, often collected through interviews, empirical observations, and interpretation of texts, artwork, old maps, and other archives. Quantitative data are typically numerically based, understood, and evaluated with statistical methods.</p>
</div>

## Question 268

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 268</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Which of the following is true concerning regions?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They are strict functional units.</li><li>B. They are usually defined by a standard mathematical formula.</li><li>C. They are figments of the imagination.</li><li>D. They are conceptual units.</li><li>E. They all have well-defined boundaries.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Regions are an organizing tool that allow geographers to combine areas with similar features into one conceptual unit that provides them with a more manageable unit for analysis.</p>
</div>

## Question 269

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 269</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Geographic scale refers to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. the ratio between distance on a map and distance on Earth's surface.</li><li>B. a conceptual hierarchy of spaces.</li><li>C. a notion of place based on an individual's perception of space.</li><li>D. the many ways that people define regions.</li><li>E. the level of aggregation at which geographers investigate a particular process.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Geographic scale refers to a scale of analysis. It looks at phenomena through a hierarchy of scale such as neighborhood, city, state, and nation.</p>
</div>

## Question 270

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 270</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Seattle is located on Puget Sound in northwestern Washington. It has a large university, a famous downtown market, and a moist, marine climate. Seattle's primary economic activities include ship and aircraft construction and high-technology enterprises. This information gives us a description of Seattle's</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. situation.</li><li>B. cognitive image.</li><li>C. site.</li><li>D. landscape.</li><li>E. relative distance.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Site is a description of the qualities of a place, independent of that place's relationship to other places around it. Situation refers to a place's relationship to the other places around it.</p>
</div>

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 271</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Lines of longitude</p>
<ul class="qlist">

</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) All latitudes are parallel, but all lines of longitude converge at the North and South Poles. In many map projections
					</p></div>

## Question 272

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 272</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Even though some cities are far apart in terms of absolute distance, they are actually quite connected economically and socially. This is representative of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. topographic space.</li><li>B. cognitive space.</li><li>C. relative distance.</li><li>D. relative location.</li><li>E. situation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Relative distance the level of connectivity between places. Although some places may be quite far from each other in absolute space, in actuality they might be quite close in terms of the economic, social, and cultural relationships between them. New York and Los Angeles are much more connected in terms of economic and cultural relationships than are Los Angeles and Lincoln, Nebraska, even though Nebraska is much closer in absolute distance to Los Angeles.</p>
</div>

## Question 273

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 273</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following is a true statement regarding time-space convergence?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Places seem to all look the same.</li><li>B. Places seem to be getting closer together.</li><li>C. Places are increasingly concentrated on maintaining their histories.</li><li>D. Places are making more of an effort to converge activities to save time.</li><li>E. Places are implementing more rapid forms of transportation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Time-space convergence is the notion that distance between places seems to be "shrinking" with increased improvements in transportation and communication technologies.</p>
</div>

## Question 274

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 274</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following is NOT a measure of relative distance?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. 2,339 centimeters</li><li>B. 35 seconds</li><li>C. Two dollars and fifty cents</li><li>D. 216 footsteps</li><li>E. 15 minutes</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Since the centimeter is a standard unit of measurement, it is a measure of absolute distance that can be universally understood across the globe.</p>
</div>

## Question 275

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 275</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Tobler's First Law of Geography states, "Everything is related to everything else, but</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. distant things are generally unrelated."</li><li>B. near things are more closely related than you might think."</li><li>C. distance is always a factor."</li><li>D. near things are more related than distant things."</li><li>E. distance is relative."</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Tobler's First Law of Geography expresses the concept of distance decay. Generally, things are less related the farther away they are from each other in absolute space.</p>
</div>

## Question 276

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 276</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Rap music first appeared in New York in the 1970s. Later it spread to large cities with vibrant African American populations
						<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. relocation potential.</li><li>B. hierarchical diffusion.</li><li>C. contagious diffusion.</li><li>D. cultural diffusion.</li><li>E. cascade diffusion.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Hierarchical diffusion is the form of spatial diffusion that occurs when a phenomenon spreads from one place to another because the places have something in common. Large cities were the first to adopt rap music. Rap later spread to medium and small cities across the United States, but it has yet to be fully absorbed into many rural areas.</p>
</p></div>

## Question 277

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 277</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Stores and restaurants in Oregon that find it cheaper to buy fresh vegetables grown in California than to buy those grown in Florida are taking advantage of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. expansion diffusion.</li><li>B. distance decay.</li><li>C. economies of scale.</li><li>D. intervening opportunities.</li><li>E. retail gravitation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) An intervening opportunity exists when a closer source is available for the supply of some desired good or service. All else being equal, people tend to prefer closer sources of goods and services to those farther away.</p>
</div>

## Question 278

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 278</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> According to the gravity model, which two places are most likely to have a high level of interaction?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Two cities with very large populations but separated by the Atlantic Ocean like New York and London</li><li>B. Two cities with medium populations separated by a whole continent like Grand Rapids, Michigan, and Gulf Shores, Alabama</li><li>C. Two cities with small populations that are relatively close together like Richmond, Virginia, and Winchester, Kentucky</li><li>D. Two cities, one with a large population and the other with a medium population that are very close in distance like Seattle and Tacoma, Washington</li><li>E. Two cities with medium populations that are relatively close to each other like Akron, Ohio, and Springfield, Missouri</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) The gravity model predicts the level of interaction between two cities in terms of their populations and distances apart from one another. The correct option has a very large numerator (product of both populations) and a very small denominator (distance between Seattle and Tacoma). Thus, the resulting level of interaction will be quite high.</p>
</div>

## Question 279

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 279</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following is NOT a good example of a barrier to spatial diffusion?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A mountain range</li><li>B. A different language</li><li>C. A different dietary preference</li><li>D. A highway system</li><li>E. A strict religious system</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) A highway system facilitates diffusion because it connects places. In contrast, the other four options prevent certain innovations and cultural traits from spreading.</p>
</div>

## Question 280

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 280</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The ratio between distance on a map and distance on Earth's surface is called the</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. projection.</li><li>B. resolution.</li><li>C. scale.</li><li>D. azimuth.</li><li>E. aggregation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) In cartography, scale refers to the ratio of map distance to the distance on the earth's surface. Large-scale maps have a large ratio, such as 1:2,000. Small-scale maps have a small ratio, such as 1:200,000.</p>
</div>

## Question 281

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 281</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Cartography is the art and science of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. demographics.</li><li>B. mapmaking.</li><li>C. spatial orientation.</li><li>D. cognitive imagery.</li><li>E. making visualizations.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Cartography is the art and science of mapmaking. Cartography is an art because of the challenge of effectively communicating spatial information in an aesthetically pleasing way. It is a science because of the difficulty of transforming the three-dimensional Earth onto a two-dimensional piece of paper.</p>
</div>

## Question 282

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 282</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Map projections attempt to correct for errors in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. transferability.</li><li>B. area, distance, scale, and proportion.</li><li>C. area, distance, shape, and direction.</li><li>D. distance, proximity, and topology.</li><li>E. distance, shape, and lines of latitude and longitude.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Map projections represent attempts by cartographers to correct for the simple geometrical fact that a spherical or geoidal surface, such as Earth, cannot be accurately depicted on a two-dimensional surface. Map projections attempt to correct for errors in the area and shape of features on Earth's surface, errors in the distance between places, and errors in the compass direction from one place to another.</p>
</div>

## Question 283

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 283</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The Mercator projection preserves</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. direction.</li><li>B. area.</li><li>C. shape.</li><li>D. scale.</li><li>E. distance.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) The Mercator projection accurately preserves compass direction. However, because the lines of longitude do not meet at the poles in the Mercator projection as they do on the globe, area is distorted, with increasing inaccuracy at high latitudes.</p>
</div>

## Question 284

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 284</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Topographic maps use which of the following symbols to convey change over space?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Tonal shadings</li><li>B. Isolines</li><li>C. Proportional symbols</li><li>D. Location charts</li><li>E. Cartograms</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Isolines, or contours, are lines of equal value. Isolines are used on topographic maps to show the locations of places with equal elevation. Isolines are also commonly used for maps that represent spatial densities, such as population density or pollution concentration.</p>
</div>

## Question 285

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 285</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following map projections preserves the correct shape of Earth's landmasses?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Fuller projection</li><li>B. Mercator</li><li>C. Robinson</li><li>D. Mollewide</li><li>E. Smithsonian</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) The Fuller projection correctly preserves area and shape, although distance and direction are severely distorted.</p>
</div>

## Question 286

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 286</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> The size of a map's smallest discernable unit is its</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. scale.</li><li>B. density.</li><li>C. region.</li><li>D. resolution.</li><li>E. projection.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Resolution is important in geography. The smallest discernable unit is directly related to both the map's scale and to the amount of spatial data that can be displayed. Generally, large-scale maps have a greater resolution, although this is not always the case.</p>
</div>

## Question 287

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 287</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following regions is currently experiencing the fastest population growth?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Northern Asia</li><li>B. Tropical Africa</li><li>C. Eastern Europe</li><li>D. Sun Belt</li><li>E. Northeast United States</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Tropical Africa is one of the fastest-growing areas in the world. Increases in crop production and better access to medical care, combined with high fertility rates, have caused tremendous population growth throughout the region. Cities, like Lagos, Nigeria, are also among the fastest-growing urban areas anywhere. Although the Sun Belt region of the United States has grown rapidly since World War II, this growth is nowhere near as sudden or as dramatic as that of tropical Africa.</p>
</div>

## Question 288

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 288</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Most of the world's people live in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. the world's poorest countries.</li><li>B. the southern hemisphere.</li><li>C. the developed world.</li><li>D. China.</li><li>E. urban areas in the developed world.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Approximately 80% of the world's population lives in the less-developed countries, which include all of Africa, Asia (excluding Japan), Latin America, and the island nations of the Caribbean and Pacific.</p>
</div>

## Question 289

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 289</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Throughout human history, world population has</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. grown at a steady rate.</li><li>B. experienced numerous periods of dramatic decline.</li><li>C. been confined to countries in the southern hemisphere.</li><li>D. grown most rapidly over the last 200 years.</li><li>E. grown most rapidly in the developed world.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Human population has demonstrated overall steady growth throughout human history; however, in the last 200 years, population has been growing at exponential rates.</p>
</div>

## Question 290

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 290</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> ______________ occurs when a population is adding a fixed percentage of people to a growing population each year.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Doubling</li><li>B. Arithmetic growth</li><li>C. Overpopulation</li><li>D. Exponential growth</li><li>E. Demographic accounting</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) When you add a fixed number of people to a growing population each year, it is called arithmetic growth, but when you add a fixed percentage of people each year, it is called exponential growth. Exponential growth is compound, since the same percentage is being added to an increasing population each year; if the population is growing, then the same percentage will include more people next year than it does this year.</p>
</div>

## Question 291

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 291</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Life expectancy has increased</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. only in the most-developed countries.</li><li>B. only in the least-developed countries.</li><li>C. due to increased food production.</li><li>D. worldwide.</li><li>E. due to the Green Revolution.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Life expectancy varies both between countries and within countries and is related to many factors, including race, sex, and wealth.</p>
</div>

## Question 292

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 292</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The number of live births per thousand people per year is called the</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. total fertility rate.</li><li>B. natural increase rate.</li><li>C. crude birth rate.</li><li>D. exponential growth rate.</li><li>E. infant growth rate.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Many people get the total fertility rate (TFR) and the crude birth rate (CBR) mixed up. The TFR refers to the average number of children born to a woman over the course of her life.</p>
</div>

## Question 293

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 293</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Which of the following countries is most likely to be showing the lowest natural increase rate?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Afghanistan</li><li>B. Liechtenstein</li><li>C. United States</li><li>D. Japan</li><li>E. Chile</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Liechtenstein is a small, wealthy, and highly developed country located in the European Alps between Switzerland and Austria. Like other wealthy European countries with aging populations, Liechtenstein's growth rate is currently less than 1%.</p>
</div>

## Question 294

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 294</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Total fertility rate is NOT closely correlated with which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Industrial output</li><li>B. Gender empowerment</li><li>C. Education</li><li>D. Economic development</li><li>E. Literacy</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Although the total fertility rate is correlated with overall development, its relationship to industrial output is less direct. Small, highly developed countries, like Liechtenstein, may have little heavy industry but low fertility rates, while countries like Brazil may have much more industrial activity but much higher fertility rates. Gender empowerment, education, and general economic development are all closely correlated with fertility.</p>
</div>

## Question 295

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 295</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The demographic accounting equation does NOT take into account ______________ when calculating a country's population.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. the death rates</li><li>B. emigration</li><li>C. natural increase over time</li><li>D. instances when natural increase is negative</li><li>E. immigration</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) The demographic accounting equation predicts a country's future population on the basis of current birth rates, death rates, immigration rates, and emigration rates. It is not always a very accurate prediction, because these rates can change dramatically over time.</p>
</div>

## Question 296

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 296</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Within the United States, overall life expectancy</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. is limited by an unusually high infant mortality rate.</li><li>B. varies between various cohorts within the larger population.</li><li>C. varies between regions, with people in the Southwest living longer on average.</li><li>D. All of the above</li><li>E. Both (B) and (C)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) On average, white American males live longer than males of other races within the United States. Generally, life expectancy is calculated for particular countries; thus, it would be hard to determine regional variations in this statistic.</p>
</div>

## Question 297

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 297</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Millions of ______________ came to the United States during the early years of the 20th century.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. suburbanites</li><li>B. emigrants</li><li>C. immigrants</li><li>D. refugees</li><li>E. colonists</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) During the late 19th and early 20th centuries, millions of immigrants came to the United States from all over the world. Many came from southern and Western Europe in search of new economic opportunities.</p>
</div>

## Question 298

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 298</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> In the 1930s, thousands of "Okies" fled the Dust Bowl of the southern Great Plains and moved to the fertile agricultural regions of California to start a new life. This is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. external migration.</li><li>B. eco-migration.</li><li>C. political migration.</li><li>D. economic migration.</li><li>E. forced migration.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) The Dust Bowl refugees, often called Okies, left the southern Great Plains because of the environmental disaster of the Dust Bowl. When people leave an area because of environmental factors, it is called eco-migration.</p>
</div>

## Question 299

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 299</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Which of the following is the result of chain migration?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The African slave trade</li><li>B. French colonial rule</li><li>C. The formation of Israel</li><li>D. San Francisco's Chinatown</li><li>E. Colonization of the American frontier</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Ethnic urban enclaves, such as San Francisco's Chinatown, result when people follow those who went before them in migrating from one region to another. Chinatown has been an attractive place for many Chinese immigrants to settle after arriving in the United States because of the neighborhood's familiar language and customs.</p>
</div>

## Question 300

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 300</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Refugees are produced through</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. cultural migration.</li><li>B. forced migration.</li><li>C. internal migration.</li><li>D. economic migration.</li><li>E. chain migration.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Refugees, by definition, are people who are forced to leave their homes and move to a new place. Refugees can be produced through any type of forced migration, such as religious persecution, environmental degradation, or even natural disasters.</p>
</div>

## Question 301

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 301</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Many recent college graduates and young professionals move to large, vibrant cities
						<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. economic factors.</li><li>B. mobility opportunities.</li><li>C. suburban amenities.</li><li>D. pull factors.</li><li>E. push factors.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Pull factors include anything that draws someone from one place to another. Cities provide strong pull factors for young people looking for economic opportunities and recreational diversions.</p>
</p></div>

## Question 302

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 302</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Suburbanization is most evident in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. older American cities like Boston.</li><li>B. large European cities like Madrid.</li><li>C. regionally planned Canadian cities like Toronto.</li><li>D. newer American cities like Las Vegas.</li><li>E. large South American cities like Sao Paulo.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Most newer American cities, and newer areas of older American cities, have been designed to accommodate sprawling suburban housing communities and wide highways geared for automobile transportation. Although some European cities have been affected by sprawl, it is much less of a problem in countries like France and Germany, where people tend to live in older neighborhoods and the car is less important for transportation. Some Canadian cities, such as Toronto, have limited sprawl through well-coordinated urban planning.</p>
</div>

## Question 303

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 303</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> The Sun Belt includes</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. the Rocky Mountain States.</li><li>B. Alabama and Louisiana.</li><li>C. Texas and New Mexico.</li><li>D. Southern Nevada, southern California, and South Florida.</li><li>E. Florida, Georgia, Alabama, and South Carolina.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Parts of the Rocky Mountains, the Old South, and the Southwest are all considered to be within the Sun Belt. However, each of these regions also contains areas that have not benefited from the economic growth associated from the Sun Belt phenomenon. Southern Nevada, southern California, and South Florida are all classic Sun Belt regions.</p>
</div>

## Question 304

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 304</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Thomas Malthus predicted that</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. technology will offset population growth.</li><li>B. the distribution of resources would be a continuing problem.</li><li>C. population would outpace food production.</li><li>D. the environment would allow less food to be grown in the future.</li><li>E. the Green Revolution would provide agricultural technology to support increasing populations.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Thomas Malthus predicted that food production would grow arithmetically while population would grow geometrically (exponentially). Malthus's theory has been criticized because it does not account for other factors affecting food production and population, such as technology, the distribution of food resources, personal choice, and environmental change.</p>
</div>

## Question 305

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 305</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Which of the following countries is at stage two of the demographic transition model?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. San Marino</li><li>B. Nigeria</li><li>C. Denmark</li><li>D. Russia</li><li>E. Finland</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) In stage two of the demographic transition model, a country's population growth is high because death rates have decreased but birth rates have not. Nigeria's explosive population growth is an example of this situation. Denmark, Russia, and San Marino have all advanced to stage three, in which fertility decreases and population growth slows down.</p>
</div>

## Question 306

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 306</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> A rectangle-shaped population pyramid indicates a country that is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. growing slowly or not at all.</li><li>B. growing rapidly.</li><li>C. experiencing high immigration rates.</li><li>D. composed mainly of the older age classes.</li><li>E. highly dependent on the economically productive generations.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) A triangle-shaped population pyramid indicates that there is a high percentage of young people in the population and that it is growing rapidly. A rectangle-shaped age-sex distribution means that the population is composed of a more even range of older and younger people and that the population is growing slowly or not at all.</p>
</div>

## Question 307

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 307</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The baby boom</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. occurred in the years following World War I.</li><li>B. was a result of free love during the late 1960s.</li><li>C. was fostered by economic prosperity and relative peace.</li><li>D. was limited to California and the West.</li><li>E. was described by the off-beat author Douglas Coupland.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) The baby boom, which occurred during the years following World War II, was a national phenomenon in which economic prosperity and relative peace were accompanied by high fertility rates. Although fertility began to decline as early as the late 1940s, the baby boom generation became the most numerous, wealthiest, and most prosperous generation in American history.</p>
</div>

## Question 308

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 308</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> When baby boomers have reached retirement age, what will the population pyramid for the United States look like?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. An hourglass, wide at both top and bottom but narrow in the middle</li><li>B. Relatively rectangular, with a slight bulge near the top</li><li>C. Carrot-shaped, a narrow bottom and wide top</li><li>D. Pear-shaped, wide at the bottom, but narrow at the top</li><li>E. None of these</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) The baby boom is a large cohort of the American population, larger than the generation behind them. When they reach retirement age, their bracket, near the top of the pyramid, will most likely be larger than other segments of the pyramid. This demonstrates the magnitude of the dependency ratio, or number of individuals relying on younger, economically productive generations for support.</p>
</div>

## Question 309

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 309</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following countries would you expect to have the densest population?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. China</li><li>B. Peru</li><li>C. Mexico</li><li>D. Belgium</li><li>E. Colombia</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Small northern European countries, such as the Netherlands and Belgium, are some of the most densely populated in the world. China has the largest population of any country on Earth, yet its immense size allows for large, sparsely populated rural areas to remain.</p>
</div>

## Question 310

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 310</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Carrying capacity is a function of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. echnology.</li><li>B. natural resources.</li><li>C. resource allocation.</li><li>D. limiting factors.</li><li>E. (A), (B), and (D)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) The quality and quantity of natural resources available in an area and technological innovations that help people to use those resources both affect carrying capacity. The limiting factor describes the resource in scarcest supply within a region and thus provides a method for understanding how big a population an area can adequately sustain. However, the limiting factor within a region can be extended by use of technological innovations. Because of this, carrying capacity changes over time and is notoriously hard to pin down.</p>
</div>

## Question 311

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 311</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Population policy usually involves limitations on</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. fertility levels.</li><li>B. immigration levels.</li><li>C. education levels.</li><li>D. All of the above</li><li>E. Both (A) and (B)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) These two forces, births and immigration, are the largest contributors to population increase within a country. Humane population policy usually seeks to limit or decrease somehow the fertility level within a country, or it seeks to limit the number of individuals allowed into a particular country.</p>
</div>

## Question 312

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 312</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> India and China are the world's two most populous countries. While China has instituted a strict population policy, India</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. for cultural reasons, encourages women to continue to reproduce.</li><li>B. does not endorse birth control because of the Catholic majority.</li><li>C. encourages lower fertility through education and access to family planning.</li><li>D. has a similar policy to China.</li><li>E. because of its agricultural system, encourages reproduction.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Population policies implemented within countries usually reflect the country's prevailing ideologies and, thus, usually its political system. China is a communist-controlled country, which was demonstrated in their strict enforcement of their one-child policy. However, India is a democratic nation that encourages, rather than demands, lower fertility through increased education and access to family planning.</p>
</div>

## Question 313

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 313</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Cultural geography is the study of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. global customs and artifacts.</li><li>B. cultural complexes.</li><li>C. the spatial distribution of cultural traits.</li><li>D. human-environment relationships.</li><li>E. how cultures change through time.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Cultural geographers do study customs, artifacts, cultural complexes, and human-environment relationships; however, what makes cultural geography different from other disciplines, like anthropology, is its focus on the spatial distribution and diffusion of human cultures.</p>
</div>

## Question 314

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 314</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Throughout history, numerous colonial powers have argued that certain types of people, living in certain areas of the world, are less able to govern themselves because of the qualities they have developed due to their interactions with natural factors, such as climate. This is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. environmental determinism.</li><li>B. cultural ecology.</li><li>C. possibilism.</li><li>D. ecumenism.</li><li>E. positivism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Environmental determinism is the notion that human traits or historical events are directly attributable to environmental factors, that people's actions are determined by environmental factors. This idea has been discredited as simplistic and racist. Possibilism, the notion that humans have agency and yet are limited somewhat by the environmental surroundings, provides an attractive alternative to environmental determinism.</p>
</div>

## Question 315

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 315</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Cultural traditions, such as Christmas, are ____________ since they borrow from the past and are continually reinvented in the present.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. erratic</li><li>B. inauthentic</li><li>C. complex</li><li>D. syncretic</li><li>E. ecumenical</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) The term "syncretic" refers to something, such as a cultural tradition, that borrows from multiple sources.</p>
</div>

## Question 316

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 316</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The cultural hearth of Christianity is in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. New York.</li><li>B. Rome.</li><li>C. Israel.</li><li>D. South Carolina.</li><li>E. Turkey.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Rome is the center and headquarters of Catholicism, which is the largest wing of Christianity. However, the hearth, or birthplace, of Christianity is in Israel, where Jesus was born and lived his life.</p>
</div>

## Question 317

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 317</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Wooden shoes characteristic of the Dutch culture are an example of a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. mentifact.</li><li>B. artifact.</li><li>C. custom.</li><li>D. syncretism.</li><li>E. complex.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Artifacts are the material aspects of a particular culture and would include such things as wooden shoes or other fashion apparel, along with artwork or tools.</p>
</div>

## Question 318

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 318</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The most widespread language family on Earth is the</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Sino-Tibetan.</li><li>B. Romance.</li><li>C. Germanic.</li><li>D. Indo-European.</li><li>E. Mandarin Chinese.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) The Indo-European family includes the Romance and Germanic groups. About 50% of the world's people speak Indo-European languages.</p>
</div>

## Question 319

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 319</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> People in London, Melbourne, Vancouver, and Mumbai all speak</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a pidgin language.</li><li>B. lingua francas.</li><li>C. different dialects.</li><li>D. official languages.</li><li>E. different Creoles.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Although many people in all of these cities speak English, the versions of English that they speak all vary somewhat in pronunciation, spelling, and other characteristics.</p>
</div>

## Question 320

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 320</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Acculturation is a common cause of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. illiteracy.</li><li>B. language extinction.</li><li>C. assimilation.</li><li>D. creolization.</li><li>E. cultural diffusion.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Literally thousands of languages are currently in danger of becoming extinct. Reasons for language extinctions include genocide, cultural collapse, and acculturation.</p>
</div>

## Question 321

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 321</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> A simple trade language is called a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. lingua franca.</li><li>B. pidgin.</li><li>C. dialect.</li><li>D. Creole.</li><li>E. syncretic.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Simple trade languages are called lingua francas and use terms developed and understood by both cultures to complete economic transactions.</p>
</div>

## Question 322

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 322</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Literacy rates vary by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. sex.</li><li>B. location.</li><li>C. education.</li><li>D. economic development.</li><li>E. All of the above</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) Sex, geographic location, education, and economic development are all factors affecting literacy rates. In many countries where women are prevented from attaining education, women's literacy rates are considerably lower then men's.</p>
</div>

## Question 323

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 323</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> All evangelical religions are also</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. local religions.</li><li>B. universal religions.</li><li>C. animist religions.</li><li>D. ethnic religions.</li><li>E. polytheistic religions.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) A universal religion is one that seeks to unite people from different backgrounds under one all-encompassing faith. Christianity is the best example of an evangelical, universalizing religion.</p>
</div>

## Question 324

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 324</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Local Native American and African religions that teach a belief in a natural world full of spiritual beings and supernatural powers are often referred to as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. animist.</li><li>B. shamanistic.</li><li>C. missionary.</li><li>D. denominational.</li><li>E. local religions.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Many animist religions also include a shamanistic aspect. However, shamanism itself refers specifically to beliefs in which a single person takes on supernatural and healing powers.</p>
</div>

## Question 325

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 325</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The world's most widespread religion is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Islam.</li><li>B. Animism.</li><li>C. Christianity.</li><li>D. Hinduism.</li><li>E. Buddhism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) With about 2.4 billion believers, Christianity is the most widespread world religion. Islam is the second largest, and Hinduism is the third.</p>
</div>

## Question 326

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 326</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The hearth and spiritual center of Islam is at</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Baghdad.</li><li>B. Cairo.</li><li>C. Jakarta.</li><li>D. Mecca.</li><li>E. Jerusalem.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Mecca is the hearth and holy city of Islam. Many Muslims face Mecca and pray several times each day.</p>
</div>

## Question 327

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 327</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> ____________ is an excellent example of a nonevangelical, universalizing religion.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Christianity</li><li>B. Buddhism</li><li>C. Protestantism</li><li>D. Polytheism</li><li>E. Hinduism</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Buddhism teaches beliefs about the nature of life and human suffering that are universally applicable, yet its adherents generally do not attempt to recruit followers.</p>
</div>

## Question 328

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 328</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> In ____________ religions, community, common history, and social relations are inextricably intertwined with spiritual beliefs.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. monotheistic</li><li>B. local</li><li>C. evangelical</li><li>D. ethnic</li><li>E. universal</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) In ethnic religions, culture, history, public life, and spiritual beliefs are interwoven. Examples of ethnic religions include Judaism and Hinduism.</p>
</div>

## Question 329

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 329</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> An ethnicity is defined as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a group of people with a common history.</li><li>B. a group of people with similar physical characteristics.</li><li>C. a group of people who share a common identity.</li><li>D. a group of people united against a common enemy.</li><li>E. a group of people with a similar religion.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Whereas race connotes common physical characteristics, ethnicity connotes a common identity. Because people's outward traits do not necessarily say anything about their personal identities, and because the notion of race is associated with prejudice and superficiality, ethnicity has largely replaced it as a way of grouping people.</p>
</div>

## Question 330

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 330</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> In the 1990s, the United States</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. became less ethnically diverse.</li><li>B. decreased in overall population.</li><li>C. saw few changes in its ethnic composition.</li><li>D. saw dramatic changes in its ethnic composition.</li><li>E. remained relatively homogenous in its ethnic makeup.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) During the 1990s, large-scale immigration from Asia and Latin America dramatically changed the ethnic composition of the United States, making it a truly polyglot nation. In some areas, whites are no longer a majority.</p>
</div>

## Question 331

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 331</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> A group of people, all of the same ethnicity, live in the same area of a city near a nuclear waste facility. This is an example of a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. diaspora.</li><li>B. ghetto.</li><li>C. cultural landscape.</li><li>D. ethnic neighborhood.</li><li>E. gentrified neighborhood.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) A ghetto is a form of an ethnic neighborhood where individuals of a particular ethnicity are essentially forced to live. They usually exist in areas of a city where most individuals would rather not live, such as near a nuclear waste facility.</p>
</div>

## Question 332

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 332</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which is the most characteristic statement of a folk culture?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They look virtually the same anywhere on the globe.</li><li>B. Individuals within the culture specialize in producing specific goods for the community.</li><li>C. They quickly adopt new techniques useful for their community.</li><li>D. They have a subsistence economy.</li><li>E. They have weak ties to friends and family.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Folk cultures vary significantly over space as opposed to pop culture, which looks similar everywhere you encounter it. Also, pop culture is characterized by a consumer economy, whereas folk cultures practice a subsistence economy; individuals usually do not specialize in any one activity but instead provide multiple goods and skills for the community.</p>
</div>

## Question 333

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 333</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> A ______________ is a group of people with a common political identity, and a ______________ is a country with recognized borders.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. territory . . . federalism</li><li>B. nation . . . territory</li><li>C. state . . . nation</li><li>D. nation . . . state</li><li>E. territory . . . state</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Although the terms "nation" and "state" are often used interchangeably, they actually have specific and quite different definitions. Nation connotes a common sense of political identity, while a state has an official government and geographic borders.</p>
</div>

## Question 334

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 334</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> ______________ governments are organized into a geographically based hierarchy of local government agencies.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Federal</li><li>B. Territorial</li><li>C. Consolidated</li><li>D. Electoral</li><li>E. National</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) A federal system is a form of territorial, or geographically subdivided, organization in which governments give their constituent territories some degree of autonomy. Federal governments are frequently broken down into states, counties, parishes or other local areas, municipalities, voting districts, and so on, each of which has specific powers within its borders.</p>
</div>

## Question 335

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 335</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> With its system of regional provinces, Canada is an example of a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. microstate.</li><li>B. electoral state.</li><li>C. reapportioned state.</li><li>D. federal state.</li><li>E. nation-state.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Canada, like the United States and Mexico, has a federally organized government in which power is distributed to local areas, in this case, regional provinces.</p>
</div>

## Question 336

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 336</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The drawing of new voting districts is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. reapportionment.</li><li>B. gerrymandering.</li><li>C. reelection.</li><li>D. redrawing.</li><li>E. discretization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) After a census, the demographic data collected is used to form more accurate boundaries around voting districts to ensure fair representation within a political district. This process is called reapportionment or redistricting.</p>
</div>

## Question 337

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 337</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> When voting districts are redrawn in such a way that they purposely favor a political party, they have been</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. vetoed.</li><li>B. reapportioned.</li><li>C. redistricted.</li><li>D. gerrymandered.</li><li>E. reelected.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) The purposeful drawing of a political district to favor a political party is called gerrymandering, named both for the first person accused of doing this, and also for the shape of the first gerrymandered district, which resembled the shape of a salamander.</p>
</div>

## Question 338

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 338</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Indonesia is an example of a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. elongated state.</li><li>B. microstate.</li><li>C. compact state.</li><li>D. fragmented state.</li><li>E. prorupted state.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Indonesia consists of about 13,000 islands and islets scattered throughout the giant Malay Archipelago. Because the country is separated into so many small pieces, it is referred to as fragmented. Elongated states, like Chile, are stretched long and thin, and compact states, like Poland, are nearly circular.</p>
</div>

## Question 339

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 339</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Which of the following is a landlocked country?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Peru</li><li>B. Germany</li><li>C. Burma</li><li>D. Afghanistan</li><li>E. Colombia</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Landlocked countries have no outlet to the ocean. Surprisingly few countries are fully landlocked
					</p></div>

## Question 340

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 340</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> In Antarctica, geometric political borders do little to organize a vast</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. frontier.</li><li>B. borderland.</li><li>C. wasteland.</li><li>D. tundra.</li><li>E. territory.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Several countries have claimed portions of Antarctica as their own; however, these territorial claims have little meaning on the ground. In 1959, 12 countries signed an international treaty establishing large portions of the continent as an international commons, protected for conservation and scientific research.</p>
</div>

## Question 341

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 341</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> ______________ forces work to pull countries apart, while ______________ forces work to bind them together.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Centripetal . . . centrifugal</li><li>B. Centrifugal . . . centripetal</li><li>C. Communist . . . democratic</li><li>D. Capitalist . . . socialist</li><li>E. Socialist . . . centripetal</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Forces such as regionalism are centrifugal, meaning that they work to weaken central authority and cohesiveness, while forces such as nationalism generally work to solidify central authority and bind countries together.</p>
</div>

## Question 342

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 342</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> When one country exerts political, economic, or social influence over another without the aid of official government institutions, it is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. dominance.</li><li>B. imperialism.</li><li>C. colonialism.</li><li>D. federalism.</li><li>E. territorialism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Colonialism involves official institutional domination of one group over another; imperialism usually includes unofficial forms of social, cultural, or economic dominance.</p>
</div>

## Question 343

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 343</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> For many years, French Canadians from Quebec sought ______________, or the right to govern themselves and to establish their own independent state.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. nationalism</li><li>B. self-determination</li><li>C. anticolonialism</li><li>D. reapportionment</li><li>E. colonization</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) For many years Canadians of French descent have struggled to maintain their political autonomy and cultural heritage. In recent years, separatist movements have waned, but citizens of Quebec still fiercely defend their unique history, language, and traditions.</p>
</div>

## Question 344

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 344</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Hitler's nationalist/expansionist philosophies drew in part from</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. self-determination.</li><li>B. sound historical evidence.</li><li>C. organic geopolitical theory.</li><li>D. rimland theory.</li><li>E. heartland theory.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Organic geopolitical theory, which held that states must expand their land base in order to grow and maintain viability, influenced many 19th and 20th century nationalist politicians, including Adolf Hitler.</p>
</div>

## Question 345

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 345</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> When countries come together for a common purpose, somewhat limiting their own individual powers, the resulting body is called a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. international organization.</li><li>B. confederacy.</li><li>C. supranational organization.</li><li>D. union.</li><li>E. national alliance.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) In supranational organizations member states must give up some dimension of their individual autonomy for some greater cause, such as political or economic security. In international organizations, no such sacrifice is called for.</p>
</div>

## Question 346

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 346</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> OPEC is an example of a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. supranational organization.</li><li>B. commonwealth.</li><li>C. confederacy.</li><li>D. international organization.</li><li>E. national organization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) In OPEC, petroleum-exporting countries have joined together to regulate and stabilize oil markets around the world. This is an example of an international organization based on economic gain.</p>
</div>

## Question 347

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 347</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The ______________ was based on control of land, markets, and political ideology, whereas the ______________ is based on wealth and poverty.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. east/west divide . . . north/south divide</li><li>B. domino theory . . . heartland theory</li><li>C. north/south divide . . . east/west divide</li><li>D. organic theory . . . rimland theory</li><li>E. core/periphery . . . east/west divide</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) During the Cold War, countries were aligned on either side of an east/west divide, based largely on control of land and political ideology. In the post
					</p></div>

## Question 348

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 348</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> ______________ boundaries characterize much of Africa as they ignore cultural and tribal differences across space.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Superimposed</li><li>B. Subsequent</li><li>C. Colonial</li><li>D. Antecedent</li><li>E. Territorial</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) During colonialism, many nations imposed political boundaries designating certain territories for themselves without paying attention to any divisions they may have caused between different tribes. Even after decolonization, these boundaries remain, causing much of the bloodshed that has occurred and will continue to occur on this continent.</p>
</div>

## Question 349

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 349</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The first agriculturalists were</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. commercial farmers.</li><li>B. European entrepreneurs.</li><li>C. also hunter-gatherers.</li><li>D. also ranchers.</li><li>E. most likely males.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Hunter-gatherers were the first individuals to domesticate plants and animals. Even after domesticating certain species, most hunter-gatherers continued hunting and gathering to round out their diet.</p>
</div>

## Question 350

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 350</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Slash-and-burn agriculture is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. not sustainable.</li><li>B. practiced in high, mountainous regions.</li><li>C. typical for tropical forests.</li><li>D. a relatively new invention.</li><li>E. always completely sustainable.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Slash-and-burn agriculture is an agricultural method that introduces nutrients into the soil through burning of organic matter. It occurs mostly in tropical forests, where the soil is rather nutrient poor, as a way to increase soil productivity. Slash and burn can be unsustainable if farmers who practice it do not allow the land enough time to regenerate itself. Generally, the system of shifting cultivation can be quite sustainable if managed sensibly.</p>
</div>

## Question 351

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 351</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The Industrial Revolution transformed Western agriculture</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. through mechanization and the creation of new markets.</li><li>B. with biotechnology.</li><li>C. through technological and religious change.</li><li>D. by eliminating agricultural pests.</li><li>E. by eliminating plant hybridization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) During the Industrial Revolution, many people migrated from rural areas to large urban centers, generating a great need for agricultural goods within those centers. Furthermore, the technology characteristic of the Industrial Revolution transformed agricultural production as mechanization allowed for much more rapid cultivation of greater expanses of land.</p>
</div>

## Question 352

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 352</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The Green Revolution greatly increased crop production in some countries</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. without adverse side effects.</li><li>B. as a replacement for deindustrialization.</li><li>C. with some adverse side effects.</li><li>D. by encouraging the cultivation of local crop varieties.</li><li>E. by introducing organic agricultural methods.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) The Green Revolution brought technology, miracle seeds, fertilizer, and other inventions of the developed world into developing nations to stimulate agricultural growth. While certainly these new inputs led to increased agricultural productivity, they carried with them detrimental implications for the local natural environment.</p>
</div>

## Question 353

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 353</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following was NOT a location of independent plant and animal domestication?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. India</li><li>B. Iraq</li><li>C. California</li><li>D. China</li><li>E. Peru</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Although many people associate the Fertile Crescent with the first site of agricultural activity, in reality, several other places across the globe independently began domesticating plants and animals for human sustenance at around the same time. California, although currently an extremely important location of agricultural activity, was not one of these first hearths.</p>
</div>

## Question 354

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 354</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Ranching is a good example of which type of agricultural system?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Intensive subsistence cultivation</li><li>B. Extensive commercial cultivation</li><li>C. Labor-intensive agriculture</li><li>D. Capital-intensive agriculture</li><li>E. Controlled agriculture</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Ranching is an agricultural activity that takes place over large expanses of land and as such is a good representative of an extensive commercial agricultural activity. Additionally, it does not require either large amounts of human labor or capital inputs.</p>
</div>

## Question 355

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 355</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The modern global geography of agriculture is determined by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. climate.</li><li>B. soil.</li><li>C. cultural traditions.</li><li>D. All of the above</li><li>E. Only (A)and (B)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Geographers are concerned with what is grown where on the earth's surface. Both currently and historically, climate, soil, and cultural traditions determine this pattern. With increasing technology, these factors are losing their potency, but they still remain the dominant forces in the world's current agricultural mosaic.</p>
</div>

## Question 356

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 356</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> According to von Thunen, the regional geography of agriculture is determined by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. land area.</li><li>B. rent.</li><li>C. urban marketing.</li><li>D. availability of material inputs.</li><li>E. climate.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) According to the von Thunen model, the land located nearest the market will have the highest rent. Generally, agricultural activities that occur in this region are those that are expensive to transport and require intensive cultivation.</p>
</div>

## Question 357

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 357</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> ___________ is (are) widespread in semiarid climates throughout the world.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Ranching</li><li>B. Tropical plantations</li><li>C. Dairying</li><li>D. Slash-and-burn agriculture</li><li>E. Rice paddies</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Ranching takes place in the drier climates across the globe, where wide expanses of land that are not very good for cultivation exist. Both tropical plantations and slash-and-burn agriculture exist in warm, moist climates, and dairying usually exists in cooler climates, such as northern Europe and the northern United States.</p>
</div>

## Question 358

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 358</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The effects of biotechnology</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. are positive because it allows for much greater agricultural yields.</li><li>B. are negative because its expense limits its availability to all farmers across the globe.</li><li>C. are unknown because very little research has been conducted on them.</li><li>D. All of the above</li><li>E. None of the above</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) While the effects of biotechnology have not been critically investigated, it still is affecting global agricultural production, allowing for much greater yields of certain products. Because the processes of biotechnology are patented by private companies, only large agribusinesses can afford them, thereby limiting their use.</p>
</div>

## Question 359

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 359</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Agribusiness has had all of the following effects on agriculture, EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. the farm is no longer the center of agricultural activity.</li><li>B. TNCs often control agricultural activity abroad.</li><li>C. family farmers, through increasing technology, are producing goods for the global economy.</li><li>D. agriculture has become a multilevel process of production, processing, marketing, and consumption.</li><li>E. some corporations essentially dictate agricultural production in other countries besides their own.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Agribusiness has largely contributed to the demise of the family farm. As agriculture becomes increasingly controlled by large corporations that have the technology to mass produce goods without much human capital, it loses its need for human labor. Furthermore, the agricultural activities that require large amounts of labor have been relocated to parts of the globe where human labor is cheaper.</p>
</div>

## Question 360

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 360</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> In arid climates, like southern California and the Middle East, ___________ can cause the soil to become salty and infertile.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. erosion</li><li>B. topsoil loss</li><li>C. salinization</li><li>D. saltation</li><li>E. droughts</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Salinization occurs when arid environments use irrigation to provide enough moisture for plant production. When the water evaporates, it leaves a salty residue, which eventually causes the soil's infertility.</p>
</div>

## Question 361

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 361</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> ___________ is a common cause of decreasing farmland in rapidly growing urban areas.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Urban sprawl</li><li>B. Topsoil loss</li><li>C. Loss of material inputs</li><li>D. Industrialization</li><li>E. Agribusiness</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) As urban areas continue to expand outward, usually in the form of suburbs, the development often takes over agricultural land.</p>
</div>

## Question 362

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 362</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> DDT is an example of a ___________ that has had negative effects all the way through the food chain.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. herbicide</li><li>B. pesticide</li><li>C. bacteria</li><li>D. fungicide</li><li>E. genetically modified organism</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) The effects of DDT, made known by Rachel Carson in <i>Silent Spring</i>, demonstrate the various detriments pesticide use has all the way through the food chain. All the other options may too have effects through the food chain, but DDT is a pesticide specifically designed to eliminate insects, or pests, that threaten certain agricultural products.</p>
</div>

## Question 363

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 363</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Soil specialists must work to overcome the negative effects of ___________ associated with agricultural production.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. fertilization and salinization</li><li>B. pesticides and fertilization</li><li>C. salinization and topsoil loss</li><li>D. topsoil loss and gentrification</li><li>E. the Green Revolution and agribusiness</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Chemical fertilizers may cause negative effects on the soil, but some forms of fertilizers are organic, meaning that they use natural products rather than chemicals to stimulate plant growth and, therefore, do not harm the soil. Both salinization and topsoil loss destroy the soil's properties and must be overcome by soil scientists if they want the land to remain fertile.</p>
</div>

## Question 364

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 364</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The first cities arose in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. ancient Greece.</li><li>B. hearths of early agriculture.</li><li>C. the Indian subcontinent.</li><li>D. central Mexico.</li><li>E. near the equator.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) The first cities only developed after sedentary agriculture advanced to the point at which crop surpluses allowed some people to take up professions other than farming, such as brick laying and carpentry. When and where this occurred, the first cities arose.</p>
</div>

## Question 365

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 365</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Some prominent Native American cities later became</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. manufacturing hubs.</li><li>B. agricultural distribution centers.</li><li>C. gateway cities.</li><li>D. colonial cities.</li><li>E. export-processing zones.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Mexico City is just one example of a great Native American city (Tenochtitlan) that eventually became a center of colonial government administration and military might. Colonial powers used these cities as bases from which to dominate people in the surrounding countryside.</p>
</div>

## Question 366

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 366</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The Industrial Revolution</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. had little impact on urban areas.</li><li>B. spawned vast manufacturing centers.</li><li>C. began in the Great Lakes region.</li><li>D. made factory workers obsolete.</li><li>E. caused an urban-to-rural migration.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Chicago is the classic example of a city that was born during the Industrial Revolution and then experienced tremendous growth, becoming a great center of manufacturing, processing, and transportation.</p>
</div>

## Question 367

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 367</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> _______________ is an important gateway city.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Oslo, Norway,</li><li>B. Perth, Australia,</li><li>C. Nairobi, Kenya,</li><li>D. Honolulu, Hawaii,</li><li>E. Denver, Colorado,</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Honolulu's extremely strategic location, isolated in the center of the Pacific Ocean, has made it an important gateway for travelers heading both east and west. As a result of its position, Honolulu has become an important shipping hub and military base. The city has also attracted an extremely diverse population of people from around the Pacific Rim.</p>
</div>

## Question 368

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 368</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> During the Middle Ages, _______________ dramatically slowed the growth of urban areas.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. feudalism</li><li>B. colonialism</li><li>C. the Black Death</li><li>D. the Renaissance</li><li>E. the Industrial Revolution</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Feudalism fostered a system of dependence between landholders and lowly peasants that worked the land. During the Middle Ages, this system prevailed, and because of the lack of opportunity imbedded within it, urban areas experienced a period of stagnation.</p>
</div>

<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
