					</p></div>

## Question 370

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 370</strong></p>

<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. postmodern school</li><li>B. modernist tradition</li><li>C. City Beautiful movement</li><li>D. Beaux Arts school</li><li>E. classical movement</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Both the Beaux Arts and City Beautiful movements were attempts to create urban spaces that reflected changing social values while harkening back to classical forms. The City Beautiful movement, which is well represented in cities like Chicago and Washington, D.C., was, more specifically, an effort to give new industrial spaces
					</p></div>

## Question 371

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 371</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Modernist architecture</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. stressed efficiency and geometrical order.</li><li>B. uses eclectic and classic forms.</li><li>C. stressed the ornate.</li><li>D. is limited to newer American cities.</li><li>E. is characterized by skyscrapers.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Boxy, geometrical structures built of concrete and glass typify the modernist movement. Modernist architects tried to convey a sense of futuristic order and scientific rationality on urban spaces. Many such spaces would later be thought of as sterile and impersonal.</p>
</div>

## Question 372

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 372</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Asian, African, and South American cities</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. contain dominant centers, usually surrounding something of religious significance.</li><li>B. contain strong manufacturing and industrial sectors within the city.</li><li>C. display mostly modern forms of architecture as they are recently developing themselves after colonialism.</li><li>D. contain many structural relics from colonialism.</li><li>E. usually have a church at the center of the city.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) The majority of cities in each of these three areas, at one time, were colonial cities. As such, this extremely devastating historical process has largely determined their spatial organization.</p>
</div>

## Question 373

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 373</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Medieval European cities usually contain all the following characteristics EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. winding streets and tall, narrow buildings.</li><li>B. large, ornate cathedrals.</li><li>C. walls surrounding the city for defense purposes.</li><li>D. wide streets to accommodate large military troops.</li><li>E. a high density of buildings.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Medieval streets are generally narrow and winding. The only forms of transportation that traversed them were people on foot or horses, neither of which necessitated wide streets.</p>
</div>

## Question 374

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 374</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Los Angeles provides an excellent example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. the Beaux Arts tradition.</li><li>B. a central business district.</li><li>C. the multinucleated metropolis.</li><li>D. the concentric zone model.</li><li>E. disagglomeration.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Although Los Angeles has a central industrial core, its downtown area is not nearly as dominant of a city center as, say, the Loop in Chicago. Instead, Los Angeles is a vast metropolis with many "centers," or nodes of commercial and industrial activity.</p>
</div>

</ul>

<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) The sector model of urban geography describes cities in which different types of development

## Question 376

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 376</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> In cities such as Baltimore, inner-city revitalization has transformed _______________ into gentrified urban neighborhoods.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. suburbs</li><li>B. central business districts</li><li>C. edge cities</li><li>D. ghettos</li><li>E. agglomerations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Ghettos are economically depressed inner-city neighborhoods often populated by ethnic minorities. During the past 20 years, many American cities have successfully revitalized their inner cities by luring young urban professionals back into funky urban neighborhoods. However, many long-time residents of these former ghettos have been forced to move owing to increasing costs of living. Other cities, such as Detroit, have had much less success at transforming their urban cores.</p>
</div>

## Question 377

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 377</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following cities exemplifies an urban geography defined by railroads?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Boston</li><li>B. Mexico City</li><li>C. Chicago</li><li>D. San Francisco</li><li>E. Los Angeles</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Historically, Chicago has been a city of railroads. Chicago has served as the railroad hub of the West since the 1870s and, within the city itself, many people travel by light rail. The elevated train system or "el" moves hundreds of thousands of people per day around the tightly packed urban area.</p>
</div>

## Question 378

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 378</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following best describes edge cities?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They are located along freeways on the outskirts of major cities.</li><li>B. They are usually found in Europe and Asia.</li><li>C. They are small, isolated communities.</li><li>D. They are designed in the City Beautiful tradition.</li><li>E. They are gentrified communities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Edge cities serve the same functions as many urban areas but, for many, are conveniently located just outside of urban areas, usually on important corridors or freeway systems.</p>
</div>

## Question 379

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 379</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> According to the central-place theory,</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. small communities bind regions together.</li><li>B. most people live in mid-sized cities.</li><li>C. large cities serve as economic hubs.</li><li>D. regions are impossible to define.</li><li>E. there are more large cities than small cities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Large cities, because they generally have a large population, have a much greater economic base and thus can support and provide a greater variety of economic and cultural opportunities.</p>
</div>

## Question 380

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 380</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> The coastal southern California and northern Baja, Mexico region can be described as a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. central place.</li><li>B. artificial construction.</li><li>C. megacity.</li><li>D. megalopolis.</li><li>E. agglomeration.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) This region consists of a conurbation of linked cities such that, as you drive north or south along the coast in this region, you will always be driving through urban areas. These cities, at one time, were probably very geographically separate from one another but, because they have been increasingly expanded, have molded together into a megalopolis.</p>
</div>

## Question 381

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 381</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following was NOT one of the main elements contributing to a city's legibility according to Kevin Lynch?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Landmarks</li><li>B. Nodes</li><li>C. Links</li><li>D. Edges</li><li>E. Districts</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) According to Kevin Lynch, the five main elements contributing to a city's legibility include paths, edges, districts, landmarks, and nodes. Links may exist in cities in the form of transportation systems, but they do not exist as one of the fundamental units that make cities more easily readable for their inhabitants and first-time visitors.</p>
</div>

## Question 382

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 382</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Action space consists of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. recreational facilities in an urban area.</li><li>B. the space in which individual daily activity occurs.</li><li>C. spaces within a city designated for transportation.</li><li>D. a diagrammatic representation of the amount of time it takes to travel between activities on a particular day.</li><li>E. the area surrounding the interactions a central place has with the surrounding community.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Action spaces are used by behavioral geographers to analyze individuals' daily spatial activities. They describe all the typical interactions individuals have with their environment on any given day, and thus can provide insightful information for urban planners in making decisions on transportation routes and locations of various facilities within a city.</p>
</div>

## Question 383

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 383</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Individual spatial behavior on a daily basis</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. generally involves more shorter trips than longer trips.</li><li>B. can be described as that individual's action space.</li><li>C. can be limited by transportation possibilities.</li><li>D. mostly involves work-related travel.</li><li>E. All of the above</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) Behavioral geographers have analyzed numerous people's action spaces to draw general conclusions about human spatial behavior on a daily basis. In general, this kind of behavior conforms to five rules: people take many more shorter trips than longer trips, most trips tend to be work-related, trips of greater distances require more thought and planning, travel decisions can be quite limited by transportation, and people tend to avoid perceived hazards when going about their daily activities.</p>
</div>

## Question 384

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 384</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The Industrial Revolution</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. began in Germany in the 16th century.</li><li>B. was initiated by Henry Ford.</li><li>C. began in England in the 18th century.</li><li>D. reached its peak in the 1970s.</li><li>E. began in the United States in the early 20th century.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) The Industrial Revolution began in England in the 18th century and then spread to continental Europe, particularly France and Germany, and North America. The Industrial Revolution reached its peak in the 19th and early 20th centuries, but by the 1970s many formerly industrialized regions had lost their manufacturing bases to developing countries such as Mexico and China.</p>
</div>

## Question 385

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 385</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Which of the following are commonly associated with the Industrial Revolution?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Specialty goods</li><li>B. Cottage industries</li><li>C. New forms of capital investment</li><li>D. The printing press</li><li>E. Guild industries</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) When most geographers, economists, and historians think about the Industrial Revolution, massive factories, standardized goods, and new forms of capital investment are among the first things to come to mind.</p>
</div>

## Question 386

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 386</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Deindustrialization has had a dramatic impact on which of the following regions?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The lower Mississippi Valley</li><li>B. The Great Plains</li><li>C. The Great Lakes</li><li>D. The Pacific Northwest</li><li>E. The Cotton Belt</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) During the first half of the 20th century, the Great Lakes region, including Ohio, Michigan, and portions of Illinois, Pennsylvania, Indiana, and Wisconsin, became vibrant centers of manufacturing and heavy industry. By the 1970s, that same region had slipped into economic depression, as corporations moved their factories to developing countries and relocated their headquarters to Sun Belt states.</p>
</div>

## Question 387

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 387</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> _____________ take advantage of geographic differences in wages, labor laws, environmental regulations, taxes, and the distribution of natural resources by locating various aspects of their production in different countries.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Conglomerate corporations</li><li>B. E-businesses</li><li>C. Transnationals</li><li>D. Service industries</li><li>E. Footloose industries</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Transnational corporations attempt to maximize their profits by taking advantage of different regulatory and economic situations in different countries. One transnational corporation may have its headquarters in the United States, locate its factories in Mexico and Thailand, and keep its finances at banks in Switzerland and the Cayman Islands.</p>
</div>

## Question 388

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 388</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Mexico's maquiladoras are examples of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. offshore financial centers.</li><li>B. transnationals.</li><li>C. brick-and-mortar businesses.</li><li>D. export-processing zones.</li><li>E. ancillary activities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Maquiladoras are manufacturing areas located along the US-Mexico border. Products are assembled at maquiladora factories and then exported across the border to US markets.</p>
</div>

## Question 389

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 389</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Niger's economy is mostly limited to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. service industries.</li><li>B. primary economic activities.</li><li>C. export-processing activities.</li><li>D. quaternary economic activities.</li><li>E. nonbasic industry.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Countries at low levels of economic development, like Niger, have economies that are mostly oriented toward primary activities, such as fishing, farming, and mining.</p>
</div>

## Question 390

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 390</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Rostow's stages-of-development model predicts that each country's economy will progress from</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. high consumption to ecological sustainability.</li><li>B. low output to high input.</li><li>C. low per-capita incomes to high per-capita incomes and high consumption.</li><li>D. high levels of pollution to efficient resource use.</li><li>E. low employment in tertiary activities to high employment in primary activities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Rostow's stages-of-development model provides a teleological view of economics in which the economies of all nations are headed toward a single ultimate purpose
					</p></div>

## Question 391

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 391</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The _____________ is a measure of all goods and services produced by a country in a year, including production from its investments abroad, minus the loss or degradation of natural resource capital as a result of productivity.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Net National Product</li><li>B. Gross National Product</li><li>C. Human Development Index</li><li>D. Intrinsic-Productivity Index</li><li>E. Purchasing-Power Parity</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) The Gross National Product computes the value of all goods and services produced by a country in a year, but the Net National Product also subtracts capital lost through the degradation of natural resources.</p>
</div>

## Question 392

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 392</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Gender equity is related to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Gross National Product.</li><li>B. cultural traditions.</li><li>C. education.</li><li>D. All of the above</li><li>E. Only (A)and (B)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Gender equity, or women's welfare, is related to a wide range of cultural and economic issues, including, but not limited to, economic productivity, cultural traditions, and education.</p>
</div>

## Question 393

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 393</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> First-tier world cities include</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Tokyo, Mexico City, and Sao Paulo.</li><li>B. Tokyo, London, and New York.</li><li>C. Paris, Brussels, and Moscow.</li><li>D. Washington, Moscow, and London.</li><li>E. Los Angeles, London, and Paris.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Tokyo, London, and New York are the world's three most important centers of economic activity and are thus categorized as first-tier world cities. Other important centers of government, finance, and popular culture, such as Paris, Washington, Brussels, and Los Angeles, are considered to be second-tier world cities.</p>
</div>

## Question 394

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 394</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Firms try to locate their production facilities to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. maximize spatial accessibility.</li><li>B. maximize visibility and minimize transportation.</li><li>C. maximize agglomeration.</li><li>D. minimize costs and maximize profits.</li><li>E. minimize competition.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Firms try to locate their production and distribution facilities in ways that maximize their profit through cutting down on transportation costs.</p>
</div>

## Question 395

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 395</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> The clustering of financial firms on Wall Street in New York is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. least-cost theory.</li><li>B. agglomeration.</li><li>C. deindustrialization.</li><li>D. ancillary industry.</li><li>E. central-place theory.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Agglomeration occurs when firms find that it is to their advantage to locate close to other firms in the same industry. Advantages include being able to use the same pool of employees and being close to important infrastructure components, such as transportation depots or movie sets.</p>
</div>

## Question 396

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 396</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Mr. Jemstone located his jewelry shop in a place near his home so that he can eat lunch with Mrs. Jemstone every afternoon.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. His locational decision represents a market orientation.</li><li>B. Since Mr. Jemstone owns his own business, he has chosen an optimal site as he minimizes transport costs to and from work.</li><li>C. It doesn't matter too much where Mr. Jemstone put his jewelry shop because it is a footloose industry and as long as a viable market exists, he can locate pretty much anywhere.</li><li>D. Because most jewelry shopping occurs online, the actual location of the shop is unimportant.</li><li>E. Mr. and Mrs. Jemstone probably participate in a cottage industry.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Because both the inputs used to make jewelry and the finished product are so lightweight, this type of industry can locate basically anywhere a large enough market exists to make a profit.</p>
</div>

## Question 397

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 397</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Economic activities that increase and thereby benefit from agglomerations in particular regions are called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. ancillary activities.</li><li>B. tertiary activities.</li><li>C. basic sector services.</li><li>D. quinary activities.</li><li>E. footloose industries.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Ancillary activities include all the necessary services to sustain and provide for a local population, such as grocery stores, haircutters, and veterinary hospitals. As the population within a region increases, as it does when an area becomes the site for a particular agglomeration, more of the services become necessary. Thus, agglomerations have tremendous impacts on the overall economy within a specific region.</p>
</div>

## Question 398

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 398</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following regions is NOT an economic backwater?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Buenos Aires, Argentina</li><li>B. Western China</li><li>C. Sao Paolo, Brazil</li><li>D. Lower Mississippi Valley</li><li>E. Upper Great Plains</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Sao Paolo, Brazil, is actually one of the most dominant economic areas in all of South America. Backwaters exist when other regions in a country experience great levels of economic development
					</p></div>

## Question 399

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 399</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The idea that resources should be conserved so that people living today can meet their needs without limiting the ability of future generations to do the same is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. globalization.</li><li>B. gross national happiness.</li><li>C. sustainable development.</li><li>D. environmental conservation.</li><li>E. subsistence economics.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Although the term "sustainable development" has many definitions, this one, paraphrased from the Bruntland Report, or "Our Common Future," which was published by the World Commission on Environment and Development in 1987, is the standard that is most frequently quoted.</p>
</div>

## Question 400

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 400</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Globalization</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. is a new and unique phenomenon.</li><li>B. has penetrated the entire world.</li><li>C. is always good for people in the poorest countries.</li><li>D. has a long and circuitous history.</li><li>E. does not cause a countermovement of localization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) During the past 500 years, the world economic system has undergone several periods of greater or less economic integration, or globalization.</p>
</div>

## Question 401

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 401</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> London and New York City are approximately 3,500 miles apart from one another in terms of absolute distance, but they are quite connected economically and culturally. What best explains this level of connectivity?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Both cities have similar transportation and communications infrastructure, which facilitates interaction.</li><li>B. Both cities have diverse populations, which leads to common cultural experiences.</li><li>C. Both cities have high populations, counteracting distance in the gravity model.</li><li>D. Both cities have similar economic bases, which leads to higher trade between the two.</li><li>E. Both cities have airports that allow for large jets and frequent arrivals and departures, making travel between the cities quite easy.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) The gravity model predicts interaction between two places based on the size of their population and the distance between them. Large populations (in the numerator) lessen the friction of distance between two places.</p>
</div>

## Question 402

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 402</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> In developed countries, such as the Netherlands, it is difficult to classify agriculture as part of the primary economy. Why?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Because agriculture in developed countries is primarily controlled by large agribusinesses that coordinate research, production, harvest, and distribution on global scales</li><li>B. Because agriculture in developed countries no longer happens in fields, but rather through almost completely through high-tech methods in factories</li><li>C. Because so little of the labor force in developed countries is engaged in this economic activity, the category essentially no longer exists</li><li>D. Because developed countries now outsource all of their agricultural production from developing countries</li><li>E. Because agricultural production is still very much a primary economic activity in developed countries, the methods are comparable to those in developing countries</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Developed countries, such as the Netherlands, grow an abundance of food using a wide variety of sophisticated technologies. These supporting activities, such as research and development, use of machinery for planting and harvest, and international marketing, all involve significant labor inputs in other sectors of the economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 403

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 403</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Which of the following countries is the most probable location for the image above?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The United States</li><li>B. Bangladesh</li><li>C. China</li><li>D. Argentina</li><li>E. Japan</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) In highly developed countries, such as the United States, the dependency ratio is increasing as a result of longer life expectancies and decreasing fertility rates. The rise in elderly populations has led to a corresponding rise in services that provide for the specific needs of this population. Memory care facilities and long-term care centers are becoming increasingly popular across the United States and other developed countries.</p>
</div>

## Question 404

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 404</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Countries that have a growing number of facilities such as those depicted in the above image are most likely in which stage of the demographic transition model?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Stage 1</li><li>B. Stage 2</li><li>C. Stage 3</li><li>D. Stage 4</li><li>E. The demographic transition model has no relation to facilities that cater to elderly populations.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Countries that are in stage 4, or even stage 5, of the demographic transition model have low birth and death rates and growing elderly populations as a result of those low rates. The growing upper brackets of these countries' population pyramids leads to growth in services that support these cohorts.</p>
</div>

## Question 405

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 405</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following types of population-related policies might be in place in a country with a growing number of these types of facilities?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Pronatalist population policies</li><li>B. Policies limiting the number of immigrants</li><li>C. Policies discouraging large families through tax penalties</li><li>D. Policies restricting guest workers and temporary migrants</li><li>E. Policies decreasing the retirement age</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Pronatalist population policies are those that encourage higher fertility rates, either through tax incentives and/or support for parents, economically and socially, as they raise multiple children.</p>
</div>

## Question 406

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 406</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> The cultural and political ideas of nationalism can sometimes work to sever the social fabric of a state. In this case, nationalism can be seen as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a push factor.</li><li>B. a pull factor.</li><li>C. a centrifugal force.</li><li>D. a centripetal force.</li><li>E. an intervening opportunity.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Centrifugal forces are those that tear apart the social fabric of a country and can potentially lead to devolution. When a state is made up of multiple ethnic groups, nationalism can become a threat if those groups compete with one another for political dominance.</p>
</div>

## Question 407

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 407</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0037-01.jpg"/></p><p>The pie charts above most likely represent the labor force by occupation in which of the following pairs of countries?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Mexico; Denmark</li><li>B. Saudi Arabia; South Africa</li><li>C. Ethiopia; Norway</li><li>D. Argentina; Belarus</li><li>E. Italy; Australia</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Ethiopia is a less-developed country with a large agricultural labor force, whereas Norway is a highly developed country with a diverse labor force that concentrates in the services sector.</p>
</div>

## Question 408

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 408</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> In some spots along the Great Rift Valley, such as Rwanda in eastern Africa, population density is high despite the country's equatorial location. This density is partially attributable to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. volcanic activity along the plate boundaries, which feeds the typically poor equatorial soil.</li><li>B. government incentives to increase population density through pronatalist policies.</li><li>C. Rwanda's size as a comparatively small country in terms of area.</li><li>D. Rwanda's location near the Indian Ocean.</li><li>E. Rwanda's proximity to the Nile River.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Because of Rwanda's equatorial position, the soil quality should not allow for substantial agricultural production. However, because of volcanic activity along the Great Rift Valley, the soil is nutrient-rich, and the elevation gains are more suited for high population density than in other parts of equatorial Africa such as the Democratic Republic of the Congo.</p>
</div>

## Question 409

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 409</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> The position of neo-Malthusians, similar to that of Thomas Malthus, is indicative of the tension that exists between</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. gender equality and fertility.</li><li>B. population growth and poverty.</li><li>C. social welfare (health care and education) and fertility.</li><li>D. economic growth and population decline.</li><li>E. population growth and consumption of resources, including food.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) Malthus and those that subscribe to his ideas posit that when populations exceed the resource base needed to support them, the population must be "checked" (intentionally or unintentionally) through war, famine, disease, or some other means.</p>
</div>

## Question 410

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 410</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> When recent college graduates and young professionals move to large cities with diverse employment, cultural, and entertainment opportunities, to what are they responding?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Suburban amenities</li><li>B. Push factors</li><li>C. Pull factors</li><li>D. Mobility opportunities</li><li>E. Centripetal forces</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Pull factors, such as job and recreational opportunities, attract people to move to new places, often urban areas. Push factors, such as violence and economic stagnation, motivate people to leave their old homes and search for new places to live with better prospects.</p>
</div>

## Question 411

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 411</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> In squatter settlements, such as the favelas of Rio de Janeiro, poorer rural-to-urban migrants tend to make a living in which sector of the economy?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Basic</li><li>B. Informal</li><li>C. Nonbasic</li><li>D. Formal</li><li>E. Primary</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Most migrants in squatter settlements have relocated to the city, often primate cities, in search of employment in growing urban economies. Until these individuals can secure a job in the formal economy, they make a living through informal economic activities, such as the sale of goods (e.g., food, clothing, and handicrafts) or services (e.g., childcare, handiwork, and transportation).</p>
</div>

## Question 412

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 412</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Some religious practices in South America result from combining elements from traditional religions and religions diffused by colonizers. This is an example of:</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a cultural complex.</li><li>B. a cultural confluence.</li><li>C. a counterculture.</li><li>D. a cultural diaspora.</li><li>E. a cultural syncretism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) A cultural syncretism occurs when two or more different cultures or cultural traits, such as religion, converge to form something new.</p>
</div>

## Question 413

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 413</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> __________ maps work well when seeking to understand the location of countries in relation to one another, while __________ maps help in understanding how a particular variable changes over space.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Thematic . . . reference</li><li>B. Reference . . . thematic</li><li>C. Spatial . . . cartographic</li><li>D. Cartographic . . . spatial</li><li>E. Topologic . . . choropleth</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) A good way to think about basic cartographic representation is to divide maps into those used for reference purposes and those that focus on a specific theme. An example of a reference map would be a road map or an atlas. An example of a thematic map would be a dot map that shows distribution and density of tobacco harvested in sub-Saharan Africa in 2010.</p>
</div>

## Question 414

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 414</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> <table class="table table-bordered"><tbody><tr><td><b>Country</b></td><td><b>Population living in urban areas (%)</b></td><td><b>Labor-force composition (%)</b></td></tr><tr><td>Australia</td><td>86</td><td>Agriculture: 3.6<br/>Industry: 21.1<br/>Services: 75.3</td></tr><tr><td>Zimbabwe</td><td>32.2</td><td>Agriculture: 67.5<br/>Industry: 7.3<br/>Services: 25.2</td></tr><tr><td>Bangladesh</td><td>36.6</td><td>Agriculture: 42.7<br/>Industry: 20.5<br/>Services: 36.9</td></tr></tbody></table></p><p>On the basis of the data in the table above, how does a country's level of urbanization relate to its labor-force composition?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Highly urbanized countries, such as Australia, concentrate in services.</li><li>B. Less urbanized countries, such as Zimbabwe, have a highly diverse labor force.</li><li>C. Urbanized countries tend to have little to no industry.</li><li>D. Less urbanized countries tend to have less agricultural production.</li><li>E. There is no clear relationship between urbanization and labor-force composition.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Countries that are urbanized tend to have more highly educated populations that specialize in a variety of service-based occupations, jobs that typically concentrate in cities. Countries that are mostly rural have labor forces that concentrate in the agricultural sector of the economy. As countries industrialize, they also typically urbanize, as factories and associated industries tend to concentrate in urban centers.</p>
</div>

## Question 415

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 415</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Given Bangladesh's data, its position in the demographic transition model is most likely</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. stage 1.</li><li>B. stage 2.</li><li>C. stage 3.</li><li>D. stage 4.</li><li>E. stage 5.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) As countries industrialize and urbanize, birth rates tend to drop as women become more active in the labor force. A falling birth rate characterizes stage 3 countries, such as Bangladesh, where women provide a significant source of labor in the industrial sector of the economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 416

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 416</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> If the chart contained an additional column with data showing the Gender Development Index (GDI), what would the data be likely to reveal?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. GDI would be highest in Zimbabwe because service-based jobs tend to employ mostly women.</li><li>B. GDI would be highest in Bangladesh because of increasing growth in microcredit opportunities for women.</li><li>C. GDI would be the same in Bangladesh and Australia, where industry and service-occupation percentages are higher.</li><li>D. GDI would likely be highest in Australia, where service-based occupations dominate.</li><li>E. Data on GDI would likely reveal that the three countries differed only minimally.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Highly developed countries, such as Australia, have strong, diverse, service-based economies, typically with strong, stable political systems. Women are highly educated and participate in both the formal economy and in government positions, leading to a higher development index.</p>
</div>

## Question 417

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 417</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Von Thunen's model of rural land use is based on which of the following premises?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Value of land decreases the farther it is from the urban center.</li><li>B. Value of land increases the farther it is from the urban center.</li><li>C. Perishable goods are the least valuable.</li><li>D. Railroads provide fixed transportation costs.</li><li>E. Vegetarianism is environmentally beneficial.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) In von Thunen's model, agricultural land use changes with distance from the city center, primarily due to land and commodity values. Expensive, perishable commodities are grown closer to urban markets, while less expensive, more expansive (in terms of land area necessary for cultivation) agricultural goods are grown farther from the city center.</p>
</div>

## Question 418

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 418</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Catalonia, a region in northeast Spain with its own language and culture, voted on which of the following in 2017 in an effort to maintain its cultural identity?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Electoral reapportionment</li><li>B. Economic freedom</li><li>C. Unitary standing</li><li>D. Self-determination</li><li>E. Membership in the United Nations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Catalonia, because of its unique language and cultural identity, sought independence from Spain in a referendum in October 2017. The referendum was not recognized by the Spanish government, which considered it illegal.</p>
</div>

## Question 419

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 419</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The existence of Dutch Village in Holland, Michigan; Jaarsma [Dutch] Bakery in Pella, Iowa; and Dutch Roots Farm in Ripon, California, are all a result of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. forced migration.</li><li>B. religious conversions.</li><li>C. relocation diffusion.</li><li>D. colonial-era labor migrations.</li><li>E. rural-to-urban migrations.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Relocation diffusion occurs when a cultural group brings a particular trait to a new area and diffuses it to that local community. Dutch communities throughout the United States (that resulted from chain migration) brought with them certain Dutch traditions, such as tulips at the farm in Ripon and speculaas cookies at the bakery in Iowa.</p>
</div>

## Question 420

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 420</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Hong Kong is 22
						<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. relative location.</li><li>B. absolute location.</li><li>C. relative direction.</li><li>D. absolute direction.</li><li>E. relative distance.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Coordinates of latitude and longitude express absolute location, which identifies a place's location precisely and universally.</p>
</p></div>

## Question 421

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 421</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Although no longer in effect, China's one-child policy has led to which of the following demographic challenges?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Large-scale emigration to economically advanced countries</li><li>B. Mass rural-to-urban migration</li><li>C. Smaller total population in China</li><li>D. Immigration from less-developed countries to fulfill lower level industrial jobs</li><li>E. An imbalance between males and females of marrying age</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) China's traditionally patriarchal society favors males over females which, combined with the one-child policy and the availability of sonograms, led to a much larger portion of male births while the policy was in effect. This, in turn, has led to a huge current discrepancy between males and females of marrying age.</p>
</div>

## Question 422

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 422</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Which of the following agricultural techniques do farmers use to adapt to poor soil quality in rain forest regions, such as the Amazon River basin in Brazil?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Nomadism</li><li>B. Slash and burn</li><li>C. Drip irrigation</li><li>D. Composting</li><li>E. Hydroponics</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Because rainforest soils lack nutrients, to make them agriculturally productive, farmers slash existing vegetation and burn it, releasing nutrients into the soil for a limited period of time. Slash and burn can be sustainable provided cultivated landscapes are given enough time to regenerate.</p>
</div>

## Question 423

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 423</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Deindustrialization in both North America and Europe was largely driven by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. cheaper wages in areas and regions of lower economic development.</li><li>B. relaxed environmental and labor regulations overseas.</li><li>C. technology and automation replacing the need for human labor in certain industries.</li><li>D. none of the above.</li><li>E. all of the above (A</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) Patterns of deindustrialization are largely driven by economic forces. Industrial activities concentrate in areas where goods can be produced at the least cost (e.g., cheaper labor and lack of costly regulations) with the greatest efficiency (e.g., automation).</p>
</div>

## Question 424

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 424</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> How do patterns of urbanization in Europe differ from those in North America?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. North American cities focus on tourism, while European cities are much more focused on industry.</li><li>B. European cities have a much stronger suburban fringe in comparison to North American cities.</li><li>C. In both regions, urban populations concentrate in urban cores with a decreasing portion of the population living in suburbs.</li><li>D. In European cities, housing is much denser with only a small percentage of families living in stand-alone housing.</li><li>E. European cities tend to follow the rank size rule, while North America has mostly primate cities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) North American cities, particularly those in the United States, have strong suburban populations, where houses tend to be stand-alone and located on larger lots, making houses much more spread out than cities in Europe. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 425

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 425</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Current fertility rates in Europe exhibit which of the following trends?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. In most countries, fertility rates are near or below replacement level.</li><li>B. In most countries, fertility rates are slightly above replacement level.</li><li>C. Fertility rates are highly variable across the region.</li><li>D. Fertility rates are higher in countries without significant immigrant populations.</li><li>E. Fertility rates are lower in European countries that are less economically developed.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Most European countries are in stage 4 (or even stage 5) of the demographic transition model. Birth rates and fertility rates are low (at or below replacement level) because women tend to marry later in life and participate actively in the formal economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 426

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 426</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> How does microcredit overcome some of the challenges related to the employment opportunities for women in less-developed countries, particularly in South and Southeast Asia?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Microcredit is a form of feminization of labor seen within the Export Processing Zones (EPZ) in Southeast Asia.</li><li>B. Microcredit is the main avenue for union formation, which works to combat unfair labor conditions in South and Southeast Asia.</li><li>C. With microcredit, women have control over their own business and therefore set their own hours, wages, and working conditions.</li><li>D. With microcredit, women are able to pay for childcare while they work factory jobs in the EPZs.</li><li>E. Microcredit has not offered many distinct changes for female employment opportunity in South and Southeast Asia.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Microcredit has proven highly successful in parts of South and Southeast Asia as a means to encourage female empowerment and meaningful engagement in the formal economy. With small loans, women become entrepreneurs in working environments that they oversee, thus helping their communities and families.</p>
</div>

## Question 427

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 427</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Immediately after independence, many developing countries adopted which of these types of economic strategies to limit dependence on former colonizers and/or highly developed economies?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Neo-liberal (free trade) policies that encouraged involvement in the global economy</li><li>B. "Bottom-Up" initiatives that promoted local sustainable development through microfinance</li><li>C. Regional economic alliances that promoted common currencies and easy movement of goods and people among member nations (similar to the EU)</li><li>D. Industrial modernization through investments in technology</li><li>E. Protectionist strategies that encouraged economic self-sufficiency through import substitution and barriers to international trade</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) After independence, many developing countries sought to free themselves from the problematic economic relationships and dependencies established under colonial regimes. To do this, governments protected local producers and farmers by promoting domestic production of previously imported goods, and by limiting, through various means, international trade.</p>
</div>

## Question 428

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 428</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Followers of animistic religions</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. believe that features in nature, such as animals, mountains, and trees, have spiritual value.</li><li>B. believe in one god.</li><li>C. believe in polytheism.</li><li>D. do not believe in a spiritual realm.</li><li>E. do not believe there is an afterlife.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Animistic religions are based on the belief that certain items in nature hold spiritual value. These religions are common among Native American cultures and in various sub-Saharan Africa cultures.</p>
</div>

## Question 429

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 429</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> In spite of the risks of nuclear power generation
						<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. construction of nuclear power plants is relatively inexpensive.</li><li>B. nuclear waste storage solutions are becoming increasingly low risk.</li><li>C. nuclear fuel is easy to access.</li><li>D. of the lack of carbon emissions in nuclear power generation.</li><li>E. nuclear power technology can be easily accessed across the globe.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) In spite of the risks associated with nuclear power generation, it does not emit carbon into the atmosphere, making it an appealing energy source for some environmentalists.</p>
</p></div>

## Question 430

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 430</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> The above image of the Over the Rhine neighborhood in Cincinnati, Ohio, exhibits the efforts of many postindustrial cities in America's heartland to increase the livability of an old central business district. This process is referred to as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. suburbanization.</li><li>B. gentrification.</li><li>C. redlining.</li><li>D. mart growth.</li><li>E. postmodernism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Gentrification involves the revitalization of old industrial office buildings and warehouses into residential, commercial, and office space. These spaces frequently attract younger, urban professionals, and often coincide with revitalization efforts related to recreation and transportation. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 431

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 431</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following postindustrial cities in the United States is likely to exhibit similar gentrification patterns to those that exist in Cincinnati?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Silicon Valley, California</li><li>B. Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania</li><li>C. Seaside, Florida</li><li>D. Las Vegas, Nevada</li><li>E. Kalispell, Montana</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Industrial and manufacturing cities in the heart of the Midwest, such as Cincinnati, Cleveland, and Detroit, among many others, suffered when industry relocated to areas with cheaper labor (initially to the southern United States and then overseas). These abandoned, formerly industrial landscapes are increasingly seeing a revival with buildings restored for commercial and residential purposes. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 432

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 432</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> This area of Cincinnati is most likely inhabited by which of the following demographic cohorts?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Single, young college graduates</li><li>B. Retired baby boomers</li><li>C. Families with school-aged kids</li><li>D. Low-income families</li><li>E. High-income families</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) Gentrified landscapes such as Over the Rhine attract younger, urban, often single professionals. The housing is such that it does not typically support larger families and requires a stable, significant income. In fact, one of the arguments against gentrification is that it displaces low-income, often minority populations that previously lived in those areas. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 433

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 433</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> In comparison to other models of urban structure, the sector model</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. incorporates a strong central business district (CBD).</li><li>B. suggests a concentric form of differing functions around an industrial core.</li><li>C. portrays ethnic neighborhoods and areas of industrial concentration.</li><li>D. displays a decentralized version of urban life.</li><li>E. relies on an assumption that real estate value decreases with distance from the city center.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Unlike other models of urban form, such as the multiple-nuclei model or concentric-zone model, the sector model accounts for variation in the ethnic makeup of neighborhoods; immigrants frequently live in low-income housing, often near manufacturing or industrial areas. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 434

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 434</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> As the economies of industrialized countries continue to advance, agricultural production within these countries tends to follow which of the following patterns?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Farms are getting larger and are increasingly owned by just one entity (family or corporation).</li><li>B. Farms are getting larger and are increasingly government-owned.</li><li>C. Farms are getting smaller and are increasing the diversity of crops they produce.</li><li>D. Farms are getting smaller and are increasingly owned by farming cooperatives.</li><li>E. Farming is being completely eliminated in favor of importing agricultural goods from abroad.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) As countries become increasingly economically advanced, agricultural production becomes increasingly mechanized. Production, in terms of volume, tends to increase as farms become more efficient through the use of machinery and other technologies. However, although volume increases, the number of farmers decreases as corporate entities take over farming, or as families expand their operations.</p>
</div>

## Question 435

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 435</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> In the former Yugoslavia, the forced expulsion and killing of specific cultural groups during the 1990s is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. insurgency.</li><li>B. devolution.</li><li>C. chain migration.</li><li>D. ethnic cleansing.</li><li>E. Balkanization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) During the 1990s, minority groups in the former Yugoslavia were forced out of their communities, often at gunpoint. Those who resisted were typically killed, in what is described as ethnic cleansing
					</p></div>

## Question 436

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 436</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> The number of smaller, family-owned farms in North America has increased in recent decades largely as a result of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. an increase in consumption of organic and locally produced food items.</li><li>B. an increase in the costs of fuel, which presents prohibitive challenges to large-scale farming.</li><li>C. an increase in the export of crops to least-developed countries (LDCs).</li><li>D. a large-scale switch to production of staple crops such as corn and rice.</li><li>E. a decrease in the amount of subsidies provided by the government to support agricultural production.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) In recent decades, many Americans have become more concerned about the quality of their food and about the use of toxic pesticides in farming. This concern has led to an increase in demand for locally produced, organic farm products, which has led to greater opportunities for smaller farms that produce a wider variety of sustainably raised goods.</p>
</div>

## Question 437

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 437</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> What is most responsible for hierarchical diffusion, as opposed to contagious diffusion?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Distance decay effects</li><li>B. Special network links between major nodes</li><li>C. Some people's need for multiple contacts before they adopt an innovation</li><li>D. Proximity of the innovation to the varying degrees of diffusion</li><li>E. Relevance of particular innovations to only specific locations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Hierarchical diffusion describes the spread of an innovation through specific nodes, which are not usually located close together in space, but exhibit strong links to one another in a network. For example, fashion trends tend to diffuse hierarchically between major fashion nodes (e.g., Paris, London, and Milan) before spreading contagiously to surrounding areas.</p>
</div>

## Question 438

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 438</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Individuals, after experience with a place, form subjective images based on their perceptions of that place. This image is referred to as a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. thematic map.</li><li>B. reference map.</li><li>C. mental map.</li><li>D. contour map.</li><li>E. topographic map.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Mental maps are highly individualized personal images about a place, which are composed of subjective perceptions, memories, biases, and feelings. These perceptions and feelings can result from direct experience or from knowledge gained indirectly from various media outlets.</p>
</div>

## Question 439

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 439</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which of the following best describes a "pull factor" that would cause a rural family living in a least-developed country to leave their farm and migrate away from their home community?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Civil war or armed conflict in the rural countryside</li><li>B. Job opportunities in manufacturing in the country's urban area</li><li>C. Drought in the rural countryside</li><li>D. Lack of educational opportunity in the home community</li><li>E. Lack of healthcare in the home community</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Pull factors are just as they sound; they pull an individual or family toward a destination. This is in contrast to push factors, which compel people to leave their home or community. Option B
					</p></div>

## Question 440

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 440</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Poorer rural-to-urban migrants in Latin America are most likely to have residences or homes</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. in slums or squatter settlements.</li><li>B. in single-family homes in the suburbs.</li><li>C. in government-provided public housing projects.</li><li>D. in high-density urban apartments.</li><li>E. in communal housing cooperatives.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) In Middle and South America, as depicted in the Ford Griffin Model of the Latin American City, poor urban inhabitants typically occupy areas on the outer fringes of the city, often in marginal landscapes. These migrants are searching for economic opportunity, often in the informal sector of the economy, and they do not have the income to afford more established housing options. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 441

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 441</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> A description of Paris as a place (rather than a space) would include</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Paris's geographic coordinates.</li><li>B. the position of Paris relative to the Seine River.</li><li>C. the highways connecting Paris to the rest of France.</li><li>D. Parisians' love for pain au chocolat (chocolate croissants).</li><li>E. Paris's location relative to London.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) The concept of space simply describes a place's location, either in absolute or relative terms (or both). Descriptions of place involve unique characteristics that are essential elements of that location's identity. Parisians' love for chocolate croissants is a unique attribute of that city (even though they're also thoroughly enjoyed by tourists!).</p>
</div>

## Question 442

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 442</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Angeline's mom immigrated to the United States (from the Netherlands) in the early 1950s by boat; the trip took several days. Her cousin immigrated by plane (also from the Netherlands) in the 1980s and it took half a day. What phenomenon does the travel-time difference illustrate?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Relative location</li><li>B. Situation</li><li>C. Time-space convergence</li><li>D. Connectivity</li><li>E. Absolute location</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Time-space convergence describes how the relative distance between places decreases as a result of improvements in transportation and communications technology. The United States became much "closer" to the Netherlands after air travel became more accessible.</p>
</div>

## Question 443

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 443</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Which of the following events was an early form of globalization?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. European colonization</li><li>B. The formation of NAFTA (North American Free Trade Agreement)</li><li>C. The invention of the internet</li><li>D. The invention of the airplane</li><li>E. The invention of refrigeration</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(A) European colonization created a global network of exchange. Typically, raw materials flowed from the colonies to Europe, while manufactured goods flowed in the reverse direction. This same pattern exists in the modern era, but without official colonial rule. Raw materials typically flow from less-developed countries, which have large markets for manufacturing and industrial products.</p>
</div>

## Question 444

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 444</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> When looking at labor-force distribution on a global scale, which of the following patterns is generally true?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. In highly developed (rich) countries, the labor force is evenly distributed across all economic sectors (primary, secondary, tertiary, and quaternary).</li><li>B. In least-developed countries, most laborers are in service-based industries (tertiary sector).</li><li>C. The world's wealthiest countries tend to have vast natural resources; thus, their labor force is predominantly primary sector (agriculture and mining).</li><li>D. Developed countries tend to concentrate in the secondary sector, while less developed countries concentrate in primary economic activities.</li><li>E. Poor countries tend to concentrate in primary sector economic occupations, while a richer country's labor force concentrates in service-based sectors (tertiary and quaternary).</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) The least-developed countries (LDCs) have labor force concentrations in the primary sector of the economy (harvesting of raw materials); industrial (secondary sector) activities tend to concentrate in developing economies. In highly developed regions, information-based and other services employ the largest sector of the labor force
					</p></div>

## Question 445

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 445</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Which of the following is the BEST description of "sustainable development"?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Promotion of development strategies that encourage growth primarily in ecologically sustainable industries</li><li>B. Promotion of development strategies that will sustain economic growth in the long-term rather than short-term</li><li>C. Promotion of development strategies that focus primarily on reaching and sustaining a replacement (or lower) total fertility rate</li><li>D. Promotion of development strategies that improve current living standards without jeopardizing those of future generations</li><li>E. Promotion of development strategies that focus on integrating countries into the global economy, thus making countries more economically sustainable</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Sustainable development initiatives focus on strategies that do not limit future generations' access to resources or to reasonable and healthy standards of living.</p>
</div>

## Question 446

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 446</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Increased air pollution, inner-city decay, homogenization of landscapes, and loss of productive farmlands are all caused by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. climate change.</li><li>B. postmodernism.</li><li>C. gentrification.</li><li>D. suburbanization.</li><li>E. ghettoization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Suburbanization describes the process of urban areas expanding outward, converting productive farmland to housing and other services. Initially, individuals and families that moved to the suburbs commuted back to the city for work, a process accommodated by the automobile and improved highway systems. Even today, when commuting patterns don't always lead to the central business district (CBD), the suburban way of life still depends on the automobile, which leads to increased pollution levels. Additionally, as people continue to move out from the city, the city's tax base suffers, causing rundown in the infrastructure, vacant buildings, and substandard education and housing opportunities. Finally, most suburban landscapes in America today look similar, with the same fast food chains, big box stores, and shopping opportunities, leading to a homogenization of the American landscape. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 447

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 447</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> All of the following characterize the Green Revolution EXCEPT:</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Development and improvement of chemicals used in agricultural production</li><li>B. Technological improvements such as hybrid seeds</li><li>C. Export of agricultural techniques from developed to developing countries</li><li>D. Use of environmentally sustainable "green" techniques in agricultural production</li><li>E. More intensive production of agricultural goods in developing regions</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) The Green Revolution refers to an agricultural revolution in which improved technology allowed for intensive cultivation of landscapes, particularly in the developing world. The new technologies consisted of herbicides and pesticides, hybrid seeds that could withstand some of the severe conditions present in places such as Africa and South Asia, and mechanical improvements such as irrigation. Additionally, these technologies and techniques were imported from the developed world to developing regions to help them produce more goods on less land. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 448

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 448</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Paper-based maps differ from Geographic Information Systems (GIS) in that</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. traditional maps typically show only land features, whereas a GIS takes into account a variety of different phenomena.</li><li>B. data can be more easily manipulated or analyzed within a GIS, whereas information is static on traditional maps.</li><li>C. a GIS produces thematic maps, whereas traditional maps tend to be reference maps.</li><li>D. GIS, because they're on the computer, are not projected, whereas traditional maps are.</li><li>E. GIS provide locational features, whereas traditional maps are mostly symbolic.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) GIS combine "geographic" (maps) with "information" (data tables) in one digital system that can integrate multiple layers of geospatial information. These layers can be manipulated or queried to conduct varying levels of spatial analysis. Consequently, GIS are dynamic, whereas traditional paper maps are typically static.</p>
</div>

## Question 449

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 449</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> When a people group have a recognized and common cultural identity, they are considered a _________. As opposed to a _________ which is a country with recognized political boundaries.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. territory . . . state</li><li>B. nation . . . territory</li><li>C. state . . . territory</li><li>D. nation . . . state</li><li>E. territory . . . nation</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) A nation, although commonly and incorrectly used as a synonym for country, consists of a cultural group that may or may not have an internationally recognized piece of land to associate itself with. A state is a correct synonym for country; it consists of a piece of land with internationally recognized borders.</p>
</div>

## Question 450

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 450</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> When two groups of people who speak different languages interact (to make a trade, for example), they often make up a simplified language combination to communicate with each other. This is called a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. dialect.</li><li>B. pidgin.</li><li>C. pig tongue.</li><li>D. Creole.</li><li>E. accent.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) A pidgin language is a simplified language, usually developed for trading purposes, that has little grammatical structure and a limited vocabulary. When a pidgin language becomes so pervasive that generations begin speaking it as their first language, a Creole has evolved.</p>
</div>

## Question 451

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 451</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Country A is in stage 1 of demographic transition, while Country B is in stage 2. Net migration is equal in both countries. Which of the following is true about the population growth of these two countries?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Population growth rate of Country A is higher than that of Country B.</li><li>B. Population growth rate of Country B is higher than that of Country A.</li><li>C. The population of both countries is decreasing.</li><li>D. The population of both countries is not changing.</li><li>E. It depends on the total fertility rates in each country.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) The demographic transition model describes population growth (or lack of growth) in a country over time. The model states that countries go through four stages before achieving stable growth. Stage 1 is characterized by high birth and death rates and little growth; in stage 2, the death rate declines, birth rate remains high, and growth increases; in stage 3, the birth rate begins to drop and the growth rate also drops, but the country still experiences growth; and finally, in stage 4, both birth and death rates are low and growth is stable, or sometimes even declining. Country A, in stage 1, is experiencing little growth, while Country B, in stage 2, is experiencing decreasing death rates with high birth rates, consequently rapid growth.</p>
</div>

## Question 452

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 452</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Which of the following best describes exurbia?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Usually found in Europe and Asia</li><li>B. Generally located along freeways on the outskirts of major cities</li><li>C. Made up of small, isolated communities consisting mostly of telecommuters</li><li>D. Usually designed by the City Beautiful Movement</li><li>E. Lies outside of urban zoning restrictions</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Exurbia is beyond suburbia, meaning beyond the fringes of an urban area. As telecommuting continues to be a popular option thanks to communications technologies, more individuals are choosing to live far outside of urban areas in small, mostly rural communities, and to work from home rather than commute to an office. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 453

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 453</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Primate cities are those that</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. are seats of political power within a country.</li><li>B. are disproportionately larger than other cities within a country.</li><li>C. are the largest edge cities within a country.</li><li>D. conform to the rank-size rule as the highest-ranked city in a country.</li><li>E. are giant conurbations.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Countries whose cities' populations do not conform to the rank-size rule tend to exhibit a primate city pattern. Countries with primate cities tend to be either former colonial cities or cities where a current or past monarchy resided. Both types of primate cities tend to concentrate political and economic power in one place, and within such countries, one urban area contains the majority of the urban population. Unit 6.</p>
</div>

## Question 454

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 454</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> According to the gravity model, technological improvements to transportation and communications technology should</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. not affect the probability of interaction between two places.</li><li>B. increase the population of the two places.</li><li>C. decrease the amount of interaction between two places.</li><li>D. decrease the population in the two places.</li><li>E. decrease the friction of distance.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) The gravity model predicts interaction between two places. The standard model states that interaction is a function of the population of two places and the distance between them. As distance increases, likelihood of interaction decreases. However, with technologies that overcome or shrink distance, influence on the probability of spatial interaction decreases.</p>
</div>

## Question 455

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 455</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> In Von Thunen's model of agricultural land use, corn is farmed further from the market than strawberries, why?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. People like strawberries more than bread.</li><li>B. Strawberries generate more revenue per acre.</li><li>C. The climate is different near the market.</li><li>D. Land rent is more expensive farther from the market.</li><li>E. Corn is more expensive to transport.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) According to von Thunen's model, items that are perishable and expensive to transport must be grown or produced close to the market. These items, such as corn and strawberries, also tend to generate larger revenue.</p>
</div>

## Question 456

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 456</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which is true about the conditions of women in more-developed countries (MDC) compared to those in less-developed countries (LDC)?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Women are more likely to be employed in agriculture in MDC.</li><li>B. Women are less likely to be literate in MDC.</li><li>C. Women do not perform labor in MDC.</li><li>D. Women are more likely to participate in government positions in MDC.</li><li>E. Women are more likely to have multiple children in MDC.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(D) Measures of social welfare generally indicate that the conditions for women in the least developed parts of the world are much worse than those of women in the highly developed regions. One such index, the Gender Empowerment Measure, developed by the United Nations, provides an overall picture of women's roles in different countries by looking at their participation in the labor force in professional and technical jobs, their influence in administrative and managerial positions, and their participation in government. According to this measure, women in more developed countries are much more likely to participate in government positions than their counterparts in developing parts of the globe.</p>
</div>

## Question 457

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 457</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> What is the biggest difference between universalizing and ethnic religions?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Ethnic religions are exclusively monotheistic.</li><li>B. Ethnic religions show stronger patterns of spatial diffusion than universalizing religions.</li><li>C. Universalizing religions involve beliefs in one or more deities (gods).</li><li>D. Universalizing religions actively seek new converts.</li><li>E. Universalizing religions are only meant to apply to a particular cultural group.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(C) Universalizing religions, as the term implies, seek to unite people from different backgrounds under one all-encompassing faith. Consequently, a major component of most universal religions involves proselytizing
					</p></div>

## Question 458

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 458</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Which of the following exemplifies how government policy influences agricultural production?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
