<li>A. Increased transport costs for bulkier items</li><li>B. Price supports for milk</li><li>C. Pastoral nomadism</li><li>D. A price increase on oranges after a hard freeze</li><li>E. A market that conforms to von Thunen's model</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(B) Elements of government control exist in even the most commercial of economic systems as illustrated by US price supports for milk and other agricultural goods, which strongly influence production patterns.</p>
</div>

## Question 459

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 459</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> When political geographers describe a district as having been "gerrymandered", they are referring to:</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. an early technique for setting maritime boundaries.</li><li>B. the large number of federal regulations controlling pollution by corporations.</li><li>C. redistricting to ensure a majority-minority population within a district.</li><li>D. unethical zoning restrictions prohibiting low-income families from residing in upper-income areas of cities.</li><li>E. voting district boundaries configured to favor a particular political party or candidate.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) In 1812, Governor Eldridge Gerry of Massachusetts signed into law a voting district that favored his political party. The particular voting district was so convoluted in shape that a political cartoonist converted the new district into a salamander, calling it the "salamander district." The term quickly morphed into "gerrymander," and ever since, redrawing of political boundaries to favor a particular party has been called "gerrymandering."</p>
</div>

## Question 460

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 460</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Raphael's sweatshirt carries a tag stating, "Made in Bangladesh," meaning his sweatshirt was most likely constructed in a(n)</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. offshore financial center.</li><li>B. brick-and-mortar business.</li><li>C. ancillary activity.</li><li>D. informal economic center.</li><li>E. export-processing zone.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>(E) Export-processing zones are a common development strategy in peripheral countries such as Bangladesh because they provide significant employment opportunities. Further, these factories typically employ women, who do not often participate in the formal economy in developing areas.</p>
</div>

## Question 461

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 461</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which statement best exemplifies how the residential spatial patterns of wealthy urbanites in the United States compare with those of the wealthy urbanites in most European cities?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. European and US city dwellers show a very similar pattern: most of the wealthy urbanites live in the central business district (CBD).</li><li>B. In both European and US cities, wealthy urbanites live on large estates far removed from the urban core.</li><li>C. In European cities, wealthy urbanites live in the exurbs and typically telecommute, while wealthy US urbanites live in the CBD.</li><li>D. In European cities, although wealthy people live in the suburbs, they also keep a high presence in the inner rings; in the United States, the wealthy tend to collect in the suburbs.</li><li>E. Both types of cities conform to the sector model: those with wealth are concentrated in a wedge going from the urban core to the suburbs, typically along a major transportation route.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> While there are certainly wealthy people living in America's urban cores, most of America's urban residential wealth is concentrated in the suburbs, where families can enjoy sprawling estates, lower crime rates, and better schools, among other suburban amenities. In contrast, many European urbanites prefer to reside in the urban core to be in close proximity to shops, restaurants, and other cultural amenities.</p>
</div>

## Question 462

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 462</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> If a country with a rapidly growing population were to implement a strict policy of only one child per couple, how would its population pyramid change from the time of implementation to 20 years after?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The pyramid's shape would change from a triangle (the true pyramid shape) to a column as the number of younger children dramatically decreased.</li><li>B. The pyramid would not change; it would be columnar in shape for both time pyramids.</li><li>C. The pyramid would still have a wide base 20 years later because of demographic momentum.</li><li>D. The pyramid would show decline at the base after 20 years because of low replacement-level fertility.</li><li>E. The pyramid would be wide at the top after 20 years as the population policy would lead to a problematic dependency ratio.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Even with a strict policy, because of the pyramid's wide base at the time of implementation, in 20 years, <i>many</i> young people will be having just one child. It will take several generations for the population to actually stabilize, a phenomenon called <i>demographic momentum</i>.</p>
</div>

## Question 463

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 463</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> On the basis of the data, how does a country's level of urbanization relate to its labor-force composition?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Highly urbanized countries, like Australia, concentrate on services.</li><li>B. Less urbanized countries, like Zimbabwe, have a highly diverse labor force.</li><li>C. Urbanized countries tend to have less industry.</li><li>D. Less urbanized countries tend to have less agricultural production.</li><li>E. There is no clear relationship between urbanization and labor-force composition.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Countries that are urbanized tend to have more highly educated populations that specialize in a variety of service-based occupations, jobs that typically concentrate in cities. Countries that are mostly rural have labor forces that obviously concentrate in the agricultural sector of the economy. As countries industrialize, they also typically urbanize, as factories and associated industries tend to concentrate in urban centers.</p>
</div>

## Question 464

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 464</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Given Bangladesh's data, its position in the demographic transition model is most likely</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. stage 1</li><li>B. stage 2</li><li>C. stage 3</li><li>D. stage 4</li><li>E. stage 5</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> As countries industrialize and urbanize, birth rates tend to drop as women become more active in the labor force. A falling birth rate characterizes stage 3 countries, such as in Bangladesh, where women provide the majority of labor in the industrial sector of the economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 465

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 465</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> If the chart contained an additional column with data showing educational attainment of women, what would the data be likely to reveal?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Educational attainment would be highest in Zimbabwe because service-based jobs require low levels of education.</li><li>B. Educational attainment would be highest in Bangladesh because of increasing growth in microcredit for women.</li><li>C. Educational attainment would be the same in Australia and Bangladesh, where industry and service occupation percentages are higher.</li><li>D. Educational attainment would likely be highest in Australia, where service-based occupations dominate.</li><li>E. Data on women's educational attainment would be likely to reveal that the three countries differed only minimally.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Highly developed countries, such as Australia, have strong, service-based economies. These diverse economic systems require an educated population of both males and females.</p>
</div>

## Question 466

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 466</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> New York City and Los Angeles are 3,000 miles apart in terms of absolute distance, but they are quite connected economically and culturally. What explains this connectivity?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The cities have similar transportation and communications infrastructure, which facilitates interaction.</li><li>B. Both have diverse populations, which leads to a common cultural experience.</li><li>C. Both have high populations, which counteract distance in the gravity model.</li><li>D. They have similar economic bases, which leads to higher trade between the two.</li><li>E. Both have airports that allow for large jets and frequent arrivals and departures, and so travel between the two cities is very easy.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> The gravity model predicts interaction between two places on the basis of the size of their population and the distance between them. Large populations (in the numerator) lessen the friction of distance between two places.</p>
</div>

## Question 467

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 467</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Agricultural production in the developed world is difficult to classify as part of the primary economy. Why?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Production no longer happens primarily in a field but rather through high-tech methods such as hydroponics.</li><li>B. Agriculture is primarily controlled by large agribusinesses that encourage large-scale industrial production.</li><li>C. With so little of the labor force engaged in this economic activity, the category essentially no longer exists for the developed world.</li><li>D. Developed countries now outsource all of their agricultural production from the developing world.</li><li>E. Agricultural production is still very much a primary economic activity in the developed world, and its methods are comparable to those of the developing world.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Primary economic activities involve direct extraction of resources from the land. Modern-day agricultural production, particularly in the developed world, is difficult to categorize as a primary economic activity because of how industrialized it has become.</p>
</div>

## Question 468

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 468</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Many countries in developing regions are experiencing dramatic declines in their fertility rates. What is the main cause for this pattern?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Women are marrying less frequently because many developing countries struggle with gender imbalances.</li><li>B. Women are becoming more educated and more active in the formal economy.</li><li>C. Women's access to contraception is getting better.</li><li>D. As more men in developing countries emigrate, women are left with fewer potential marriage partners.</li><li>E. Women are dying from infectious diseases before they reach childbearing age.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> As women gain access to educational and economic opportunities, an additional, professional role is given priority over their roles as wives and homemakers. This additional role tends to lead to less childbearing along with greater investment in the now smaller family's educational opportunities.</p>
</div>

## Question 469

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 469</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Java's population density, by far the highest of Indonesia's 13,000-plus islands, is attributable to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. volcanic activity, which feeds the soil.</li><li>B. government limitations on which islands Indonesians can inhabit.</li><li>C. Java's size</li><li>D. Java's strategic geographic location.</li><li>E. Java's accessibility as an island.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Because of Java's equatorial position, the soil quality should not allow for substantial agricultural production. However, because of volcanic activity on the island, the soil is nutrient-rich and more suited for higher population density than nearby Indonesian islands.</p>
</div>

## Question 470

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 470</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> The cultural landscape is an example of the human-environment relationship in that</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. it shows how the physical environment has been negatively altered to fulfill the needs of a particular cultural group.</li><li>B. it shows how humans have reshaped a local space to meet their needs.</li><li>C. It shows how various cultural groups have suffered or thrived on the basis of geographic conditions.</li><li>D. it shows how spatial variation in this relationship might be used for finding ways to curb environmental damage resulting from human activity.</li><li>E. the cultural landscape involves investigation and analysis of human activity, but it does not consider the physical environment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Cultural landscapes include the interaction of physical features, economic practices, religious and linguistic characteristics, and other forms of cultural expression all in one space. As a result, they nearly perfectly embody the concept of the human-environment relationship.</p>
</div>

## Question 471

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 471</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> The ideas of Thomas Malthus and the neo-Malthusians describe the tension that exists between</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. gender equality and fertility.</li><li>B. population growth and poverty.</li><li>C. social welfare (health care, education) and fertility.</li><li>D. economic growth and population decline.</li><li>E. population growth and consumption of resources, including food.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> Malthus and those that subscribe to his ideas posit that when populations exceed the resource base needed to support them, the population must be "checked" through war, famine, disease, or some other means.</p>
</div>

## Question 472

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 472</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> In squatter settlements in many Latin American cities, poor rural-to-urban migrants tend to make a living in which sector of the economy?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Basic</li><li>B. Informal</li><li>C. Nonbasic</li><li>D. Formal</li><li>E. Primary</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Most migrants in squatter settlements have relocated to the city in search of employment in growing urban economies. Until these individuals can secure a job in the formal economy, they make a living through informal economic activities, such as the sale of goods (e.g., food, clothing, handicrafts) or services (e.g., child care, handiwork, transportation).</p>
</div>

## Question 473

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 473</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> How is microcredit related to other common economic opportunities for women in the developing world, specifically work in an export-processing zone (EPZ)?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. In order to fund dormitory housing, women must have microcredit to work in an export-processing zone.</li><li>B. Microcredit is the main avenue for union formation, which works to combat unfair labor conditions in factories.</li><li>C. With microloans, women can control their own businesses and therefore set their own hours and wages.</li><li>D. With microloans, women can pay for child care while they work factory jobs in the EPZ.</li><li>E. In the developing world, microcredit is available only to men; women must be married to have access to it.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Microlending is proving to be a revolutionary sustainable development strategy as it allows women to control how they earn and spend money. They are not at the mercy of factory owners who require them to work long hours in substandard conditions, as is often the case for female laborers in export-processing zones.</p>
</div>

## Question 474

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 474</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> The cultural and political ideas of nationalism can work to sever the social fabric of a state. In this case, nationalism can be seen as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a push factor.</li><li>B. a pull factor.</li><li>C. a centrifugal force.</li><li>D. a centripetal force.</li><li>E. an intervening opportunity.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Centrifugal forces are those that tear apart the social fabric of a country and can potentially lead to devolution. When a state is made up of multiple ethnic groups, nationalism can become a threat if those ethnic groups compete with one another for political dominance.</p>
</div>

## Question 475

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 475</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> _________ involves the economic and political domination of one state by another, while _____________ includes official, institutionalized government rule.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Regionalism . . . sectionalism</li><li>B. Sectionalism . . . regionalism</li><li>C. Imperialism . . . colonialism</li><li>D. Colonialism . . . imperialism</li><li>E. Nationalism . . . isolationism</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> A country need not have formal rule over another in order to dominate it. Imperialism can include cultural, political, and other forms of external control. Colonialism includes officially organized political and military rule.</p>
</div>

## Question 476

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 476</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Russia's takeover of the Crimean Peninsula, given the language patterns, illustrates which concept?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Irredentism</li><li>B. Gerrymandering</li><li>C. Devolution</li><li>D. Terrorism</li><li>E. Demilitarization</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Irredentism describes any political or popular movement that involves reclaiming a territory that previously belonged to the movement's members-in this case, Russia. As seen on the accompanying map, the majority of Crimea's population is of Russian descent. Russia gifted the peninsula to Ukraine in 1954. The referendum, deemed illegal by the United Nations, was an effort to reestablish the territory as Russian.</p>
</div>

## Question 477

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 477</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> What does the map show about differences between ethnic boundaries and political boundaries?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. That ethnic boundaries do not typically differ from political boundaries</li><li>B. That political boundaries, which indicate sovereignty, sometimes fail to recognize cultural and ethnic diversity within a territory</li><li>C. That ethnic boundaries are absolute, whereas political boundaries are relative</li><li>D. That political boundaries are fuzzy, whereas ethnic boundaries are clearly defined</li><li>E. That both political and ethnic boundaries are clearly defined in the landscape</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Boundary lines can be defined in numerous ways. Sometimes political boundary lines, which indicate internationally recognized sovereignty over certain areas, do not align with ethnic, linguistic, and cultural boundaries, which tend to be fuzzier but are often more important, as they indicate a region with a common language and common customs.</p>
</div>

## Question 478

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 478</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Why is it important to look at linguistic diversity on a national scale in addition to a global scale?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It is likely that there would be little difference between global and national maps when looking at linguistic diversity.</li><li>B. The global-scale map shows variation that would be difficult to detect on a national-scale map.</li><li>C. The national map shows patterns that would not be apparent on a global map.</li><li>D. Global-scale maps are more distorted than national-scale maps.</li><li>E. Data tends to lose accuracy as a map's scale becomes larger.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> As shown in the map accompanying the question, some parts of Ukraine use Russian much more prevalently than Ukrainian, their official language. Having access to data at a finer scale, in this case the national scale as opposed to the global scale, allows for greater insight into spatial patterns.</p>
</div>

## Question 479

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 479</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Von Thunen's model of rural land use is based on which of the following premises?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Value of land decreases the farther it is from the urban center.</li><li>B. Value of land increases the farther it is from the urban center.</li><li>C. Perishable goods are the least valuable.</li><li>D. Railroads provide fixed transportation costs.</li><li>E. Vegetarianism is environmentally beneficial.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> In von Thunen's model, agricultural land use changes with distance from the city center, primarily due to land and commodity values. Expensive, perishable commodities are grown closer to urban markets, while less expensive, more expansive (in terms of land area necessary for cultivation) agricultural goods are grown farther from the city center.</p>
</div>

## Question 480

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 480</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Some political geographers argue that every war is fought essentially for space (space to rule, space in which to practice one's religion, space to harvest certain resources, etc.). This argument illustrates the power of which concept?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Territoriality</li><li>B. Proxemics</li><li>C. Ethology</li><li>D. Sacred space</li><li>E. Topophilia</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Territoriality describes the deep connection of a people, their culture, and their economic systems to their land. Because of this deep connection and all that it encompasses, disputes or wars often center on maintaining ownership or control of land.</p>
</div>

## Question 481

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 481</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Because of its heritage of the Catalan language and culture, Catalonia, a region in northeast Spain, voted on which of the following in 2017?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Electoral reapportionment</li><li>B. Economic freedom</li><li>C. Unitary standing</li><li>D. Self-determination</li><li>E. Membership in the United Nations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Catalonia, because of its unique language and cultural identity, sought independence from Spain in a referendum in October 2017. The referendum was not recognized by the Spanish government, which considered it illegal.</p>
</div>

## Question 482

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 482</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> "Food security" is the term used to describe</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. reliable access, across scales, to food at all times.</li><li>B. a reliable national system for ensuring food safety.</li><li>C. a reliable labeling system that lets people know what they are consuming (e.g., GMOs).</li><li>D. a reliable international trading system that insures against fluctuation in the market.</li><li>E. a reliable international regulatory system that ensures similar safety standards across the globe.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Food security is a condition related to food supply and an individual's access to it. It is a concern whose scale encompasses everything from food deserts in some of America's urban centers to entire countries that struggle against famine.</p>
</div>

## Question 483

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 483</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> The disproportionate siting of power plants and waste-disposal facilities in African American and Latino neighborhoods
						<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. postmaterialism.</li><li>B. environmental racism.</li><li>C. deindustrialization.</li><li>D. environmental justice.</li><li>E. ecological inferiority.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Environmental racism is any activity that causes people of a particular racial or ethnic group to be purposefully and disproportionately exposed to environmental hazards and pollution or to be denied access to environmental amenities such as clean water and open space.</p>
</p></div>

## Question 484

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 484</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> The religious practices of some Native American groups combine elements from their traditional religion and from Christianity. This is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a cultural complex.</li><li>B. a cultural confluence.</li><li>C. a counterculture.</li><li>D. a cultural diaspora.</li><li>E. a cultural syncretism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> A cultural syncretism occurs when two or more different cultures or cultural traits converge to form something new.</p>
</div>

## Question 485

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 485</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> _____ maps work well for locating and navigating between places, while __________ maps display one or more variables across a specific space.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Reference . . . thematic</li><li>B. Thematic . . . reference</li><li>C. Spatial . . . cartographic</li><li>D. Cartographic . . . spatial</li><li>E. Topologic . . . choropleth</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Another way to think about cartographic representation is to divide maps into those used for reference and those that focus on a specific theme. An example of a reference map would be a road map or an atlas. An example of a thematic map would be a dot map that shows instances of petty crimes in the London metropolitan area.</p>
</div>

## Question 486

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 486</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> The excerpt reveals the tension in many urban areas around which of the following urban geography processes?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Gentrification</li><li>B. Commercialization</li><li>C. New urbanism</li><li>D. Edge cities</li><li>E. Primate cities</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Gentrification describes the process whereby people, typically middle- and upper-income people, move into city centers and rehabilitate much of the architecture for commercial and residential purposes. While it has its benefits, gentrification can also displace low-income populations and change the social character of certain neighborhoods.</p>
</div>

## Question 487

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 487</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> "Preserving the street's character" is an example of the importance of which of the following concepts?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Place</li><li>B. Space</li><li>C. Distance</li><li>D. Absolute location</li><li>E. Relative location</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> A space describes a location-an address or a set of coordinates-whereas the concept of "place" connotes the set of characteristics that make a location special and unique. It is essentially the difference between a house and a home: a house being the structure you live in and "home" describing the feeling you have about the structure and the people and things within it.</p>
</div>

## Question 488

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 488</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> On the basis of this excerpt, those most likely to relocate to gentrified areas seem to be</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. families.</li><li>B. retired couples.</li><li>C. low-income or unemployed individuals.</li><li>D. young, creative entrepreneurs.</li><li>E. working-class couples.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Gentrified urban areas typically attract young, single entrepreneurs, white-collar workers, and couples without kids. While gentrified areas offer the attraction of cultural amenities, restaurants, and bars, they do not often offer the types of amenities sought by families, such as large yards, high-quality education, and varying recreational opportunities.</p>
</div>

## Question 489

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 489</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Swahili is the language of trade for most of East Africa and the only African language in use by the African Union. As such it is a good example of a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. lingua franca.</li><li>B. dialect.</li><li>C. syncretism.</li><li>D. Creole.</li><li>E. cultural hearth.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> A lingua franca is a simple language that combines aspects of two or more other, more-complex languages; it is usually used for quick and efficient communication.</p>
</div>

## Question 490

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 490</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Slash-and-burn agriculture meets all of the following conditions EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. it occurs mainly in tropical environments.</li><li>B. it is associated with deforestation.</li><li>C. it is part of the Green Revolution.</li><li>D. it was practiced sustainably by indigenous peoples.</li><li>E. it is uncommon in the temperate latitudes.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Slash-and-burn agriculture historically was practiced in a sustainable manner by native people in tropical regions across the globe. However, it has now become associated with population growth, migration, and tropical deforestation in Brazil and elsewhere. It is not part of the Green Revolution, which involves increasing crop yield through new crop strains and other technological systems.</p>
</div>

## Question 491

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 491</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The pan-Arab region of northern Africa and Southwest Asia is best classified as which region type?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Functional region</li><li>B. Formal region</li><li>C. Administrative region</li><li>D. Perceptual region</li><li>E. Hierarchical region</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> A formal region is one in which the population shares one or more unique characteristics, such as language, religion, and ethnicity. The boundary that defines the pan-Arab region includes people that typically embrace Islam and are of Arab descent.</p>
</div>

## Question 492

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 492</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Which of the following universalizing religions originated in northern India and then spread across Central and Southeast Asia, Indonesia, and Japan?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Hinduism</li><li>B. Buddhism</li><li>C. Islam</li><li>D. Taoism</li><li>E. Judaism</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Buddhism, one of the three great world religions, began in the Indian subcontinent and then spread across central and eastern Asia.</p>
</div>

## Question 493

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 493</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The Industrial Revolution transformed Western agriculture</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. through mechanization and the creation of new markets.</li><li>B. with biotechnology.</li><li>C. through technological and religious change.</li><li>D. by eliminating agricultural pests.</li><li>E. by eliminating plant hybridization.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> During the Industrial Revolution, many people migrated from rural areas to large urban centers, generating a great need for agricultural goods within those centers. Furthermore, the technology characteristics of the Industrial Revolution transformed agricultural production as mechanization allowed more rapid cultivation of greater expanses of land.</p>
</div>

## Question 494

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 494</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following BEST describes the purpose of the European Union?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. An economic organization whose focus is on easy flow of goods, services, and people among member nations</li><li>B. A political organization whose focus is on maintaining peaceful relations, particularly with nations to the east of Europe</li><li>C. A diplomatic organization whose focus is on increasing democracy and capitalism in the Western world</li><li>D. A cultural organization whose focus is on cultural integration across a variety of ethnicities and religions</li><li>E. A social organization whose focus is on easing relations between a diverse set of ethnic and religious groups</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> The European Union, which stemmed from the European Economic Community, is at its heart an economic organization that integrated separate economies into one unit in order to be more competitive in the global marketplace.</p>
</div>

## Question 495

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 495</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> In general, the countries with the least linguistic diversity tend to be located</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. in the southern hemisphere.</li><li>B. in the eastern hemisphere.</li><li>C. in the world's most developed regions.</li><li>D. in the world's least developed regions.</li><li>E. in the Americas.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Some of the world's least-developed regions, including sub-Saharan Africa, South Asia, and Southeast Asia, are rich in linguistic diversity, as opposed to developed regions of North America, Western Europe, and Oceania, where linguistic diversity tends to be quite low.</p>
</div>

## Question 496

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 496</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following are the correct scales of analysis presented by these two maps?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Regional vs. national</li><li>B. Global vs. regional</li><li>C. Global vs. national</li><li>D. Global vs. local</li><li>E. National vs. province</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> One map shows variation in linguistics across the globe-global scale. The other shows variation within a nation-state or country-national scale. Comparing data across scales allows for a richer and more nuanced understanding of a pattern or trend.</p>
</div>

## Question 497

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 497</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Which of the following is the likely result of Nigeria's linguistic diversity?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Increased political fragmentation as linguistic diversity often acts as a centripetal force</li><li>B. Increased immigration as linguistic diversity attracts Africans from across the continent</li><li>C. Increased global trade as linguistic diversity opens up economic opportunities</li><li>D. Decreased political tension as diversity leads to tolerance</li><li>E. Decreased immigration as people stick to their own ethnic enclaves</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> While Nigeria's linguistic diversity contributes to its rich history, strong family traditions, and vibrant culture, it also contributes to political tension. Operating as one cohesive nation with a multiplicity of languages and ethnicities proves challenging.</p>
</div>

## Question 498

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 498</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> The fact that Cincinnati, OH, is able to support a major-league baseball team and an NFL football team, while its neighbor, Toledo, can support only a minor league team, is largely attributable to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. metropolitan-area theory.</li><li>B. sector theory.</li><li>C. central-place theory.</li><li>D. urban-matrix theory.</li><li>E. the rank-size rule.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Central-place theory describes the organization of urban areas in a region or country. According to the theory, there should be a few large centers that provide a wide range of goods and services requiring a large market area (like a major-league baseball team). The central place is surrounded by a matrix of smaller cities, towns, and hamlets that offer progressively fewer products and enticements.</p>
</div>

## Question 499

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 499</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> One important consequence of cultural extinction is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. decreasing population.</li><li>B. increased poverty in peripheral regions.</li><li>C. loss of genetic diversity.</li><li>D. loss of indigenous knowledge about ecosystems.</li><li>E. increasing population.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Many geographers, ecologists, and medical researchers have noted that indigenous knowledge about nature can be helpful in understanding ecosystems and in locating potential organisms for biomedical research. However, with decreasing cultural diversity, such knowledge is inevitably being lost.</p>
</div>

## Question 500

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 500</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> States with a federal form of government must also have</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. territorial organization.</li><li>B. fascist regimes.</li><li>C. social-democracies.</li><li>D. proportional representation.</li><li>E. congressional oversight.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Federalism implies territorial organization. In territorial organization, national governments divide up their land base into smaller units, such as states and counties. These smaller units assume some level of autonomy in local governance and representation.</p>
</div>

## Question 501

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 501</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which urban model best describes the typical suburban American city?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Multiple-nuclei model</li><li>B. Concentric-zone model</li><li>C. Demographic-transition model</li><li>D. Hoyt-sector model</li><li>E. Ecological model of urban land use</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> The multiple-nuclei model describes urban areas that contain numerous centers of business and cultural activity rather than a single central place. As American communities have become increasingly suburbanized, commercial and cultural opportunities have spread to the suburbs, creating multiple nuclei of activity within one urban area.</p>
</div>

## Question 502

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 502</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Monocultural agricultural systems tend to be most prevalent</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. in the least-developed countries and regions of the world.</li><li>B. in developing countries that are transitioning through industrialization.</li><li>C. in highly developed countries with labor-force concentrations in the tertiary and quaternary sectors.</li><li>D. in challenging climate regimes.</li><li>E. in tropical climate regimes where slash-and-burn is practiced.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> In highly developed countries, labor is concentrated in the service sector of the economy. Machines do the bulk of agricultural work instead of people, a process most suited to monoculture crops such as corn, soybeans, cotton, and wheat.</p>
</div>

## Question 503

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 503</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> To get an understanding of voting patterns within the Los Angeles metropolitan area, what would be the best scale at which to investigate these data?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Global</li><li>B. Country</li><li>C. State</li><li>D. County</li><li>E. Census tract</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> The finer the scale, the greater the ability to recognize and understand spatial patterns. If voting patterns are looked at on the state scale, Los Angeles County is likely to be categorized in one way. When the data are looked at by census tract, voting patterns in different parts of the city become observable.</p>
</div>

## Question 504

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 504</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Many of the most successful and sustainable population programs focus on which of the following as a means for curbing fertility rates?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Establishing quotas on resources such as food, water, and land</li><li>B. Increasing access to sterilization procedures for males and females</li><li>C. Increasing women's access to education</li><li>D. Instituting penalties on families that have more than a designated number of children</li><li>E. Providing incentives to make it easier for women to stay at home with their children</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> As women gain access to education, employment opportunities in the formal economy open up to them. With more time invested in education and employment, less time is available to manage a family. Furthermore, as women become more educated, their awareness of family planning increases. Taken together, these factors lead to a dramatically lower fertility rate.</p>
</div>

## Question 505

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 505</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Replacing imports with goods manufactured locally (import substitution) falls under which philosophy of development?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Sustainable</li><li>B. Modernization</li><li>C. Neoliberal</li><li>D. Dependency</li><li>E. Maturity</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> The dependency theory of development describes a desire to become economically self-sufficient rather than relying on the problematic economic relationship set into play under colonization. Instead of relying on their colonizers for expensive manufactured imports, newly independent countries chose to develop a manufacturing base in order to substitute imports with domestically manufactured goods.</p>
</div>

## Question 506

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 506</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0281-01.jpg"/></p><p>The pattern on this map is the likely result of which of the following processes?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Stepped migration</li><li>B. Chain migration</li><li>C. Forced migration</li><li>D. Redlining</li><li>E. Blockbusting</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Chain migration describes the social process by which immigrants from a particular area follow others, typically family members or close friends, to a new area. These new neighborhoods often take on the cultural characteristics of "home" and include restaurants, stores, and places of worship, among other things.</p>
</div>

## Question 507

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 507</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> The political geographic concept of the nation is defined as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a group of people defined and organized by a centralized government.</li><li>B. a smaller unit of a federal system, such as a Canadian province.</li><li>C. a group of people represented by a singular and unique culture.</li><li>D. a group of people with a singular culture and a singular government.</li><li>E. being synonymous with a state or country.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> A nation is not synonymous with a state or country, both of which connote political sovereignty over a particular piece of space. A nation is a tightly knit group of individuals that share a language, ethnicity, religion, and other unique cultural attributes.</p>
</div>

## Question 508

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 508</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> What is most responsible for hierarchical diffusion, as opposed to contagious diffusion?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Distance decay effects</li><li>B. Special network links between major nodes</li><li>C. Some people need multiple contacts before they adopt an innovation.</li><li>D. Proximity of the innovation to the varying degrees of diffusion</li><li>E. Relevance of particular innovations only to specific locations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Hierarchical diffusion describes the spread of an innovation through specific nodes that are not usually located close together in space but exhibit strong links to one another in a network.</p>
</div>

## Question 509

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 509</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> In highly developed countries such as France and Germany, what lies behind most population growth?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Natural increase</li><li>B. Immigration</li><li>C. Emigration</li><li>D. Adoption</li><li>E. Population is declining, not growing, in these countries.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> France and Germany, both highly developed countries, are in stage 4 of the demographic transition model, meaning each couple replaces itself, if that. In order for the population of these countries to grow, they must allow for immigration. The opportunities available in both countries make them appealing destinations for many migrants.</p>
</div>

## Question 510

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 510</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following countries is likely to list HIV/AIDS as a significant cause of death?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Finland</li><li>B. Brazil</li><li>C. Botswana</li><li>D. Mongolia</li><li>E. Turkmenistan</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Botswana, located in sub-Saharan Africa, is a low-income nation that has been ravished by the HIV/AIDS epidemic. As the graph shows, low-income countries struggle much more with infectious diseases than do high-income countries.</p>
</div>

## Question 511

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 511</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which human geography concept or model explains the difference between causes of death in low-income vs. high-income countries?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Core-periphery model</li><li>B. Epidemiological transition</li><li>C. Demographic transition</li><li>D. Rostow's modernization model</li><li>E. Differing beliefs on vaccination</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Epidemiological transition accounts for the replacement of infectious diseases with chronic diseases as a major cause of death. As countries become more developed, they gain access to the medical care that prevents infectious disease, as well as discover the causes of chronic diseases (sedentary occupations, processed foods, and the like).</p>
</div>

## Question 512

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 512</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Development indicators are often categorized as economic or social. How should mortality rates be categorized?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. As a social indicator of development</li><li>B. As an economic indicator of development</li><li>C. As both a social and an economic indicator of development</li><li>D. If mortality is included with economics, as an economic indicator of development</li><li>E. As having nothing to do with development</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Economic indicators of development typically describe measures of wealth, such as Gross National Product and Gross National Income. Social-welfare indicators demonstrate how a country is investing in the well-being of its population in terms of education, health, and other social services. Therefore, mortality rates are often seen as a social indicator of economic development.</p>
</div>

## Question 513

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 513</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0283-01.jpg"/></p><p>This image above illustrates which of the following processes?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Chain migration</li><li>B. Forced migration</li><li>C. Voluntary migration</li><li>D. Step migration</li><li>E. Ravenstein's third law of migration</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> In forced migration, people leave an area for reasons other than their own choice. Factors leading to this movement include political unrest, religious persecution, ethnic cleansing, and environmental degradation. Often those fleeing their homes for these reasons seek refuge in a different country, as illustrated in this photo of a refugee camp in Pakistan.</p>
</div>

## Question 514

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 514</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Many of Africa's recent political and economic challenges can be attributed to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. lack of natural resources.</li><li>B. climate change.</li><li>C. colonialism.</li><li>D. nepotism.</li><li>E. the Cold War.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Many attribute the lack of political cohesion in much of sub-Saharan Africa to the way colonizing countries divided the space without any consideration of ethnic boundaries. Even after decolonization, much of the region's resources still flow out, with the wealth often accruing to corporations based in the countries of the former colonizers.</p>
</div>

## Question 515

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 515</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> A Pakistani family moves to a predominantly Pakistani neighborhood in London, where the family members maintain many of their cultural traditions. Which of the following terms best describes this circumstance?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A diorama</li><li>B. A diaspora</li><li>C. An ethnic enclave</li><li>D. Step migration</li><li>E. Gentrification</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> A diaspora refers to a group of people with a common ethnic identity who are spread out over a large geographic area. Such an ethnic group often exists in an enclave that allows its members to maintain the group's cultural traditions.</p>
</div>

## Question 516

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 516</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which of the following is an example of how patterns of food production and consumption have shifted in highly developed countries, such as the United States, in recent years?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The rise of pesticides and other chemicals</li><li>B. The rise of genetically modified organisms (GMOs)</li><li>C. The rise of agricultural machinery</li><li>D. The rise in number and popularity of urban farmer's markets</li><li>E. The decline in food-related legislation</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> The growth in farmer's markets and urban gardening in highly developed countries, particularly the United States, indicates a growing backlash against large-scale industrial agriculture. Many consumers want to support local farms and farmers so as to be assured that their food is healthy for themselves and the environment.</p>
</div>

## Question 517

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 517</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> The growing number of retirement homes and memory-care facilities being built throughout the Western world is an indication of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A columnar-shaped population pyramid</li><li>B. A population pyramid with a wide bottom</li><li>C. A problematic dependency ratio</li><li>D. A problematic family dynamic</li><li>E. A problematic health-care system</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> The dependency ratio refers to the percentage of people in a population who are either too old or too young to work and thus must rely on the productive labor of others to meet their needs. The growing number of retirement homes in developed countries, particularly the United States, reflects the entry of baby boomers into the later stages of life.</p>
</div>

## Question 518

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 518</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> According to the gravity model, technological improvements in transportation and communications technology should</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. have no effect on the probability of interaction between two places.</li><li>B. increase the population of the two places.</li><li>C. decrease the amount of interaction between two places.</li><li>D. decrease the population in the two places.</li><li>E. decrease the friction of distance.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> The gravity model predicts interaction between two places. The standard model states that interaction is a function of the population of two places and the distance between them. As distance increases, the likelihood of interaction decreases. However, with technologies that overcome or shrink distance, its influence on the probability of spatial interaction decreases.</p>
</div>

## Question 519

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 519</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> A Geographic Information System (GIS) differs from a traditional map in what ways?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A traditional map typically shows only land features, whereas a GIS takes a variety of different phenomena into account.</li><li>B. Data can be more easily manipulated or analyzed within a GIS, whereas information is static on a traditional map.</li><li>C. A GIS produces a thematic map, whereas a traditional map tends to be a reference map.</li><li>D. Because a GIS is on a computer, it isn't projected; a traditional map is.</li><li>E. There are no major differences between a GIS and a traditional map.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> GIS combines "geographic" (maps) and "information" (data) in one digital system that can integrate multiple layers of geospatial information. These layers can be manipulated or queried to conduct varying levels of spatial analysis. Thus, GIS is dynamic, while a traditional paper map is static.</p>
</div>

## Question 520

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 520</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Domingo owns a piece of land in the US Southwest that he irrigated heavily in order to grow tomatoes. Domingo's land is now infertile. What process is most likely to have caused Domingo's soil to become unproductive?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Gentrification</li><li>B. Deforestation</li><li>C. Salinization</li><li>D. Bromidification</li><li>E. Desertification</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> When farmers irrigate desert landscapes in an effort to increase productivity of an otherwise unproductive piece of land, the outcome typically involves salinization. The water applied to the land through irrigation evaporates quickly in the hot temperatures associated with these climates. After evaporation, a thick salty residue remains that renders the soil infertile. This process is what is meant by the term "salinization."</p>
</div>

## Question 521

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 521</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following best describes the difference between hierarchical and contagious diffusion?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. In hierarchical diffusion, transmission occurs due to the relationships between places, whereas in contagious diffusion, transmission occurs due to the proximity between places.</li><li>B. Hierarchical diffusion is rare, whereas contagious diffusion is common.</li><li>C. Hierarchical diffusion occurs when people stay in place, whereas contagious diffusion occurs when they move.</li><li>D. Hierarchical diffusion is a form of expansion diffusion, whereas contagious diffusion is a form of relocation diffusion.</li><li>E. In hierarchical diffusion, transmission occurs due to the proximity between places, whereas in contagious diffusion, transmission occurs due to the relationships between places.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Hierarchical diffusion occurs when a cultural trait is transmitted from one place to another because the two places have some common characteristic or relationship. It is different from contagious diffusion, in which a cultural trait is passed from one person or place to another simply because of their proximity.</p>
</div>

## Question 522

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 522</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> When recent college graduates and young professionals move to large cities with cultural amenities and job opportunities, to what are they responding?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Suburban amenities</li><li>B. Push factors</li><li>C. Pull factors</li><li>D. Mobility opportunities</li><li>E. Centripetal forces</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Pull factors, such as job and recreational opportunities, attract people to move to new places. Push factors, such as violence and economic stagnation, encourage people to leave their old homes and search for new places to live with better prospects.</p>
</div>

## Question 523

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 523</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0310-01.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the countries represented in the figure above is experiencing the slowest rate of population growth?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Denmark</li><li>B. United States</li><li>C. Kenya</li><li>D. Denmark and the United States are roughly equivalent.</li><li>E. The country with the greatest proportion of young people</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> The population pyramids provided show that Denmark, which has the smallest proportion of young people and largest proportion of older people, is experiencing the slowest population growth.</p>
</div>

## Question 524

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 524</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The largely urbanized landscape that stretches along the US eastern seaboard from Washington, D.C., to Boston is an example of what?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A megacity</li><li>B. An edge city</li><li>C. A megalopolis</li><li>D. An urban agglomeration economy</li><li>E. A primate city</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> A megalopolis is an entire region that has become highly urbanized. In North America, megalopolises include the Boston-New York-Philadelphia-Baltimore-Washington, D.C. urban mass along the eastern seaboard and the Los Angeles-Orange County-San Diego-Tijuana megalopolis in southern California and Baja, Mexico.</p>
</div>

## Question 525

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 525</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which of the following describes religions that combine elements of Christianity with other traditional beliefs or practices?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Independent innovation of cultural traits</li><li>B. False idols</li><li>C. Cultural lags</li><li>D. Creolized religion</li><li>E. Cultural appropriation</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Creolized religions combine aspects of world religions with local beliefs and traditional practices to create something new.</p>
</div>

## Question 526

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 526</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following does not describe the Green Revolution?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Development and improvement of agricultural chemicals</li><li>B. Technological improvements such as hybrid seeds</li><li>C. Transfer of knowledge and technology from developed to developing countries</li><li>D. Application of more environmentally sustainable farming techniques</li><li>E. Intensification of farming practices in developing regions</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> The Green Revolution was an effort to increase agricultural yields in the short term through the use of selective breeding, technology, and fertilizers. It did not seek to be more environmentally sustainable in the long term.</p>
</div>

## Question 527

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 527</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> A ___________ is a group of people with a common cultural identity, whereas a __________ is a country with established and recognized borders.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. territory . . . state</li><li>B. nation . . . territory</li><li>C. state . . . territory</li><li>D. nation . . . state</li><li>E. territory . . . nation</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> A nation is a group of people with a common cultural identity, whereas a state is a country with established and recognized borders.</p>
</div>

## Question 528

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 528</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Which of the following is not included as a term in the demographic accounting equation?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Natural increase</li><li>B. Natural decrease</li><li>C. Total fertility rate</li><li>D. Immigration</li><li>E. Emigration</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Natural decrease is not a term in the demographic accounting equation, but a country can have a negative rate of natural increase.</p>
</div>

## Question 529

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 529</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which of the following refers to a simplified language used to communicate among people who speak different native tongues?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Dialect</li><li>B. Pidgin</li><li>C. Lingua franca</li><li>D. Creole</li><li>E. Accent</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> A lingua franca is a simplified language often used to communicate when traveling or engaging in trade.</p>
</div>

## Question 530

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 530</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0311-01.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the following describes a country in stage 3 of the demographic transition model shown above?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It has a high and consistent death rate.</li><li>B. It has a high and consistent birth rate.</li><li>C. It has a stable population.</li><li>D. It is undergoing rapid but declining population growth.</li><li>E. It is undergoing slow but increasing population growth.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> In stage 3, death rates decline dramatically, followed by birth rates. The decline in death rates results, for a time, in rapid growth, but this growth slows considerably as birth rates drop. Longer lives and lower fertility are common in more-developed countries.</p>
</div>

## Question 531

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 531</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which of the following best describes a primate city?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The major seat of political power within a country</li><li>B. A city that is disproportionately larger than other cities in a country</li><li>C. The largest edge city in a country</li><li>D. The top city in the rank-size hierarchy</li><li>E. A suburban metropolis</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> A primate city is one that is disproportionately larger-at least twice as large and often several times bigger-than other cities in a country. Many countries have primate cities. Paris and London are examples, as are Mexico City and Tokyo. The United States, China, India, and Germany are examples of countries without true primate cities.</p>
</div>

## Question 532

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 532</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> According to the gravity model, technological improvements in transportation and communication between two places should result in which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They should have no effect on the two places' interactions.</li><li>B. They should cause an increase in the populations of both places.</li><li>C. They should cause a decrease in the amount of interaction between the two places.</li><li>D. They should cause a decrease in the populations of both places.</li><li>E. They should cause a decline in the friction of distance between the two places.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> The gravity model says that greater connectivity between two places will reduce the friction of distance between them. They will seem closer together even though they remain the same distance apart.</p>
</div>

## Question 533

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 533</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Which of the following terms best describes the makeshift neighborhoods, constructed of inexpensive scrap materials, found in all of the world's largest peripheral cities?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Edge cities</li><li>B. Squatter settlements</li><li>C. Swidden lands</li><li>D. Gentrified districts</li><li>E. Informal economic sectors</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Squatter settlements are unplanned neighborhoods that have developed around the world in fast-growing cities in developing countries. These neighborhoods often lack basic infrastructure and services and are plagued by crime, but their resilient residents are known for finding creative ways to overcome these challenges and hardships.</p>
</div>

## Question 534

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 534</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> According to von Thunen's model of regional agricultural landscapes and economies, why is wheat farmed farther than dairy is from the markets where both are sold?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. People like milk more than bread.</li><li>B. Dairy generates more revenue per acre.</li><li>C. The climate is different near the market.</li><li>D. Land rent is more expensive farther from the market.</li><li>E. Wheat is more expensive to transport.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Dairy generates greater profits from a smaller land area, making it better suited for the higher rents closer to markets. Dairy is also heavier than wheat per unit sold, which increases transportation costs.</p>
</div>

## Question 535

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 535</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> On a topographic contour (isoline) map, which pattern of contour lines corresponds to the steepest slope?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Open areas with no contour lines</li><li>B. Widely spaced contour lines</li><li>C. Evenly spaced contour lines</li><li>D. Closely spaced contour lines</li><li>E. Only elevation, not slope, can be deciphered from contour lines</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Since topographic contour lines follow points of equal elevation, the closer the contour lines are, the steeper the slope they describe.</p>
</div>

## Question 536

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 536</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which is a good example of a functional region?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The Bible Belt states</li><li>B. The area served by a local bus line</li><li>C. The state of California</li><li>D. An individual's perception of his/her daily activity space</li><li>E. An area where one dominant language prevails</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Unlike other region types, which are typically defined according to some sort of uniform characteristic within an area, a functional region is defined by a particular function, usually involving spatial interaction, which takes place within a fairly defined boundary. The only option among the possible responses that describes a functional region of interaction is that of the area a local bus line serves.</p>
</div>

## Question 537

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 537</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> On a Mercator projection map, where will you find the landmasses most exaggerated in relative size?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Near the poles</li><li>B. Near the prime meridian</li><li>C. Near the equator</li><li>D. Near the major oceans</li><li>E. Near the tropics</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Because it is impossible to project a rounded surface onto a flat one with full accuracy, all map projections distort either area, distance, shape, or direction. The Mercator projection distorts area such that landmasses near the poles appear far bigger than they actually are relative to landmasses at lower latitudes.</p>
</div>

## Question 538

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 538</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0312-01.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the following is the proper term for the above map depicting the size of each country in proportion to its population?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. An image map</li><li>B. A choropleth map</li><li>C. A projected map</li><li>D. An isoline map</li><li>E. A cartogram</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> A choropleth map uses area to depict relative values, such as population size.</p>
</div>

## Question 539

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 539</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> When looking at labor-force distribution on a global scale, which of the following patterns is generally true?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. In highly developed (rich) countries, the labor force is evenly distributed across all economic sectors (primary, secondary, tertiary, and quaternary).</li><li>B. In the least-developed countries, most laborers are in service-based industries (tertiary sector).</li><li>C. Since the world's wealthiest countries tend to have vast natural resources, their labor forces are mainly in the primary sector (agriculture and mining).</li><li>D. A poor country's labor force is concentrated in the primary sector, while a richer country's labor force skews toward the tertiary and quaternary sectors.</li><li>E. Both highly developed and least-developed countries.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Poor countries have labor forces concentrated in the primary sector, while a richer country's labor force skews toward the tertiary and quaternary sectors.</p>
</div>

## Question 540

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 540</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Which is generally true regarding the conditions of women in more-developed countries (MDCs) compared to those in less-developed countries (LDCs)?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Women are more likely to be employed in agriculture in MDCs.</li><li>B. Women are less likely to be literate in MDCs.</li><li>C. Women do not perform labor in MDCs.</li><li>D. Women are more likely to participate in government positions in MDCs.</li><li>E. Women are more likely to have multiple children in MDCs.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Women in MDCs tend to have more education and political empowerment, and thus they are more likely to participate in government.</p>
</div>

## Question 541

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 541</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following did not contribute to suburbanization in the United States in the 1950s and 1960s?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Greater availability of mortgage loans</li><li>B. The baby boom</li><li>C. Economic growth</li><li>D. Road construction</li><li>E. Urban gentrification</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> Several factors-including more accessible loans, higher fertility rates, economic growth, and road building-enabled large-scale suburbanization in the decades after World War II. Urban gentrification is mainly associated with the period since 1990, when cities that declined during the postwar era started to receive increasing investment and, as a result, property values rose.</p>
</div>

## Question 542

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 542</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Population information from the US Census affects the political process by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. determining the number of electoral votes given to each state.</li><li>B. determining the number of Senate seats given to each state.</li><li>C. determining the number of electoral votes given to each political party.</li><li>D. determining voting district boundaries within states.</li><li>E. determining when each state holds its primary election.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> US Census information is used in many ways. For example, it helps set the amount of funding that goes to different areas on the basis of each area's population and socioeconomic needs. The census also determines the number of electoral votes given to each state in upcoming presidential elections.</p>
</div>

## Question 543

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 543</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Mexico's maquiladoras are examples of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Offshore financial centers</li><li>B. Brick-and-mortar businesses</li><li>C. Ancillary activities</li><li>D. Informal economic activities</li><li>E. Export-processing zones</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> Mexico's maquiladoras are export-processing zones where goods are manufactured and distributed to consumers mostly in the United States and Canada.</p>
</div>

## Question 544

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 544</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0313-01.jpg"/></p><p>The pie charts above most likely represent the labor force by occupation in which of the following pairs of countries?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Mexico; Denmark</li><li>B. Saudi Arabia; South Africa</li><li>C. Cameroon; Denmark</li><li>D. New Zealand; Russia</li><li>E. Chile; Oman</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Cameroon is a less-developed country with a large agricultural labor force, whereas Denmark is a highly developed country with a large service sector.</p>
</div>

## Question 545

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 545</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Rostow's stages-of-economic-development model predicts that each country's economy will progress along which of the following trajectories?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. High consumption to ecological sustainability</li><li>B. Low output to high output</li><li>C. Low income to high income and high mass consumption</li><li>D. Low employment in tertiary activities to high employment in primary activities</li><li>E. Low dependency to high dependency on other economies</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Rostow's model predicts that countries will develop over time, proceeding from low income to high income and high mass consumption. It describes the trajectories of some countries, but the complexity of history and geography require that we consider it only as a general concept and not a predictive model applicable to specific circumstances.</p>
</div>

## Question 546

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 546</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which of the following best defines the term "gerrymandering"?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. An early technique for setting maritime boundaries</li><li>B. The large number of federal regulations controlling pollution by corporations</li><li>C. Redistricting to ensure a majority-minority population within a district</li><li>D. Legal "covenants" prohibiting people of color from residing in certain neighborhoods</li><li>E. Drawing voting district boundaries to favor a political party or candidate</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> Gerrymandering involves drawing voting district boundaries to favor a political party or candidate. The United States Supreme Court generally has upheld the idea that partisan gerrymandering is allowed, to a point, under the Constitution even though computer mapping has increased the ability of parties to draw biased boundaries and doing so has negative consequences for political representation.</p>
</div>

## Question 547

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 547</strong></p>
