<p><b>12.</b> The map suggests which of the following about Los Angeles?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It is organized around a dominant central business district.</li><li>B. It is a primate city.</li><li>C. It is a multinucleated urban region.</li><li>D. It is organized into concentric rings.</li><li>E. It is a new urbanist city.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Los Angeles is a classic multinucleated urban region in that it contains multiple nodes of commerce and government of similar social, political, and financial status. Los Angeles has a large downtown, but its central business district is not nearly as dominant, for example, as Chicago's Loop, which is the center for business and finance in the Midwest.</p>
</div>

## Question 548

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 548</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Based on the map, which of the following best describes Los Angeles?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It is a compact medieval city.</li><li>B. It has no squatter settlements.</li><li>C. It is a rink-sized city.</li><li>D. It contains much suburban sprawl.</li><li>E. Its highest rents are located in the outer ring.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Los Angeles is a vast, mostly low-rise city that contains extensive areas of suburban sprawl. This does not, however, mean that Los Angeles has low population density. Many people are surprised to learn that, according to the US Census, the Los Angeles metropolitan area is the most densely populated in the United States.</p>
</div>

## Question 549

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 549</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Which of the following terms describes national governments that are organized into geographically defined subunits, such as states or provinces?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Federalist</li><li>B. Territorial</li><li>C. Consolidated</li><li>D. Electoral</li><li>E. Republican</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Federalist systems of government are organized hierarchically into geographically defined subunits to which the national government delegates some power.</p>
</div>

## Question 550

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 550</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0314-01.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the following best explains the above map of dominant religions by region in the United States?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Climate determines people's religious affiliations.</li><li>B. Different religions tend to take hold in rural rather than urban areas.</li><li>C. Different US states have different official religions.</li><li>D. Religious affiliation is related to historic patterns of immigration.</li><li>E. Republicans tend to be Protestant, whereas Democrats tend to be Catholic.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> The dominant religious affiliation in any region is usually a product of historic patterns of immigration. In the US Intermountain West, for example, the arrival of Mormons during the 19th century still profoundly shapes religious institutions and beliefs in the region.</p>
</div>

## Question 551

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 551</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Canada is an example of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A primate state</li><li>B. A multinational state</li><li>C. A prorupted state</li><li>D. A centrifugal state</li><li>E. A supranational state</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Canada is a multinational state because the province of Quebec contains a distinct history, language, and identity and has a long-established separatist movement.</p>
</div>

## Question 552

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 552</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0314-02.jpg"/></p><p>The sector model of urban geography above best fits which American city?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. New York</li><li>B. San Francisco</li><li>C. Chicago</li><li>D. Honolulu</li><li>E. Miami Beach</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Chicago is a distinctive American city that has both concentric rings of increasingly recent development as one moves outward from the center and rail lines that act as spokes extending into these newer communities.</p>
</div>

## Question 553

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 553</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0315-01.jpg"/></p><p>In the aerial photograph above, the grid of rural north
						<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The original surveyors must have made an error in laying out the roads.</li><li>B. Due to the curvature of the earth, north</li><li>C. Frontier geographies often contain such unusual local features.</li><li>D. These grid corrections are an example of relative-versus-absolute distance.</li><li>E. These grid corrections are an example of space-time convergence.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Due to the curvature of the earth, north-south lines converge as they near the poles. This means that in regions with rectangular grid layouts and infrastructure, occasional "corrections" must be built into the grid.</p>
</p></div>

## Question 554

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 554</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0315-02.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the following is correct regarding the above distance decay function?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The friction of distance has little effect on connectivity.</li><li>B. Connectivity is related to the position of a central place.</li><li>C. Distance imposes a significant barrier to spatial interactions.</li><li>D. Relative distance acts independently of absolute distance.</li><li>E. Absolute decay and relative decay are different.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> This distance decay function suggests that distance poses a significant barrier to spatial interactions. The intensity of this barrier can vary due to many factors, such as infrastructure, migration history, and digital connectivity.</p>
</div>

## Question 555

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 555</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Edge cities, such as Camarillo, California (pictured above), which is located about 50 miles east of Los Angeles, have which of the following qualities?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Low taxes</li><li>B. Export-processing zones</li><li>C. Commuter rail</li><li>D. Sprawling suburbs with varied amenities</li><li>E. Light traffic and clean air</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Edge cities, such as Camarillo, CA, have sprawling suburbs with varied amenities and are often located 25 to 100 miles from a major metropolitan core.</p>
</div>

## Question 556

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 556</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following statements is false regarding edge cities?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The first true edge cities had appeared by the late 19th century.</li><li>B. Edge cities tend to be located near national borders.</li><li>C. Edge cities often have high-quality public transportation systems.</li><li>D. Edge cities serve many of the same functions as traditional cities, but many lack downtown cores.</li><li>E. Edge cities are often considered examples of sustainable urban design.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Edge cities began to appear in the 1980s, not in the late 19th century.</p>
</div>

## Question 557

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 557</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0316-02.jpg"/></p><p>Opened in 1915, San Francisco's City Hall, pictured above, combines classical forms with modern industrial features. It is an example of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Beaux Arts architecture</li><li>B. Gentrification</li><li>C. Postmodern architecture</li><li>D. Node planning</li><li>E. Urban revitalization</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> San Francisco City Hall is a classic example of Beaux Arts architecture, which marries older, classical forms with newer, industrial ones. Beaux Arts planners designed wide thoroughfares, spacious parks, and civic monuments that stressed progress, freedom, and national unity.</p>
</div>

## Question 558

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 558</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> The area of the Middle East that extends from Egypt through Israel, Lebanon, Syria, and Iraq is known as which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The demilitarized zone</li><li>B. The green triangle</li><li>C. The Sahara Desert</li><li>D. Judea and Samaria</li><li>E. The Fertile Crescent</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> The Fertile Crescent, which spanned the Middle East from Egypt to Iraq, was one of the world's earliest centers of sedentary farming.</p>
</div>

## Question 559

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 559</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which of the following is incorrect of political boundaries?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They establish the limits of sovereignty.</li><li>B. They often indicate cultural, national, or economic divisions.</li><li>C. In the ocean, they are defined by rules established through the United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea.</li><li>D. They are rarely contested.</li><li>E. They usually contain well-defined nation-states.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> National boundaries are frequently contested due to their complex histories and geographies.</p>
</div>

## Question 560

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 560</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0317-01.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the following statements probably best explains the data displayed in the map above?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Children who speak languages other than English at home are randomly distributed throughout the United States.</li><li>B. Children who speak languages other than English at home live mostly in rural areas.</li><li>C. States with smaller populations tend to have a greater proportion of children who speak languages other than English at home.</li><li>D. Most children speak languages other than English at home.</li><li>E. Children who speak languages other than English at home tend to live in states with large Latino populations.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> Children who speak languages other than English at home tend to live in states with large Latino populations, as Spanish is the most frequently spoken language other than English in homes across this country.</p>
</div>

## Question 561

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 561</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0317-02.jpg"/></p><p>The above map shows the world's most heavily trafficked international migration routes. Based on the data displayed in it, which of the following statements is probably true?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Migrants almost always move from south to north.</li><li>B. Migrants usually end up in conflict zones.</li><li>C. Most cross-border migrants travel from less-developed to more-developed countries.</li><li>D. Most migrants pass easily through international borders.</li><li>E. Most migrants end up back in their place of origin.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> The map above shows that most cross-border migrants travel from less-developed to more-developed countries, as push factors drive them from their homes and pull factors attract them to places with greater security, opportunities, and quality of life.</p>
</div>

## Question 562

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 562</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Which of the following statements best describes the pattern in the above map showing the average ages of people by country?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Wealthier countries tend to have younger populations.</li><li>B. Wealthier countries tend to have older populations.</li><li>C. Poorer countries tend to have larger populations.</li><li>D. Landlocked countries tend to have older populations.</li><li>E. People living in protracted countries tend to live protracted lives.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Wealthier countries in Europe, North America, and parts of East Asia, which have low death and fertility rates, tend to have older populations.</p>
</div>

## Question 563

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 563</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Countries with large proportions of young people tend to be located</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. in landlocked areas.</li><li>B. in the Arctic.</li><li>C. in fertile agricultural regions.</li><li>D. in developing regions of Africa, Asia, and Latin America.</li><li>E. in the metropolitan core.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Countries with large proportions of young people tend to be located in the fast-growing developing regions of Africa, Asia, and Latin America.</p>
</div>

## Question 564

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 564</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Which of the following is the best predictor of the birth rate in a given country?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Gross Domestic Product</li><li>B. Demographic transition models</li><li>C. Pro-natalist policies</li><li>D. Immigration policies</li><li>E. Women's level of health, education, and empowerment</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> Women's level of health, education, and empowerment is the best predictor of the birth rate in a country. As women gain more of all three, they tend to pursue careers, have children later in life, and have fewer of them.</p>
</div>

## Question 565

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 565</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> The two maps above show the world's top 20 megacities, by population, in 2010 and then projected forward to 2100. Which of the following conclusions best describes the trends shown in these maps?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The world's largest megacities are becoming more geographically dispersed over time.</li><li>B. The world's largest megacities are becoming concentrated in developing countries.</li><li>C. Immigration from less-developed countries is fueling the growth of megacities in more-developed countries, causing them to surge ahead in population.</li><li>D. Growth of megacities in the 21st century is mainly a function of climate and distance to markets.</li><li>E. Due to their size, megacities tend to be stable over time.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Over the 21st century, the world's largest megacities are projected to become more concentrated in rapidly growing developing countries.</p>
</div>

## Question 566

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 566</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following statements will, according to projections, be true by 2100?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. There will be no more megacities in North or South America.</li><li>B. The biggest cities in North and South America will all have declined in population.</li><li>C. Millions of former residents of northern megacities like New York and Tokyo will have relocated to southern megacities like Lagos and Manila.</li><li>D. Africa and South Asia will contain almost all of the world's megacities.</li><li>E. The megacities of Africa and South Asia will probably have developed similar patterns and appearances as big cities</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> By 2100, Africa and South Asia are predicted to have almost all of the world's biggest megacities. Megacities will still exist elsewhere, but they will be eclipsed in population by these booming urban regions containing tens of millions of people.</p>
</div>

## Question 567

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 567</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> The emerging megacities in Africa and Asia face many challenges. Which of the following are not among these?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Building and maintaining adequate infrastructure</li><li>B. Fighting crime</li><li>C. Providing a clean and healthy environment</li><li>D. Controlling the cost of living</li><li>E. Protecting their populations from invading armies</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(E)</b> Although many megacities in Africa and Asia have high rates of violent crime, they are in no danger of being invaded by outside forces.</p>
</div>

## Question 568

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 568</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0319-01.jpg"/></p><p>The two maps above depict population density at two geographic scales: the whole United States and the state of California. Based on this information, which of the following statements is incorrect?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The scale of a map can fundamentally alter the information and insights it conveys.</li><li>B. The population of California is distributed highly unevenly, with large numbers of people living in relatively small areas.</li><li>C. The states with the greatest population densities tend to contain large cities.</li><li>D. As the state with the largest population, most of California's land area is urbanized.</li><li>E. Maps that include larger areas tend to display fewer details.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> California is the US state with the largest population, having surpassed New York in 1962. Yet, California's population is concentrated in a few densely populated major metropolitan areas, with vast, thinly populated expanses in between. In addition to its human population, California also has the country's biggest agricultural economy and more area in protected nature reserves than any state except Alaska.</p>
</div>

## Question 569

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 569</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0320-01.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the following statements best explains the above figure showing manufacturing output and employment since 1947?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Manufacturing employment generally has kept pace with output since World War II.</li><li>B. Increases in efficiency have enabled output to continue growing since the 1970s, even as employment has declined.</li><li>C. Employment has undergone gradual changes, while output has been more volatile.</li><li>D. Since highly skilled manufacturing jobs cost firms relatively little, employment tends to remain consistent or grow over time.</li><li>E. Deindustrialization has led to declines in both output and employment since the 1970s.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Increases in efficiency, including investments in technologies such as factory robots, have enabled output to continue growing since the 1970s even as employment has declined. Deindustrialization in the United States is thus more a story of a loss of jobs than it is a loss of industries or total productivity.</p>
</div>

## Question 570

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 570</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> In the United States, national political debates about federalism focus on topics like the environment and health care and often raise which of the following issues?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. National sovereignty</li><li>B. Self-determination</li><li>C. States' rights</li><li>D. The heartland theory</li><li>E. Buffer states</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(C)</b> Federalism debates often raise the question of states' rights. Under the US Constitution, federal laws passed by Congress supersede those passed by the states. The federal government's authority to legislate is limited, however, to specific "enumerated" areas, whereas the states, which have a "general police power," may pass laws pertaining to almost any issue or topic.</p>
</div>

## Question 571

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 571</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> <img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/br/f0320-02.jpg"/></p><p>Which of the following terms best describes the boundary separating Papua New Guinea and Indonesia on the island of New Guinea, as pictured above?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Antecedent boundary</li><li>B. Fictitious boundary</li><li>C. Prorupted boundary</li><li>D. Superimposed boundary</li><li>E. Demilitarized boundary</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> A superimposed boundary is one that does not reflect the complex social, cultural, or ecological landscape. It often comes in the form of a linear or other geometric boundary.</p>
</div>

## Question 572

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 572</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> The map above shows the 50 largest metropolitan statistical areas in the United States by population. Which of the following best defines these areas?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. An area containing several smaller urban areas that act together as a whole</li><li>B. A geographical center of activity within a larger urban region</li><li>C. A leading city, often with a population disproportionately larger than other urban areas in the same country</li><li>D. A global center of culture, government, or finance</li><li>E. A city placed in a remote area to draw population for economic or symbolic reasons</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> A metropolitan statistical area is a US Census Bureau designation that pertains to a region containing several smaller urban areas that act together as a whole.</p>
</div>

## Question 573

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 573</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Based on the above map, which of the following is correct regarding the 50 largest US metropolitan statistical areas?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They are mostly located in the West.</li><li>B. They appear to be randomly distributed.</li><li>C. They have similar land-area sizes and shapes.</li><li>D. Most are located east of the Mississippi River.</li><li>E. Every state has one.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Most of the 50 largest metropolitan statistical areas are located east of the Mississippi River, but some of the biggest-such as those centered on Houston, Dallas-Ft. Worth, Phoenix, San Francisco, and Los Angeles-are located west of the Mississippi.</p>
</div>

## Question 574

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 574</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which of the following terms refers to "the fair treatment and meaningful involvement of all people regardless of race, color, national origin, or income with respect to the development, implementation, and enforcement of environmental laws, regulations, and policies"?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Self-determination</li><li>B. Environmental justice</li><li>C. Acculturation</li><li>D. Relative distance</li><li>E. A sense of place</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(B)</b> Environmental justice is "the fair treatment and meaningful involvement of all people regardless of race, color, national origin, or income with respect to the development, implementation, and enforcement of environmental laws, regulations, and policies."</p>
</div>

## Question 575

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 575</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Thomas Malthus introduced which of the following arguments?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Fertilizers and new technologies could greatly increase crop output.</li><li>B. The best way to feed a growing population is to conserve resources.</li><li>C. Americans waste more than 30 percent of the food they produce.</li><li>D. Population growth will outstrip food production, leading to "negative checks."</li><li>E. Geography is an interdisciplinary field that draws from four distinct traditions.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> Malthus argued that population growth, which increases geometrically, will outstrip food production, which increases only linearly, leading to famine, war, and other "negative checks" on the human population. He is believed to have underestimated the potential of technology to produce more food and the role of distribution systems, markets, and democratic decision-making to supply the food needs of diverse people.</p>
</div>

## Question 576

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 576</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which of the following describes a cultural tradition's center and place of origin?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Cultural center</li><li>B. Cultural complex</li><li>C. Cultural trait</li><li>D. Cultural hearth</li><li>E. Cultural genesis</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> A cultural hearth is the place where a cultural tradition begins and from which it emanates outward.</p>
</div>

## Question 577

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 577</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> The Italian language varies significantly between Milan, Rome, Naples, and Palermo. Which of the following terms is used to describe these diverse ways of speaking and writing?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Pidgins</li><li>B. Lingua franca</li><li>C. Language groups</li><li>D. Dialects</li><li>E. Idioms</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(D)</b> A dialect is a local variation of a more widespread language.</p>
</div>

## Question 578

</ul>

</div>

## Question 579

<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Detroit, MI (a)</li><li>B. Naples, FL (b)</li><li>C. Honolulu, HI (c)</li><li>D. United States (d)</li><li>E. Dependency ratios cannot be determined using population pyramids.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>(A)</b> Detroit, MI, has the largest proportion of young people and therefore the highest birth rate.</p>

## Question 580

</ul>

<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>

## Question 581

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 581</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Since 1945, which of the following U.S. regions has seen the most population growth?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The Yellow Belt</li><li>B. The Rust Belt</li><li>C. The Shelterbelt</li><li>D. The Sunbelt</li><li>E. The Bible Belt</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>Since 1945, large numbers of people have moved to or been born in Sunbelt states from the Deep South to the Pacific Coast. Many of these newcomers previously had lived in industrial regions of the Northeast and Midwest.</p>
</div>

## Question 582

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 582</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Swidden agriculture can be sustainable if</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. people stop doing it</li><li>B. fertilizer is used</li><li>C. fields are given substantial fallow time</li><li>D. fields are tilled with mechanical machinery</li><li>E. it is outlawed</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>When fields are given sufficient fallow time, their soils are able to recover, creating nutrient-rich soils and protecting biological diversity.</p>
</div>

## Question 583

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 583</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The English language varies in its vocabulary, spelling, and pronunciation among speakers in Atlanta, Sydney, London, and Mumbai. This is an example of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Dialects</li><li>B. Local idioms</li><li>C. Accents</li><li>D. Lingua francas</li><li>E. Grammatical inconsistencies</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>A dialect is a form of a language often associated with a particular region.</p>
</div>

## Question 584

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 584</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> ____ was a hearth of domesticated agriculture.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The Horn of Africa</li><li>B. The Southern Cone</li><li>C. The Bermuda Triangle</li><li>D. The Fertile Crescent</li><li>E. The Straits of Gibraltar</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>The Fertile Crescent region, which once spanned from the Nile River Valley of Egypt east to Syria and Iran, was one of the hearths of sedentary, domesticated agriculture.</p>
</div>

## Question 585

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 585</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Population pyramids that are slightly wider at the top than at the bottom are found mostly in which regions of the world?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Idiographic regions</li><li>B. Developing regions</li><li>C. Post-colonial regions</li><li>D. Highly developed regions</li><li>E. Peripheral regions</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>Since highly developed regions tend to have slow or no population growth, or even negative growth, these regions would have population pyramids that are slightly wider at the top, with greater proportions of elderly people than in faster-growing regions.</p>
</div>

## Question 586

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 586</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following best describes transhumance?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Seasonal movement in pastoral societies</li><li>B. Shifting cultivation</li><li>C. Relocation diffusion</li><li>D. Population intercession</li><li>E. The emergence of local religions in developing countries</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Transhumance refers to the movement of livestock from summer to winter ranges, in cultures where pastoralists are able to take advantage of seasonal changes in the availability of forage.</p>
</div>

## Question 587

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 587</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Why did Pakistan relocate its capital of Karachi to Islamabad in the 1960s?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. To be closer to the coast to facilitate international trade</li><li>B. To encourage growth in the country's interior</li><li>C. The United Nations mandated it, as Karachi was too violent</li><li>D. Karachi was too close to the border of Afghanistan</li><li>E. Karachi was politically divided, and the government wanted more unity in its capital city</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>Some countries, like Pakistan and Brazil, have chosen to move their capitals from populated coastal to more remote interior locations to encourage growth in what their leaders have seen as underdeveloped regions.</p>
</div>

## Question 588

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 588</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Which of the following is a global religion?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Eastern Orthodoxy</li><li>B. Hinduism</li><li>C. Shamanism</li><li>D. Islam</li><li>E. Judaism</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>With an estimated 1.8 billion adherents in dozens of countries, Islam is one of the world's global religions.</p>
</div>

## Question 589

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 589</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which of the following is the BEST example of a tertiary economic activity?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Orange picking</li><li>B. Automobile manufacturing</li><li>C. Smartphone assembling</li><li>D. Dog grooming</li><li>E. Cattle ranching</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>Tertiary economic activities involve the exchange of goods produced in secondary activities. Retailing, restaurants, and any other basic service job猯ike dog grooming—occupy the tertiary sector of the economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 590

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 590</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Thomas Malthus believed that</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. population would level out at about 12 billion people</li><li>B. wars and famines were a good thing</li><li>C. history repeats itself</li><li>D. industrialization would raise the world's human carrying capacity</li><li>E. population growth would outpace food supply</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: E</b></p><p>Malthus believed that population growth would outpace food supply, because he thought that population grew geometrically, whereas food supply grew only arithmetically.</p>
</div>

## Question 591

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 591</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Afghanistan, Nigeria, and Somalia are similar in that all three countries have</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. high net national products</li><li>B. high immigration rates</li><li>C. high fertility rates</li><li>D. high human development indexes</li><li>E. low net national happiness</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>Afghanistan, Nigeria, and Somalia are all developing countries with high fertility rates.</p>
</div>

## Question 592

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 592</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> With its system of regional <i>estados</i>, or states, Mexico is an example of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A microstate</li><li>B. An electoral state</li><li>C. A reapportioned state</li><li>D. A federal state</li><li>E. A nation-state</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>Mexico's decentralized power structure makes it a federal state.</p>
</div>

## Question 593

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 593</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> When considered as a whole, this organization rivals the United States both in GDP and in number of exports and imports.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The United Arab Emirates</li><li>B. The Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries</li><li>C. The former Soviet Union</li><li>D. The African National Congress</li><li>E. The European Union</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: E</b></p><p>The European Union is an economic powerhouse, rivaling the United States in the scale and diversity of its economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 594

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 594</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Which of the following is the BEST example of a footloose industry?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Steel mills</li><li>B. Truck farming</li><li>C. Jewelry-making</li><li>D. Indigenous arts and crafts</li><li>E. Coffee growing</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>Jewelry-making is a footloose industry because its valuable, lightweight materials can be processed and assembled anywhere.</p>
</div>

## Question 595

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 595</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Which of the following terms best describes many of Africa's national boundaries, which were drawn and imposed during the colonial era, and now fail to reflect cultural patterns? </p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Superimposed boundaries</li><li>B. Subsequent boundaries</li><li>C. Antecedent boundaries</li><li>D. Territorial boundaries</li><li>E. Geometric boundaries</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Superimposed boundaries are drawn after a population has been settled in an area and do not pay much attention to the social, cultural, and ethnic compositions of the populations they divide.</p>
</div>

## Question 596

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 596</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following best describes the countries of the former Yugoslavia, including Serbia and Montenegro, which split up and formed their own independent states after the end of the Cold War?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Protracted states</li><li>B. Failed states</li><li>C. Unionization</li><li>D. Domino theory</li><li>E. Balkanization</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: E</b></p><p>Balkanization refers to the contentious political process by which a state may break up into smaller countries.</p>
</div>

## Question 597

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 597</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> What can play a key role in shaping local and regional geographies of a developing region's agriculture?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Regional climate</li><li>B. Cost of transportation</li><li>C. Soil fertility</li><li>D. Gentrification</li><li>E. Mechanization</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>In von Thunen's model, rents and transportation costs play key roles in shaping the local         and regional geographies of agriculture. </p>
</div>

## Question 598

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 598</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Many countries in developing regions are experiencing dramatic declines in their fertility rates. What is the main cause for this pattern?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Gender discrimination</li><li>B. Maternal mortality</li><li>C. Improved education, career opportunities, and healthcare for women</li><li>D. Male out-migration</li><li>E. Infectious diseases</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>Improved education, career opportunities, and healthcare for women all contribute to the dramatic decline in fertility rates in many countries in developing regions.</p>
</div>

## Question 599

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 599</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> After the dot-com bubble burst in early 2000, many software firms moved out of the San Francisco Bay Area to locations with cheaper real estate. This movement exemplifies which of the following processes?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Deglomeration</li><li>B. Agglomeration</li><li>C. Deindustrialization</li><li>D. Despeculation</li><li>E. Industrial diffusion</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Deglomeration occurs when firms relocate from an agglomerated region—one with many firms in the same industry—to a new place with fewer such firms.</p>
</div>

## Question 600

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 600</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> John has 300 cattle grazing on 1,500 acres of land he owns in Colorado, and he sells his beef to a local food cooperative. John is engaging in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Extensive commercial agriculture</li><li>B. Truck farming</li><li>C. Swidden agriculture</li><li>D. Feedlot agriculture</li><li>E. Intensive commercial agriculture</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Ranching is an agricultural activity that takes place over large expanses of land and, as such, is a good representative of an extensive commercial agricultural activity. Additionally, it does not require either large amounts of human labor or capital inputs.</p>
</div>

## Question 601

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 601</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following is an example of an ethnic religion?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Pentecostalism</li><li>B. Hinduism</li><li>C. Buddhism</li><li>D. Baha'i</li><li>E. Animism</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>Ethnic religions, such as Hinduism, tend to appeal to smaller groups of people with a common heritage or to large groups of people with some common identity living in a single region. Hinduism is the largest of ethnic religions due mostly to its concentration in India.</p>
</div>

## Question 602

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 602</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> By placing component factories near facilities where finished products are assembled, Japanese firms that adhere to the philosophy of Kaizen are fostering what?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Centralization</li><li>B. Deglomeration</li><li>C. Agglomeration</li><li>D. Break-bulk processing</li><li>E. Reapportionment</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>An agglomeration effect occurs when many companies from the same industry cluster together in a relatively small area to draw from the same set of collective resources.</p>
</div>

## Question 603

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 603</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> The Canadian government has relinquished some powers to First Nations groups in areas such as the Nunavut Territory. Which of the following terms describes this delegation of government powers to a subnational jurisdiction? </p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Devolution</li><li>B. Revolution</li><li>C. Perforation</li><li>D. Proruption</li><li>E. Decolonialization</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Devolution refers to the breakup of a state into its smaller constituents for any reason, including ethnic divisions, varying levels of economic development, external pressure, or other centrifugal forces.</p>
</div>

## Question 604

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 604</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> The introduction of hybrid seeds to developing regions during the Green Revolution led to food security issues in some areas, and decreases in crop species diversity. This is an example of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Biogeographic diffusion</li><li>B. Contagious diffusion</li><li>C. Maladaptive diffusion</li><li>D. Expansion diffusion</li><li>E. Decomplementarity</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>Maladaptive diffusion occurs when ideas, practices, or technologies create novel problems in the new areas where they arrive.</p>
</div>

## Question 605

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 605</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> In which of the following world regions are you MOST likely to find polytheistic religions?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Scandinavia</li><li>B. The Middle East</li><li>C. Eastern Europe</li><li>D. Sub-Saharan Africa</li><li>E. Central Asia</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>Diverse local and ethnic polytheistic religions are common in Sub-Saharan Africa.</p>
</div>

## Question 606

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 606</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> According to which model of economic development do countries with free market economies follow a set of predetermined steps on the way to becoming fully industrialized and diversified?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Core-Periphery Model</li><li>B. Rostow's Stages of Development</li><li>C. World Systems Theory</li><li>D. Marxism</li><li>E. Heartland Theory</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>Rostow's Stages of Development imagines countries as proceeding through a common, preordained set of stages.</p>
</div>

## Question 607

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 607</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> This acronym describes the cartel founded in the 1960s by some of the world's major oil producing nations to control production and price of oil. </p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. IAEA</li><li>B. NARWHAL</li><li>C. OPEC</li><li>D. NATO</li><li>E. EU</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>OPEC stands for the Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries.</p>
</div>

## Question 608

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 608</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Some U.S. citizens strongly oppose any programs or legislation that encourages bilingualism, even though the number of Spanish speakers continues to decrease. Which of the following terms could describe this resistance?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Ethnocentrism</li><li>B. Gross national product</li><li>C. Fundamentalism</li><li>D. Caste system</li><li>E. Ecunume</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Ethnocentrism is the belief that other cultures should be evaluated based on the standards of one's own culture. It often manifests in a feeling of cultural superiority or a desire to exclude or marginalize people from different cultures.</p>
</div>

## Question 609

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 609</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Which of the following statements applies to the Basques of France and Spain and the Kurds of the Middle East?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They speak pidgin languages.</li><li>B. They seek political autonomy.</li><li>C. They live in ghettos.</li><li>D. They face language extinction.</li><li>E. They fight against transculturation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>The Basques of France and Spain and the Kurds of the Middle East both seek increased political autonomy.</p>
</div>

## Question 610

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 610</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Which of the following terms may describe situations in which the construction of hazardous waste storage and treatment facilities occurs disproportionately in areas with minority populations of low socioeconomic status?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Sectorization</li><li>B. Prejudice</li><li>C. Ghettoization</li><li>D. Environmental injustice</li><li>E. Segregation</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>Environmental injustices may occur when some groups of people lack the political power to meaningfully participate in decision-making processes that affect their health and environments, or when they lack access to environmental goods, like open space, or are disproportionately exposed to greater environmental risks.</p>
</div>

## Question 611

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 611</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> When Tuan Nguyen migrated from Vietnam to the United States in 1981, he started a restaurant that introduced the local residents near Columbus, Ohio, to Vietnamese food for the first time. Which of the following terms best describes this phenomenon?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Cross-cultural traits</li><li>B. Cultural literacy</li><li>C. Contagious diffusion</li><li>D. Relocation diffusion</li><li>E. Cultural complex</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>  Relocation diffusion occurs when people migrate from one place to another, bringing with them cultural traditions from their previous homelands.</p>
</div>

## Question 612

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 612</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> In the Ozark Mountains of southern Missouri and northern Arkansas, you can still find numerous fiddlers that play traditional ballads in local taverns. Which of the following terms best describes this phenomenon? </p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Cultural hearth</li><li>B. Local religion</li><li>C. Polyglot</li><li>D. Cottage industry</li><li>E. Folk culture</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: E</b></p><p>Folk culture refers to a constellation of cultural practices that form the sights, smells, sounds, and rituals of the traditional societies in which they develop.</p>
</div>

## Question 613

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 613</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Agents of the British Empire often forced their colonial subjects to learn English. Which of the following terms best describes this effort?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Self-determination</li><li>B. Cultural imperialism</li><li>C. Rimland Theory</li><li>D. East/West divide</li><li>E. Law of the Sea</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>Cultural imperialism refers to a wide range of processes and projects by which the people from one culture or country seek to dominate those of another culture or country by imposing cultural practices on them.</p>
</div>

## Question 614

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 614</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following trends is becoming popular in separatist movements across the globe as a way of producing cultural cohesion and strength?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Purchasing new isoglosses</li><li>B. Reviving minority languages</li><li>C. Increasing syncretism</li><li>D. Transculturation</li><li>E. Adoption of Esperanto</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>Minority languages are increasingly being revived as ways to assert cultural vitality and independence among minority and separatist groups.</p>
</div>

## Question 615

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 615</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> This world map displays which of the following projections?</p><p><img src="brrn_fix_1.jpg"/></p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Azimuthal</li><li>B. Robinson</li><li>C. Toblerian</li><li>D. Mercator</li><li>E. Indicator</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>The Mercator projection is easily recognizable because it distorts the lines of longitude, making them parallel instead of allowing them to intersect at the poles as they do on a globe.</p>
</div>

## Question 616

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 616</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> All flat maps distort one or more of four projection properties. Which of the following lists correctly identifies these properties?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Distance, area, shape, direction</li><li>B. Distance, compression, elongation, eruption</li><li>C. Length, width, height, depth</li><li>D. Curvature, linearity, acuteness, directness</li><li>E. Ellipticity, tilt, obliquity, angularity</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>All flat maps distort distance, area, shape, direction, or some combination of these four. </p>
</div>

## Question 617

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 617</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Which of the following is correct regarding the map?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It distorts direction.</li><li>B. It distorts elongation.</li><li>C. It distorts curvature.</li><li>D. It distorts area.</li><li>E. It lacks distortions.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>By forcing the lines of longitude to remain parallel, the Mercator projection distorts area, making seas and landmasses at high latitudes appear much larger, proportionally, than they actually are.</p>
</div>

## Question 618

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 618</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Maps like this one often are criticized for which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Making landmasses in the middle and higher latitudes, including those in North America and Europe, look bigger than those in the lower latitudes</li><li>B. Making landmasses in the lower latitudes, including those in Africa and much of Latin America, look bigger than those in the middle and higher latitudes</li><li>C. Making Greenland look smaller than it actually is</li><li>D. Making Brazil look bigger than it actually is</li><li>E. Requiring too much space to print</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Because the Mercator projection makes landmasses in the temperate and polar regions of the Northern Hemisphere appear so large, it is often criticized for portraying a Eurocentric view of the world.</p>
</div>

## Question 619

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 619</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> In the map of South America, which of the following is an "elongated" state?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Argentina</li><li>B. Colombia</li><li>C. Suriname</li><li>D. Uruguay</li><li>E. Chile</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: E</b></p><p>At more than 2,600 miles long and just over 200 miles wide, Chile is a classic elongated state.</p>
</div>

## Question 620

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 620</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> In the map of South America, which of the following is a "compact" state?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Argentina</li><li>B. Colombia</li><li>C. Suriname</li><li>D. Uruguay</li><li>E. Chile</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: D</b></p><p>With a circular or square shape, Uruguay has a short perimeter for its area, making it compact.</p>
</div>

## Question 621

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 621</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Elongated versus compact shapes present different opportunities and challenges for various countries. Which of the following may be a challenge for elongated states?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Their relatively long edges, compared to their areas, mean that they have longer borders to manage.</li><li>B. Their relatively short edges, compared to their areas, mean that they have shorter borders to manage.</li><li>C. They often have weak central governments.</li><li>D. They often lack access to coastlines with navigable waters.</li><li>E. They often have strong separatist movements.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: A</b></p><p>Their relatively long edges, compared to their areas, mean that they have longer borders to manage.</p>
</div>

## Question 622

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 622</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Elongated versus compact shapes present different opportunities and challenges for various countries. Which of the following may be an advantage for compact states?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Their relatively long edges, compared to their areas, mean that they have longer borders to manage.</li><li>B. Their relatively short edges, compared to their areas, mean that they have shorter borders to manage.</li><li>C. They often have weak central governments.</li><li>D. They often lack access to coastlines with navigable waters.</li><li>E. They often have strong separatist movements.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>Their relatively short edges, compared to their areas, mean that they have shorter borders to manage.</p>
</div>

## Question 628

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 628</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following is a potential negative consequence of irrigating crops in arid regions?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Domestication</li><li>B. Mechanization</li><li>C. Salinization</li><li>D. Saltation</li><li>E. Transhumance</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>Salinization occurs when water evaporates from irrigated fields, leaving behind a salty residue that can diminish the productivity of the soil.</p>
</div>

## Question 630

<p><b>Answer: C</b></p><p>Islam spread first by expansion diffusion, then later by relocation diffusion as adherentsmoved to new regions, bringing their beliefs and practices withthem.</p>

## Question 635

<ul class="qlist">

</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><b>Answer: B</b></p><p>Barring other processes or events, such as severe effects from climate change, population geographers believe that demographic transitions in developing countries will cause global population to level off by 2150.</p>

## Question 641

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 641</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> The existence of "Dutch Village" in Holland, Michigan, "Jaarsma (Dutch) Bakery" in Pella, Iowa, and "Dutch Roots Farm" in Ripon, California are all a result of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. forced migration</li><li>B. religious conversions</li><li>C. relocation diffusion</li><li>D. colonial-era labor migrations</li><li>E. rural-to-urban migrations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Relocation diffusion occurs when a cultural group brings a particular trait to a new area and diffuses it to that local community. Dutch communities throughout the U.S. (that resulted from chain migration) brought with them certain Dutch traits such as tulips at the farm in Ripon and speculaas cookies at the bakery in Iowa.</p>
</div>

## Question 642

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 642</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> How would the pattern depicted on the map likely change, if the map showed national scale population density as opposed to density at the state level?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Typically as the scale of analysis increases in area, the level of detail decreases.</li><li>B. Typically as the scale of analysis increases in area, the level of detail also increases.</li><li>C. Typically level of detail only varies between local and global maps (not local vs. national).</li><li>D. The pattern on the map does not typically change with variation in the scale of analysis.</li><li>E. The pattern on the map only changes with a different projection choice.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>The "scale of analysis" describes the unit at which a phenomenon can be investigated or analyzed. The smaller that unit (e.g., a state as opposed to a country), the greater the detail on the map (e.g., states depict different patterns within a country).</p>
</div>

## Question 643

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 643</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The map of population density within Illinois is an example of which type of thematic map?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A cartogram</li><li>B. An image map</li><li>C. A proportional symbols map</li><li>D. An isoline map</li><li>E. A choropleth map</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>Choropleth maps are a common strategy for displaying thematic data by visually showing variation in a particular quantity by shading or coloring different regions.</p>
</div>

## Question 644

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 644</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Hong Kong is 22°17' north and 114°09' east. This is an expression of Hong Kong's</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. relative location</li><li>B. absolute location</li><li>C. relative direction</li><li>D. absolute direction</li><li>E. relative distance</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Coordinates of latitude and longitude express absolute location, which identifies a place's location precisely and universally.</p>
</div>

## Question 645

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 645</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> While no longer in effect, China's one-child policy has led to which of the following demographic challenges?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Large-scale emigration to economically advanced countries</li><li>B. Mass rural-to-urban migration</li><li>C. Smaller total population in China</li><li>D. Immigration from less-developed countries to fulfill lower-level industrial jobs</li><li>E. An imbalance between males and females of marrying age</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>China's traditionally patriarchal society favors males over females, which, combined with the one-child policy and the availability of sonograms, led to a much larger proportion of male births while the policy was in effect. This, in turn, has led to a huge current discrepancy between males and females of marrying age.</p>
</div>

## Question 646

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 646</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> When corporations choose to locate factories in less-developed countries (LDCs), they are typically seeking</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a highly skilled workforce</li><li>B. increased governmental regulation on industry</li><li>C. least-cost industrial locations</li><li>D. proximity to raw materials</li><li>E. proximity to major transportation nodes</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Less-developed countries offer much cheaper labor and more relaxed regulations, which makes them highly attractive to large corporations seeking to cut productions costs.</p>
</div>

## Question 647

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 647</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> The number of smaller, family-owned farms in North America have increased in recent decades largely as a result of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. an increase in consumption of organic/locally produced food items</li><li>B. an increase in the costs of fuel, which presents prohibitive challenges to large-scale farming</li><li>C. an increase in the export of crops to less-developed countries (LDCs)</li><li>D. a large-scale switch to production of staple crops, such as corn and rice</li><li>E. a decrease in the amount of subsidies provided by the government to support agricultural production</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>In recent decades, many Americans have become more concerned about the quality and health of their food. This concern has led to an increase in demand for locally produced, organic farm products, which has led to greater opportunities for smaller farms that produce a wider variety of sustainably raised goods.</p>
</div>

## Question 648

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 648</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> In the former Yugoslavia, the forced expulsion and killing of specific cultural groups during the 1990s is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. insurgency</li><li>B. devolution</li><li>C. chain migration</li><li>D. ethnic cleansing</li><li>E. Balkanization</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>During the 1990s, minority groups in the former Yugoslavia were forced out of their communities, often at gunpoint.  Resistance typically led to being killed. Ethnic cleansing describes the mass killing of a particular ethnic or cultural group.</p>
</div>

## Question 649

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 649</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Newly industrialized countries (NICs) typically exhibit which of the following population characteristics?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Slow population growth with little migration between rural and urban areas</li><li>B. Zero population growth with little rural-to-urban migration</li><li>C. High population growth with rapid rural-to-urban migration</li><li>D. High population growth with little rural-to-urban growth</li><li>E. Stable population growth with a high percentage of the population residing in urban areas</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>In newly industrializing economies, countries are typically transitioning from stage 2 to stage 3 in the demographic transition model. A large (but decreasing) gap between birth and death rates indicates a rapidly growing population.  And, with industry concentrating in urban areas, industrializing economies see a rapid internal shift in population from rural to urban areas.</p>
</div>

## Question 650

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 650</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> New York City and Chicago are roughly 800 miles apart in terms of absolute distance but are actually quite connected in terms of economics and culture. Which of the following is the best explanation for this connection?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The cities have similar transportation and communications infrastructure, which facilitates interaction.</li><li>B. Both cities have diverse populations, which leads to similar cultural experiences.</li><li>C. Both cities have high populations, which counteract distance in the gravity model.</li><li>D. Both cities have similar economic bases, which leads to higher trade between the two.</li><li>E. Both cities have sizable airports that allow for frequent arrivals/departures, facilitating travel between the two cities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>The Gravity Model predicts interaction between two places on the basis of the size of their population and the distance between them. Large populations (in the numerator) lessen the friction of distance between the two locations.</p>
</div>

## Question 651

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 651</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> What is most responsible for hierarchical diffusion, as opposed to contagious diffusion?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Distance-decay effects</li><li>B. Special network links between major nodes</li><li>C. Some people needing multiple contacts before they adopt an innovation</li><li>D. Proximity of the innovation to the varying degrees of diffusion</li><li>E. Relevance of particular innovations to only specific locations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Hierarchical diffusion describes the spread of an innovation through specific nodes, which are not usually located close together in space, but exhibit strong links to one another in a network. For example, fashion trends tend to diffuse hierarchically between major fashion nodes (e.g., Paris, London, Milan) before spreading contagiously to surrounding areas.</p>
</div>

## Question 652

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 652</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Individuals, after experience with a place, form subjective images based on their perceptions of that place. This image is referred to as a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. thematic map</li><li>B. reference map</li><li>C. mental map</li><li>D. contour map</li><li>E. topographic map</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Mental maps are highly individualized personal images about a place, which are composed of subjective perceptions, memories, biases, and feelings. These perceptions and feelings can result from direct experience or from knowledge gained indirectly from various media outlets.</p>
</div>

## Question 653

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 653</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> What is the most likely explanation for why this map separates Catalonia from Spain's other provinces?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Catalonia is part of France, not part of Spain.</li><li>B. Catalonia is seeking independence from Spain, given its distinct cultural identity.</li><li>C. Catalonia is a microstate with internationally recognized sovereignty over its people.</li><li>D. Most Catalans are of Portuguese descent.</li><li>E. Most Catalans are of Arab descent.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>The Catalans, who are currently under Spanish sovereignty, have sought political independence from the Spanish for over a century.</p>
</div>

## Question 654

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 654</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Catalonia's separation from the rest of Spain represents which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A centrifugal force</li><li>B. A centripetal force</li><li>C. An ethnic enclave</li><li>D. Irredentism</li><li>E. Gerrymandering</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Centrifugal forces are those that work toward separating a populace; devolutionary forces, such as those present in Spain, work to divide Spain's population.</p>
</div>

## Question 655

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 655</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Which of the following best describes a "pull factor" that would cause rural family living in a least- developed country to leave their farm and migrate away from their home community?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Civil war or armed conflict in the rural countryside</li><li>B. Job opportunities in manufacturing in the country's urban area</li><li>C. Drought in the rural countryside</li><li>D. Lack of educational opportunity in the home community</li><li>E. Lack of healthcare in the home community</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Pull factors are just as they sound: they pull an individual or family toward a destination. This is in contrast to push factors, which compel people to leave their home or community. Job opportunities (Option B) attract people to a destination, while all of the other options are factors related to rural, agricultural life that might push an individual or family away from that community.</p>
</div>

## Question 656

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 656</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> As the economies of industrialized countries continue to advance, agricultural production within these countries tends to follow which of the following patterns?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Farms are getting larger and are increasingly owned by just one entity (family or corporation).</li><li>B. Farms are getting larger and are increasingly government owned.</li><li>C. Farms are getting smaller and increasing the diversity of crops they produce.</li><li>D. Farms are getting smaller and are increasingly owned by farming cooperatives.</li><li>E. Farming is being completely eliminated in favor of importing agricultural goods from abroad.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>As countries become increasingly economically advanced, agricultural production becomes increasingly mechanized. Production, in terms of volume, tends to increase as farms become more efficient through the use of machinery and other technologies. However, while volume increases, the number of farmers decrease as corporate entities take over farming, or as families expand their operations.</p>
</div>

## Question 657

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 657</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> The free movement of people and the elimination of customs inspections for automotive transportation and trains between EU member nations are a result of which of the following?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The removal of tariffs</li><li>B. The development of the Euro</li><li>C. Heartland Theory</li><li>D. Rimland Theory</li><li>E. Open border policies</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>Open border policies among EU member nations have allowed for much freer movement of goods and people across European countries. These open border policies ease trade and tourism, thereby strengthening the EU economic system as a whole.</p>
</div>

## Question 658

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 658</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> When farms transition to large-scale, export-oriented agriculture, farm production typically transitions to</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. specialization in one commodity</li><li>B. specialization in a variety of seasonally variable foods</li><li>C. organic methods</li><li>D. intensive forms of labor</li><li>E. sustainable forms of pest/weed management</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Large-scale commercial agriculture typically focuses on efficiently growing large volumes of just one type of food or other agricultural product, such as corn, soybeans, or wheat—products that are often, especially in the developing world, produced for export.</p>
</div>

## Question 659

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 659</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> In comparison to other models of urban structure, the sector model</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. incorporates a strong central business district (CBD)</li><li>B. suggests a concentric form of differing functions around an industrial core</li><li>C. portrays ethnic neighborhoods and areas of industrial concentration</li><li>D. displays a decentralized version of urban life</li><li>E. relies on an assumption that real estate value decreases with distance from the city center</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Unlike other models of urban form, such as the multiple-nuclei model or concentric zone model, the sector model accounts for variation in the ethnic makeup of neighborhoods; immigrants often live in low-income housing, often along manufacturing or industrial areas.</p>
</div>

## Question 660

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 660</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> The image of the Over-the-Rhine neighborhood in Cincinnati, Ohio exhibits the efforts of many post-industrial cities in America's heartland to increase the livability of an old central business district. This process is referred to as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. suburbanization</li><li>B. gentrification</li><li>C. redlining</li><li>D. smart growth</li><li>E. post-Modernism</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Gentrification involves the revitalization of old industrial office buildings and warehouses into residential, commercial, and office spaces. These spaces often attract younger, urban professionals, and often coincide with revitalization efforts related to recreation and transportation.</p>
</div>

## Question 661

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 661</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following post-industrial cities in the U.S. is likely to exhibit similar gentrification patterns to those that exist in Cincinnati?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Silicon Valley, CA</li><li>B. Pittsburgh, PA</li><li>C. Seaside, FL</li><li>D. Las Vegas, NV</li><li>E. Kalispell, MT</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Industrial/manufacturing cities in the heart of the Midwest, such as Cincinnati, Pittsburgh, and Detroit, among many others, suffered when industry relocated to areas with cheaper labor (initially to the southern United States and then overseas). These abandoned, formerly industrial landscapes are increasingly seeing a revival with buildings restored for commercial and residential purposes.</p>
</div>

## Question 662

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 662</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> This area of Cincinnati is most likely inhabited by which of the following demographic cohorts?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Single, young college graduates</li><li>B. Retired baby boomers</li><li>C. Families with school-aged kids</li><li>D. Low-income families</li><li>E. High-income families</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Gentrified landscapes such as Over-the-Rhine attract younger, urban, often single professionals. The housing is such that it does not typically support larger families and requires a stable, significant income. In fact, one of the arguments against gentrification is that is displaces low-income, often minority populations that previously lived in those areas.</p>
</div>

## Question 663

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 663</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Which of the following events counts for change in crop yields for the specified countries on the map?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The Industrial Revolution</li><li>B. The Green Revolution</li><li>C. Seed domestication</li><li>D. The organic movement</li><li>E. The von Thunen model</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>During the Green Revolution, agricultural methods and technologies, such as genetically modified seeds, pesticides, and herbicides, were essentially exported from the developed world to the developing world in an effort to help those countries increase agricultural yields.</p>
</div>

## Question 664

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 664</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which of the following countries, not depicted on the map, also experienced dramatic crop yield changes because of the event the map illustrates?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Mexico</li><li>B. Canada</li><li>C. New Zealand</li><li>D. Iraq</li><li>E. Columbia</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Mexico's crop yields expanded greatly as a result of agricultural innovations exported from developed countries, like its neighbor to the North, the United States.</p>
</div>

## Question 665

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 665</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> In spite of the risks of nuclear power generation in terms of proper waste disposal and potential nuclear accidents, some environmentalists are in favor of this technology because</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. construction of nuclear power plants is relatively inexpensive</li><li>B. nuclear waste storage solutions are becoming increasingly low risk</li><li>C. nuclear fuel is easy to access</li><li>D. of the lack of carbon emissions in nuclear power generation</li><li>E. nuclear power technology can be easily accessed across the globe</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
