<p>Answer: D</p><p>In spite of the risks associated with nuclear power generation, it does not emit carbon into the atmosphere, making it an appealing energy source for some environmentalists.</p>
</div>

## Question 666

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 666</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Followers of animistic religions</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. believe that features in nature, such as animals, mountains, and trees, have spiritual value</li><li>B. believe in one god</li><li>C. believe in polytheism</li><li>D. do not believe in any sort of devine presence</li><li>E. do not believe in an afterlife</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Animistic religions are based on items in nature holding spiritual value; they are common among Native American cultures and in various parts of sub-Saharan Africa.</p>
</div>

## Question 667

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 667</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> When suburbs grow to the extent that they contain a large array of employment, recreational, and commercial opportunities in addition to residential opportunities, they are termed</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. conurbations</li><li>B. edge cities</li><li>C. exurban areas</li><li>D. metropolitan areas</li><li>E. central cities</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>In the post-industrial era, many cities in the United States have suburbs that have evolved into self-sustaining cities where all of the amenities and opportunities typically offered by the central city can be found.</p>
</div>

## Question 668

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 668</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> When the cultural and political ideas of nationalism serve to unite a country's populace, nationalism can be classified as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a centrifugal force</li><li>B. a centripetal force</li><li>C. a pull factor</li><li>D. a push factor</li><li>E. a devolutionary force</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Centripetal forces are those that serve to unite people in a country, typically under a common identity/sense of pride for their country. Nationalism becomes divisive, a centrifugal force, when a particular subset of a population uses nationalistic ideologies to create dissent, and to motivate separation from the larger governing body.</p>
</div>

## Question 669

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 669</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Agricultural production in North America is difficult to classify as part of the primary economy. Why?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It is primarily controlled by large agribusinesses that encourage large-scale industrial production and investments in research and development.</li><li>B. It no longer happens primarily in a field but rather through high-tech methods such as hydroponics.</li><li>C. Because so little of the labor force is engaged in this economic activity, the category essentially no longer exists for the developed world.</li><li>D. It is still very much a primary economic activity with methods comparable to those evident in the developing world.</li><li>E. North America's soil is no longer suitable for agricultural production.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>North American agricultural production is highly industrialized—that is, largely carried out by machines rather than humans. Further, in an effort to increase agricultural efficiency, firms dedicate significant funding to research and development of different tools (including seeds) and techniques to increase production.</p>
</div>

## Question 670

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 670</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Immediately after independence, many developing countries adopted these types of economic strategies to limit dependence on former colonizers and/or highly developed economies:</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. neo-liberal (free trade) policies that encouraged involvement in the global economy</li><li>B. Bottom-Up initiatives that promoted local sustainable development through microfinance</li><li>C. regional economic alliances that promoted common currencies and easy movement of goods/people among member nations (similar to the EU)</li><li>D. industrial modernization through investments in technology</li><li>E. protectionist strategies that encouraged economic self-sufficiency through import substitution and barriers to international trade</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>After independence, many developing countries sought to free themselves from the problematic economic relationships/dependencies established under colonial regimes. To do this, governments protected local producers and farmers by promoting domestic production of previously imported goods, and by limiting, through various means, international trade.</p>
</div>

## Question 671

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 671</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which of the following models of urban geography is represented by this figure?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Central place theory</li><li>B. Rank-size rule</li><li>C. Von Thunen's concentric ring theory</li><li>D. Sector model of urban development</li><li>E. Multiple-nuclei model of urban development</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>The multiple-nuclei model applies to a city that lacks a strong central core, but instead has numerous nodes of business, cultural, and residential opportunities.</p>
</div>

## Question 672

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 672</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> The multi-nuclei model is often used to describe the spatial form of which of the following American cities?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. New York City</li><li>B. Chicago</li><li>C. St. Louis</li><li>D. Los Angeles</li><li>E. Washington, D.C.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>Los Angeles has a relatively small downtown business district but contains many independent nodes of high land value and vigorous business activity in cities such as Santa Monica, Hollywood, Westwood, and Pasadena.</p>
</div>

## Question 673

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 673</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> How does microcredit overcome some of the challenges related to employment opportunities for women in less-developed countries, particularly in South and Southeast Asia?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Microcredit is a form of feminization of labor seen within the Export Processing Zones in Southeast Asia.</li><li>B. Microcredit is the main avenue for union formation, which works to combat unfair labor conditions in South and Southeast Asia.</li><li>C. With microcredit, women have control over their own businesses and therefore set their own hours, wages, and working conditions.</li><li>D. With microcredit, women are able to pay for childcare while they work factory jobs in the EPZs.</li><li>E. Microcredit has not offered many distinct changes for female employment opportunities in South and Southeast Asia.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Microcredit has proven to be highly successful in parts of South and Southeast Asia as a means to encourage female empowerment and meaningful engagement in the formal economy. With small loans, women become entrepreneurs, helping their communities and families in working environments that they oversee.</p>
</div>

## Question 674

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 674</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> When irrigation is used in arid or semi-arid environments to increase agricultural productivity, the negative environmental ramification often results in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. bromidification</li><li>B. salinization</li><li>C. desertification</li><li>D. alluviation</li><li>E. gentrification</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Excess water from the irrigation process evaporates quickly in these hot environments, leaving a salty residue. This residue seeps into the soil, making it more acidic and less productive; the entire process is called salinization.</p>
</div>

## Question 675

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 675</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> How do patterns of urbanization in Europe differ from those in North America?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. North American cities focus on tourism, while European cities are much more focused on industry.</li><li>B. European cities have a much stronger suburban fringe in comparison to North American cities.</li><li>C. In both regions, urban populations concentrate in urban cores with a decreasing portion of the population living in suburbs.</li><li>D. In European cities, housing is much denser with only a small percentage of families living in stand-alone housing.</li><li>E. European cities tend to follow the rank-size rule, while North America has mostly primate cities.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>North American cities, particularly those in the United States, have strong suburban populations where houses tend to be stand-alone and located on larger lots, making them much more spread out than in cities in Europe.</p>
</div>

## Question 676

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 676</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Current fertility rates in Europe exhibit which of the following trends?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. In most countries, fertility rates are near or below replacement level.</li><li>B. In most countries, fertility rates are slightly above replacement level.</li><li>C. Fertility rates are highly variable across the region.</li><li>D. Fertility rates are higher in countries without significant immigrant populations.</li><li>E. Fertility rates are lower in European countries that are less economically developed.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Most European countries are in stage 4 (or even stage 5) of the demographic transition model. Birth rates and fertility rates are low (at or below replacement level) as women enter into the marriage decision later in life and as women participate actively in the formal economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 677

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 677</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Reporters without Borders publishes a map of "Internet Enemies," which includes countries whose governments strictly control their populations' access to information. Which of the following countries would be included on that list?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Canada</li><li>B. Turkey</li><li>C. China</li><li>D. Venezuela</li><li>E. Poland</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>China's communist political regime limits the population's access to information through various means. One of the strategies is to censor what and how information is accessed on the Internet.</p>
</div>

## Question 678

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 678</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Indonesia, with over 13,000 islands, is considered by political geographers to be</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. compact</li><li>B. elongated</li><li>C. fragmented</li><li>D. prorupted</li><li>E. autonomous</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Geographers describe the shape of island countries separated by a water body or other feature as "fragmented." Fragmentation can be a challenge to political cohesion, especially when the physical separation coincides with different cultural or socioeconomic systems.</p>
</div>

## Question 679

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 679</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which of the following is the best example of a farmer practicing subsistence agriculture?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. John, who operates a cattle feedlot in Colorado</li><li>B. Juanita, who operates a 1,000-acre soybean farm in Argentina</li><li>C. Bold, who operates a shrimp farm in Southeast China</li><li>D. Fatima, a nomadic camel herdsman in Libya</li><li>E. Julian, a strawberry farmer in San Luis Obispo, California</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>Transhumance, or nomadic pastoralism, is a sustainable form of subsistence agriculture found primarily in different pockets of Asia. Nomadic herdsman move animals seasonally and use the animals for a wide variety of products (milk, meat, dung, leather) to support their families or tribes.</p>
</div>

## Question 680

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 680</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Deindustrialization in both North America and Europe was largely driven by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. cheaper wages in areas/regions of lower economic development</li><li>B. relaxed environmental and labor regulations overseas</li><li>C. technology and automation replacing the need for human labor in certain industries</li><li>D. none of the above</li><li>E. all of the above (A–C)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>Patterns of deindustrialization are largely driven by economic forces; industrial activities concentrate in areas where goods can be produced at the least cost (e.g., cheaper labor, lack of costly regulations) with the greatest efficiency (e.g., automation).</p>
</div>

## Question 681

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 681</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Poorer rural-to-urban migrants in Latin America are most likely to have residences or homes</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. in slums or squatter settlements</li><li>B. in single-family homes in the suburbs</li><li>C. in government-provided public housing projects</li><li>D. in high density urban apartments</li><li>E. in communal housing cooperatives</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>In Middle and South America, as depicted in the Ford Griffin Model of the Latin American City, poor urban inhabitants typically occupy areas on the outer fringes of the city, often in marginal landscapes. These migrants are searching for economic opportunity, often in the informal sector of the economy, and do not have the income to afford more established housing options.</p>
</div>

## Question 682

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 682</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Tight-knit Jewish communities can be found in the United States, Argentina, Russia, parts of Eastern Europe, and other locations across the globe. What term describes the spatial spread of this group?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Ghetto</li><li>B. Ethnic enclave</li><li>C. Diaspora</li><li>D. Localization</li><li>E. Cultural cluster</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Diaspora describes the spread of an ethnic group away from their established ancestral homeland. Often the movement is forced, but not always.</p>
</div>

## Question 683

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 683</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> During which phase in the demographic transition model would the fertility rate be at or below replacement level?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Phase 1</li><li>B. Phase 2</li><li>C. Phase 3</li><li>D. Phase 4</li><li>E. None of the phases depicted</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>Replacement fertility describes a stable population, where births are about the same as deaths. Phase 4 of demographic transition describes when a country's population growth pattern has achieved stability with low birth and low death rates.</p>
</div>

## Question 684

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 684</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Referring to the demographic transition model, the country of Nigeria with a birth rate of 36 and a death rate of 16 would be in which stage of the model?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Phase 1</li><li>B. Phase 2</li><li>C. Phase 3</li><li>D. Phase 4</li><li>E. None of the phases depicted</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>The large gap between birth and death rates in Nigeria indicates a rapidly growing population, and given its comparatively high birth rate, Nigeria fits in Phase 2 of the model.</p>
</div>

## Question 685

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 685</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Population growth in stage 4 countries is mostly attributed to ___________________ , whereas stage 2 countries typically grow as a result of ________________.</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. immigration…natural increase</li><li>B. natural increase…immigration</li><li>C. education…political incentives</li><li>D. religion…gender imbalance</li><li>E. pro-natalist policies…political turmoil</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Most countries in the developed world are at or below replacement-level fertility, meaning that, if population growth is occurring, it is most likely occurring because of immigration. In developing countries where fertility levels are higher (but decreasing), growth is attributed to natural increase.</p>
</div>

## Question 686

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 686</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> What are the problems with using GNI (Gross National Income) to measure a country's wealth?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It does not account for wealth distribution within a country.</li><li>B. It does not account for social welfare (e.g., life expectancy, access to education, etc.).</li><li>C. It does not accurately reflect the purchasing power of currency within a country.</li><li>D. All of the above are problems with using GNI as an indicator of wealth.</li><li>E. None of the above are problems; GNI makes up for these shortcomings, which is why it's now more popular than GDP.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>While Gross National Income (GNI) provides a strong indication of a country's level of wealth relative to the rest of the globe, it does not provide a full picture as it does not account for wealth distribution and access to resources within a country, which can be tremendously imbalanced.</p>
</div>

## Question 687

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 687</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Demographic information from the U.S. Census affects the political process by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. determining the amount of electoral votes given to each state</li><li>B. determining the amount of congressional delegates given to each state</li><li>C. determining the amount of aid given to various political jurisdictions</li><li>D. all of the above</li><li>E. none of the above</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>The U.S. Census provides information critical to the electoral process, since state populations determine the allocation of electoral votes and the number of representatives each receives in the House of Representatives. In addition, allocation of federal aid is often based on demographic data collected in the Census.</p>
</div>

## Question 688

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 688</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> A perceptual region's boundaries are</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. determined by a set of uniform physical or cultural characteristics across a particular area</li><li>B. drawn around the functions that occur between a particular place and the surrounding area</li><li>C. determined by the portion of a particular area that has been modified by human activities</li><li>D. fuzzy because they allow for individual interpretation</li><li>E. designated by the inclusion of a particular cultural characteristic</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>Perceptual regions are determined by commonly perceived characteristics of particular places on Earth's surface. Different individuals have different ideas about where these characteristics begin and end. Thus, the boundaries are necessarily fuzzy.</p>
</div>

## Question 689

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 689</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Multinational corporations take advantage of geographic differences in</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. wage rates</li><li>B. labor laws</li><li>C. the distribution of natural resources</li><li>D. relaxed environmental standards</li><li>E. all of the above</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>Multinational corporations, also known as transnational corporations, locate production facilities overseas to cut costs in the manufacturing process. The availability of cheap labor and more relaxed environmental and labor laws, along with greater access to natural resources, makes locating in these areas much more economically beneficial than locating in the country where the corporation is headquartered.</p>
</div>

## Question 690

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 690</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> A description of Paris as a place (rather than a space) would include</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Paris's geographic coordinates</li><li>B. the position of Paris relative to the Seine River</li><li>C. the highways connecting Paris to the rest of France</li><li>D. Parisians' love for <i>pain au chocolat</i> (chocolate croissants)</li><li>E. Paris's location relative to London</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>The concept of space simply describes a place's location, either in absolute or relative terms (or both). Descriptions of place involve unique characteristics that are essential elements of that location's identity. Parisians' love for chocolate croissants is a unique attribute of that city (even though they're also thoroughly enjoyed by tourists!).</p>
</div>

## Question 691

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 691</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which of the following social trends has had the greatest impact on urbanization rates?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Industrialization</li><li>B. Deindustrialization</li><li>C. Urban planning</li><li>D. Zoning laws</li><li>E. Central place theory</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>With industrialization, jobs concentrate in cities. With this concentration in opportunity, and the services that rise to support industry, the population within a country shifts from rural areas to cities.</p>
</div>

## Question 692

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 692</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Those who believe that the physical environment determines which cultures are going to be advanced and which cultures will remain with lower standards of living are called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. possibilists</li><li>B. neo-Malthusians</li><li>C. environmental pacifists</li><li>D. environmental determinists</li><li>E. cultural imperialists</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>Environmental determinists believe that harsh environments, such as tropical rainforests, limit certain societies' ability to advance. On the flip side, moderate climates, such as the Mediterranean climate, produces highly productive, innovative societies (according to environmental determinists).</p>
</div>

## Question 693

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 693</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> If a citizen decided to write a letter to a local legislator, in which region would that letter have the highest likelihood of being read by a female?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Europe</li><li>B. Middle East</li><li>C. Sub-Saharan Africa</li><li>D. East Asia</li><li>E. North America</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Europe, particularly countries in Northern Europe, demonstrate excellent rankings on the United Nation's Gender Development Index and Gender Empowerment Measure. Women are actively engaged in the formal economy and hold a substantial portion of government positons, particularly in comparison to women in the developing world.</p>
</div>

## Question 694

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 694</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Angeline's mom immigrated to the U.S. (from the Netherlands) in the early 1950s by boat; the trip took several days. Her cousin immigrated by plane (also from the Netherlands) in the 1980s, and it took half a day.  What phenomenon does the travel-time difference illustrate?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Relative location</li><li>B. Situation</li><li>C. Time-space convergence</li><li>D. Connectivity</li><li>E. Absolute location</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>Time-space convergence describes how the relative distance between places decreases as a result of improvements in transportation and communications technology. The U.S. became much "closer" to the Netherlands once air travel became more accessible.</p>
</div>

## Question 695

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 695</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Which of the following events was an early form of globalization?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. European colonization</li><li>B. The formation of NAFTA (North American Free Trade Agreement)</li><li>C. The invention of the Internet</li><li>D. The invention of the airplane</li><li>E. The invention of refrigeration</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>European colonization created a global network of exchange; typically raw materials flowed from the colonies to Europe, while manufactured goods flowed in the reverse. This same pattern exists in the modern era, but without official colonial rule. Raw materials typically flow from less-developed countries which have large markets for manufacturing/industrial products.</p>
</div>

## Question 696

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 696</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> When looking at labor force distribution on a global scale, which of the following patterns is generally true?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. In highly developed (rich) countries, the labor force is evenly distributed across all economic sectors (primary, secondary, tertiary, and quaternary).</li><li>B. In least-developed countries, most laborers are in service-based industries (tertiary sector).</li><li>C. The world's wealthiest countries tend to have vast natural resources, thus their labor force is predominantly primary sector (agriculture and mining).</li><li>D. Developed countries tend to concentrate in the secondary sector, while less-developed countries concentrate in primary economic activities.</li><li>E. People in poor countries tend to concentrate in primary sector economic occupations, while the labor force in richer countries concentrates in service-based sectors (tertiary and quaternary).</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: E</p><p>The least-developed countries (LDCs) have labor force concentrations in the primary sector of the economy (harvesting of raw materials), while industrial (secondary sector) activities tend to concentrate in developing economies. In highly developed regions, information-based and other services employ the largest sector of the labor force; these occupations typically require a higher-level education (and earn a greater income).</p>
</div>

## Question 697

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 697</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Which of the following agricultural techniques is used to adapt to poor soil quality in rainforest regions, such as the Amazon River basin in Brazil?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Nomadism</li><li>B. Slash and burn</li><li>C. Drip irrigation</li><li>D. Composting</li><li>E. Hydroponics</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Because rainforest soils lack nutrients, to make them agriculturally productive, farmers slash and burn existing vegetation, thereby releasing nutrients into the soil for limited period of time. Slash and burn can be sustainable provided cultivated landscapes are given enough time to regenerate.</p>
</div>

## Question 698

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 698</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> China's one child per couple population policy has had dramatic demographic ramifications. Which of the following demographic factors has NOT resulted from the implementation of this policy?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Significant imbalance between males and females</li><li>B. Loss of kinship systems (extended families)</li><li>C. Rapid rural-to-urban migration</li><li>D. Increased dependency on younger Chinese generations (as parents age)</li><li>E. Decreasing population of young people (narrowing population pyramid)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: C</p><p>While China's population has shifted from rural interior provinces to coastal urban areas, this trend did not result from the one child per couple policy. The policy did, however, lead to dramatic shifts in China's population, including population decline, changes in family dynamics, and a significant imbalance between males and females.</p>
</div>

## Question 699

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 699</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> When mass media is used to promote consumption of a particular product, it's drawing on the power of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. hierarchal diffusion</li><li>B. contagious diffusion</li><li>C. stimulus diffusion</li><li>D. channelized diffusion</li><li>E. relocation diffusion</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: B</p><p>Contagious diffusion describes trends (or other phenomena) that spread through direct exposure. Mass media, by continually bombarding individuals with advertisements for new trends, is relying on that high volume and widespread exposure to get people to buy certain products.</p>
</div>

## Question 700

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 700</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Which of the following is the BEST description of "sustainable development"?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Promotion of development strategies that encourage growth primarily in ecologically sustainable industries</li><li>B. Promotion of development strategies that will sustain economic growth in the long-term rather than the short-term</li><li>C. Promotion of development strategies that focus primarily on reaching and sustaining a replacement (or lower) fertility rate</li><li>D. Promotion of development strategies that improve current living standards without jeopardizing those of future generations</li><li>E. Promotion of development strategies that focus on integrating countries into the global economy, making countries more economically sustainable</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: D</p><p>Sustainable development initiatives focus on strategies that do not limit future generations' access to resources or their access to reasonable and healthy standards of living.</p>
</div>

## Question 701

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 701</strong></p>
<p><b>16.</b> Which of the following would NOT likely be a consideration in factory or retail location choice?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Cost of water</li><li>B. Cost of shipping</li><li>C. Taxes</li><li>D. Cost of labor</li><li>E. Government regulations</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p>Answer: A</p><p>Cost of water will be about the same regardless of location, whereas the other factors definitely show variation over distance.</p>
</div>

## Question 702

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 702</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Human geography is defined as the study of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. human interactions with the physical environment.</li><li>B. human interactions with the cultural environment.</li><li>C. human interactions with the physical and cultural environments.</li><li>D. human interactions within the natural landscape.</li><li>E. human interactions within the physical landscape.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Human geography is concerned with both the physical and cultural environments and how humans function and interact with them. Choices A, D, and E exclude the cultural environment. Choice B excludes the physical environment.</p>
</div>

## Question 703

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 703</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Cities developed 4000 to 6000 years ago to provide a center for all of the following functions EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. religion.</li><li>B. trade.</li><li>C. protection.</li><li>D. production.</li><li>E. scientific study.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—Scientific study was not a reason for the earliest cities that evolved 4000 to 6000 years ago in culture hearths where sedentary agriculture began to be practiced. They served as centers for religious worship (A), trade and commerce (B), military activities and protection (C), and for the production of commodities requiring additional workers and inputs (D).</p>
</div>

## Question 704

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 704</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Which one of the following individuals is engaged in a secondary economic activity?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A computer programmer</li><li>B. A city clerk</li><li>C. The CEO of General Motors</li><li>D. An aspirin production worker</li><li>E. A farmer</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Aspirin production workers labor in manufacturing, which is a part of the value-added secondary economic sector. Computer programmers (A) and government workers (B) are employed in the quaternary sector of the economy. High-level decision makers (C) comprise the quinary sector, and farming (E) and all agricultural activities are primary.</p>
</div>

## Question 705

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 705</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following best describes the likely impact of a large, young, single migrant population on its destination country?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. An increase in the aging population</li><li>B. An increase in births</li><li>C. A general increase in death rates</li><li>D. A decline in the carrying capacity of the host country</li><li>E. An excess of deaths over births</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—A general increase in births in the destination country is the most likely result of an influx of young migrants. Increases in the aging cohorts (A) will not occur for some time. The death rate (C) would be expected to decline—rather than rise—as a result of an influx of young migrants. The host country's carrying capacity, or the number of people an area can sustainably support, will not change. An excess of deaths over births (E) would not be expected to be a result of an influx of a large young migrant population.</p>
</div>

## Question 706

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 706</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> All of the following factors directly influence the birth rate of a country EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. government population policies.</li><li>B. the customs and family size expectations of its residents.</li><li>C. the age composition of its population.</li><li>D. government economic policies.</li><li>E. the sex composition of its inhabitants.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—The birth rate of a country is greatly and directly influenced by the population policies implemented by its government (A), by the customs and family size expectations of its population (B), and by the age and sex composition of its inhabitants (C and E). The economic policies (D) of its government have only a very indirect and variable influence on the country's birth rate.</p>
</div>

## Question 707

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 707</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> "Singapore is located on an island at the northwestern end of the Straits of Malacca adjacent to the Malay Peninsula." This statement is a description of Singapore's</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. site.</li><li>B. situation.</li><li>C. absolute location.</li><li>D. function.</li><li>E. geological history.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Situation is the relative location of a place in relation to neighboring places. Site (A) is the absolute location of a place and is usually described in physical terms using water bodies, mountains, plains, etc. Absolute location (C) is another term meaning "site." Function (D) in human geography refers to the purpose of a region or place in relation to another region or place. Geological history (E) refers to the scientific study of the Earth's history from its beginning up until now.</p>
</div>

## Question 708

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 708</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Which one of the following is not usually a reason why people move from rural areas to urban areas?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Jobs</li><li>B. Better healthcare</li><li>C. Schools</li><li>D. Safer environment</li><li>E. Cultural and social reasons</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Most people do not move from rural areas into cities to seek a safer environment in which to raise their families or live. Urban crime rates exceed rural crime rates globally; people are aware of this and base their decisions accordingly. Potential employment opportunities (A) are the hope of most rural-to-urban migrants, but while jobs used to be more available in most cities, this is increasingly not always true. Better healthcare (B), generally available in urban areas, and the potential for a better education (C) are reasons why many migrants seek city life for their families. In some cultures, such as the Latin American culture, social and cultural traditions favor life in an urban environment over a rural one.</p>
</div>

## Question 709

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 709</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> The demographic transition model</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. assumes high birth and death rates will gradually be replaced by low rates over time.</li><li>B. traces changes in fertility and mortality associated with agricultural progress.</li><li>C. consists of six stages.</li><li>D. was developed by Thomas Malthus.</li><li>E. traces the relationship between population growth and social development.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—A basic assumption of this model says high birth and death rates will drop to lower levels over time as the country develops economically. It traces changes in fertility and mortality that occur as industrialization (not agricultural development) takes place (B). Thus it shows how population growth and economic development (not social development) are linked (E). Thomas Malthus's <em>Essay</em> <em>on the Principles of Population</em> states the world's population is growing faster than the food supply (D); his predictions did not take into account the declining birth rates of the <em>demographic transition</em> <em>model</em>. The <em>demographic transition model</em> has four stages (not six), with some demographers adding a fifth stage to show a continuing drop in the crude birth rate (CBR) seen in the aging populations of wealthier countries (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 710

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 710</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> The belief that our physical environment is the chief factor influencing human thoughts, behaviors, and actions is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. environmental perception.</li><li>B. possibilism.</li><li>C. environmental determinism.</li><li>D. environmentalism.</li><li>E. a culture system.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Environmental determinism is the belief that our environment influences and controls our actions, lifestyle, and culture. Environmental perception (A) is the theory that people of different cultures look at their environments in different ways. Possibilism (B) is the theory that humans have a choice in how they think, act, and live within a range of available possibilities given to them by their physical environment. Environmentalism (D) is the movement to preserve and protect the physical environment from pollution and misuse by humans. A culture system (E) is a group of culture complexes that form the common identity of a group.</p>
</div>

## Question 711

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 711</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> The country with the largest territory is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. United States.</li><li>B. Brazil.</li><li>C. China.</li><li>D. Australia.</li><li>E. Russia.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—Russia is the largest country in terms of territory (6,591,027 square miles). Canada is the second-largest country in the world in land area. The United States (A) is third largest. China is fourth (C), Brazil fifth (B), and Australia the sixth largest (D).</p>
</div>

## Question 712

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 712</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Population pressure on an agricultural land is typically expressed as the</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. crude density.</li><li>B. arithmetic density.</li><li>C. physiological density.</li><li>D. rate of natural increase.</li><li>E. population density.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Physiological density is total population divided by arable land (area in a country that can be farmed). Crude density (A), arithmetic density (B), and population density (E) all refer to the number of people per unit of land. The rate of natural increase (D) is the birth rate minus the death rate for a population in a year's time.</p>
</div>

## Question 713

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 713</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Land in the CBD of a city is more expensive because it</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. has maximum interaction potential.</li><li>B. is more attractive.</li><li>C. has a better sense of place.</li><li>D. provides a better quality of life.</li><li>E. encompasses a larger area.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—Land in the CBD (central business district) of a city is very expensive (receives the highest bid rent) because it is the hub of the mass transit lines and is the center of the economic and social functions of the city. All public transportation routes lead to it, giving it the highest accessibility and maximum interaction potential.</p>
</div>

## Question 714

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 714</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> A political state whose territory is the same as the area occupied by people sharing a common heritage and value system is best described as a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. state.</li><li>B. country.</li><li>C. nation.</li><li>D. political state.</li><li>E. nation-state.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—A nation-state is a state or political territory with only one nation of people within its borders. Iceland and Japan are examples of nation-states because, for the most part, they contain a single nation and are homogenous. A state (A) is a political entity that occupies a definite territory with borders and full sovereignty. The United States and Thailand are examples of states. A country (B) is synonymous with a state. A nation (C) is a group of people with a common culture and history who occupy an area. A political state (D) is another term for a state.</p>
</div>

## Question 715

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 715</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Most scientists agree that the Egyptian pyramids and the Mayan temple pyramids were most likely caused by the process of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. relocation diffusion.</li><li>B. stimulus diffusion.</li><li>C. contagious diffusion.</li><li>D. hierarchical diffusion.</li><li>E. independent invention.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—While some believe there was a pre-Columbian transfer of knowledge to the Americas, the majority of scientists and anthropologists believe the Egyptian pyramids and the Mayan temple pyramids were developed independently and not by diffusion of ideas. The other answer choices describe different types of diffusion of ideas.</p>
</div>

## Question 716

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 716</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> The movement of people from Nigeria, Cameroon, Togo, and Gabon to the Americas in the sixteenth, seventeenth, and eighteenth centuries is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. chain migration.</li><li>B. circular migration.</li><li>C. cluster migration.</li><li>D. forced migration.</li><li>E. voluntary migration.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Forced migration is the involuntary historic movement of people who have no decision-making involvement in the process. Between 1519 and 1867 nearly 11 million African slaves were brought to the Americas from the countries of West Africa. The other answer choices are all forms of voluntary migration in which the immigrant makes the decision to move; most migrations are voluntary.</p>
</div>

## Question 717

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 717</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> A piece of land surrounded by a foreign territory would be viewed by the foreign territory as</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. an enclave.</li><li>B. an exclave.</li><li>C. a colony.</li><li>D. an edge city.</li><li>E. a unitary state.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—The country that surrounds another country would view the enclosed country as an enclave. Examples include the Vatican City, an enclave in Italy. An exclave (B) is a part of one country that is separated from the main part. Alaska is an exclave of the United States. A colony (C) is a territory under the control of another political state. An edge city (D) is a new urban complex outside the city center that consists of a large node of office buildings and commercial operations with more workers than residents. A unitary state (E) is a country with a strong central government, such as France.</p>
</div>

## Question 718

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 718</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> The carrying capacity of land</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. directly correlates with conditions of life there.</li><li>B. is high in many Sub-Saharan African countries.</li><li>C. is the number of people a piece of land can support in a sustainable fashion.</li><li>D. is related to social development.</li><li>E. is high in traditional slash-and-burn societies.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—The carrying capacity of land is the number of inhabitants an area of land can sustainably support given the prevailing technology. It has no direct correlation to living conditions (A) or social development (D), but is related to the level of economic development. Generally, developing countries (B) and traditional societies (E) have low carrying capacities.</p>
</div>

## Question 719

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 719</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> The Indus Valley, Egypt, West Africa, and Mesopotamia are a few examples of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. culture basins.</li><li>B. cultural convergences.</li><li>C. culture hearths.</li><li>D. culture complexes.</li><li>E. cultural divergence.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Culture hearths such as the Indus River Valley of Pakistan, the Nile River Valley of Egypt, West Africa, and Mesopotamia were birthplaces of major cultures. Culture basins (A) are basins or repositories of culture. Cultural convergence (B) refers to the tendency for cultures to become more alike as they share technologies. A culture complex (D) is a set of traits or practices that revolves around a basic activity in a culture, such as food preparation. Cultural divergence (E) is the trend for two cultures to become more different over time.</p>
</div>

## Question 720

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 720</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> The most rapidly growing minority group in the United States is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Asian.</li><li>B. Hispanic.</li><li>C. Native American.</li><li>D. Black or African American.</li><li>E. European.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—The Hispanic minority group is the fastest growing minority in the United States today. Over 50 percent of US population growth since 2000 has been due to Hispanics, and the majority of that growth is based on higher birth rates, not immigration.</p>
</div>

## Question 721

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 721</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> Using the rank-size rule, if Wood County's largest city has 200,000 residents, how many people live in Wood County's fourth-largest city?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. 75,000</li><li>B. 100,000</li><li>C. 50,000</li><li>D. 25,000</li><li>E. 10,000</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Using the rank size rule, the fourth-largest city will be one-fourth the size of the largest city; therefore, 200,000 × ? = 50,000.</p>
</div>

## Question 722

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 722</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> The Earth's surface as modified by humans is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. folk culture.</li><li>B. the carrying capacity.</li><li>C. environmental determinism.</li><li>D. the cultural landscape.</li><li>E. the physical environment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—The cultural landscape is also called the "built environment" and visibly displays human interaction with the environment. Folk culture (A) refers to the collection of culture traits of traditional societies, such as the Old Order Amish or the Hutterites. Carrying capacity (B) is the number of people a piece of land can sustainably support without ecological damage. Environmental determinism (C) is the belief that our environment influences and controls our actions, lifestyle, and culture. The physical environment (E) is the sum of everything around us in the natural world.</p>
</div>

## Question 723

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 723</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Which of the following statements correctly describes migrants today?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. They represent an accurate cross-section of their home country.</li><li>B. They represent an accurate cross-section of their destination country.</li><li>C. They include an equal number of males and females.</li><li>D. They include an equal representation from each age group.</li><li>E. They are usually young singles.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—Current research shows a majority of migrants today are young singles with the sex varying by individual case. Migrants rarely represent an accurate or representative slice of either the country they leave (A) or the country to which they are migrating (B). Migrants contribute to both the age (D) and sex (C) of their destination country in an unbalanced and irregular way.</p>
</div>

## Question 724

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 724</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Which one of the following statements does NOT correctly describe global urbanization?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The percentage of people living in cities is growing.</li><li>B. Cities are growing in size.</li><li>C. Most of the world's population will soon live in cities.</li><li>D. Most urban growth will occur in LDCs.</li><li>E. Severe environmental destruction is inevitable due to urban growth.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—The threat of severe environmental destruction caused by increasing urban populations has been overestimated by the gloomy UN prediction that megacities would bring catastrophic conditions on the Earth by the year 2015. The other choices correctly describe global urbanization.</p>
</div>

## Question 725

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 725</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> An economy in which goods and services are usually produced for internal consumption only is called a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. free market economy.</li><li>B. commercial economy.</li><li>C. planned economy.</li><li>D. command economy.</li><li>E. subsistence economy.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—Subsistence economies usually produce only enough for their population to consume with little left over to trade. Free market (A) and commercial (B) economies both refer to an economic system based on supply and demand. Planned (C) and command (D) economies both refer to an economy in which the central government makes most of the production and supply decisions.</p>
</div>

## Question 726

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 726</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> Which one of the following does NOT correctly associate a religion with its place of worship?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Shinto—shrines</li><li>B. Islam—mosques</li><li>C. Buddhism—pyramids</li><li>D. Judaism—temples</li><li>E. Christians—churches</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Buddhists do not use pyramids in their religion but instead make use of temple pagodas and shrines to various gods, especially Buddha, "the Enlightened One." They also worship at the bo (bodhi) tree. Those who practice Shinto (A) are basically animists and worship their ancestors at shrines. Muslims (B) worship in mosques, and Jews (D) worship in temples. Christians (E) of all denominations and branches worship in churches.</p>
</div>

## Question 727

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 727</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Population pyramids visually depict</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a population's age and economic composition.</li><li>B. a country's dependency ratio.</li><li>C. the ethnic composition of a population.</li><li>D. a country's population density.</li><li>E. the carrying capacity and overcrowding in a country.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—The dependency ratio is the measure of the number of economic dependents, old and young, that each 100 people in their productive years must support. The population pyramid represents a population's age and sex composition but not its economic composition (A). It does not show the ethnic composition (C), population density (D), or carrying capacity (E). The carrying capacity of a country refers to the relationship between the number of residents and the area they occupy.</p>
</div>

## Question 728

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 728</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> The French language, how to weave a basket, and the belief in ancestral spirits are all examples of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. mentifacts.</li><li>B. artifacts.</li><li>C. culture hearths.</li><li>D. culture traits.</li><li>E. dialects.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Culture traits are things that are learned by people of a certain culture. The French learn to speak French, members of certain culture groups learn to weave baskets, and some culture groups share a belief in ancestral spirits. Mentifacts (A) are the main categories of culture's values and beliefs, such as religion, language, folklore, etc. Artifacts (B) are material parts of a culture, such as houses, clothing, tools, etc. A culture hearth (C) is a location where a distinct and advanced culture originated, such as the Indus River Valley or the Nile River Valley. Dialects (E) are variations of a language such as the pronunciation of the word "started." New Englanders pronounce it as "stahted" and Southerners say "stot."</p>
</div>

## Question 729

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 729</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> The practice of judging other cultures against the standards of one's own culture is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. ethnicity.</li><li>B. assimilation.</li><li>C. ethnocentrism.</li><li>D. acculturation.</li><li>E. egocentrism.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Ethnocentrism is the practice of judging other cultures by the standards of one's own culture. Ethnicity (A) is identity in a group of people with common ancestry and culture. Assimilation (B) is the process in which people lose cultural traits as they acquire new ones from a host culture. Acculturation (D) refers to the process of adopting new cultural traits while retaining one's own cultural identity and traits. Egocentrism (E) is the view that you are the most important person in your world.</p>
</div>

## Question 730

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 730</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> Renewable fuels derived from biological materials that can be recycled are called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. renewable resources.</li><li>B. fossil fuels.</li><li>C. agricultural fuels.</li><li>D. biofuels.</li><li>E. farm products.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Biofuels like ethanol and methanol are made from biological materials that can be reproduced. Renewable resources (A) are natural resources that can be replenished. Fossil fuels (B) are fuels made from coal and petroleum—both nonrenewable resources since they require thousands of years to be created naturally from decaying organic matter. Agricultural fuels (C) are fuels like gasoline and diesel used to run farm machinery. Farm products (E) are any goods grown or produced on a farm.</p>
</div>

## Question 731

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 731</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Since 1860, death rates in Europe have declined due to all the following factors EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. improved sanitation.</li><li>B. cleaner water supplies.</li><li>C. epidemics becoming less frequent and far-reaching.</li><li>D. a lack of warfare.</li><li>E. improved nutrition and increased food supply.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—There has been no lack of warfare in Europe since 1860—two world wars and several revolutions and and a number of regional armed conflicts have ensued! After 1860, improved sanitation (A) and cleaner drinking water (B) became common in Europe's larger cities. People developed partial immunity to diseases once deadly and widespread in Europe (C). Improvements in the agricultural sector coupled with new food crops, such as the potato, stretched food supplies and increased the overall health of the population (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 732

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 732</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> All of the following factors play a role in the economic actions of humans EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. physical environment.</li><li>B. linguistic background.</li><li>C. political decisions.</li><li>D. technological development.</li><li>E. market conditions.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—While some cultural traits such as religious beliefs or food preferences determine production decisions, language does not. The physical environment (A) controls economic activity by limiting the type and availability of natural resources at a population's disposal. A government's decisions (C) to encourage (through tariffs and subsidies) or discourage economic activities (by limiting production, for example) greatly influence economic activities. The technology (D) available to a society also guides economic activities of a population. Market conditions of supply and demand (E), whether in a free market or government-controlled economy, strongly influence economic production.</p>
</div>

## Question 733

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 733</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Which one of the following is an example of a formal region?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. The US Corn Belt</li><li>B. Northwest Airlines</li><li>C. Dixie</li><li>D. Retailing region of Chicago</li><li>E. The Midwest</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—A formal or uniform region is one that is consistent in one physical or cultural characteristic, such as production of corn. Northwest Airlines (B) and the retailing district of Chicago (D) are functional, or nodal, regions of interdependency and have a core and a periphery. Dixie (C) and the Midwest (E) are vernacular, or perceptual, regions based on the way people perceive or feel about them.</p>
</div>

## Question 734

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 734</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Which type of land use would you expect to find along high-volume mass transit lines?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Big box retail stores</li><li>B. High-density apartment complexes</li><li>C. Skyscraper office complexes</li><li>D. A scrap yard</li><li>E. An industrial plant</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—High-density apartment complexes, along with retailing centers, malls, and light industries are typically located along high-volume transportation routes. Big box retail stores like Target and Walmart (A) are usually located on the outskirts of the city in suburban areas along major highway transportation corridors. Skyscraper office complexes (C) and major hotels are usually located in the fringes of the CBD. A scrap yard (D) would probably be found beside a railroad or other cargo route. An industrial plant (E) would probably be located near a waterfront, railroad, or other cargo route for easy shipment of both raw materials and finished products.</p>
</div>

## Question 735

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 735</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following is NOT an example of a compact state?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Uruguay</li><li>B. Thailand</li><li>C. Laos</li><li>D. Zimbabwe</li><li>E. Poland</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Thailand is a good example of a prorupt state, or one which is mainly compact but has a long, narrow extension or peninsula. Uruguay (A), Laos (C), Zimbabwe (D), and Poland (E) are all compact states—states with a rounded, or circular, shape.</p>
</div>

## Question 736

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 736</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> The use of seed agriculture, the plow, and draft animals started the</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. First Agricultural Revolution.</li><li>B. Second Agricultural Revolution.</li><li>C. Third Agricultural Revolution.</li><li>D. Fourth Agricultural Revolution.</li><li>E. Green Revolution.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—The use of seed agriculture, the plow, and draft animals allowed humans to greatly expand food production, and these innovations occurred during the First Agricultural Revolution. Each of the succeeding agricultural revolutions (B, C, D, and E) was marked by improved methods and factors that led to increased food supplies.</p>
</div>

## Question 737

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 737</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which one of the following does NOT correctly associate a province of Canada with a large immigrant population concentration?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. British Columbia—Chinese</li><li>B. Quebec—French</li><li>C. Ontario—British</li><li>D. Nova Scotia—Italian</li><li>E. Saskatchewan—Ukraine</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Nova Scotia is largely populated by immigrants of British descent, and the overwhelming majority of new immigrants to the province are from the United Kingdom. The other answer choices are all correct in associating the province with a large ethnic immigrant population living in the province.</p>
</div>

## Question 738

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 738</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Which statement below most accurately describes the relationship depicted in the figure below?</p><p><img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/a5/f0002-01.jpg"/></p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. One unit on the Earth's surface equals 24,000 units on the map.</li><li>B. One unit on the map equals 24,000 units on the Earth's surface.</li><li>C. One mile equals 7000 feet on the map.</li><li>D. One mile equals 24,000 units on the map.</li><li>E. One mile equals 24,000 units on the Earth's surface.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—The representative fraction given at the top of the diagram tells us that 24,000 units on the Earth's surface are represented by one unit on the map. In other words, 24,000 feet on the Earth's surface would be one foot on the map. The other answer choices all incorrectly interpret the relationship depicted in the diagram.</p>
</div>

## Question 739

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 739</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Using von Thünen's model of rural land use, which of the following agricultural products would be produced farthest from an urban market?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Fruits</li><li>B. Butter and eggs</li><li>C. Corn for cattle feed</li><li>D. Vegetables</li><li>E. Wool</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—Wool would be raised farthest from an urban market since sheep ranching requires lots of grazing land but has lower transportation costs than dairying (B), corn farming (C), or raising more perishable crops such as fruits and vegetables (A and D).</p>
</div>

## Question 740

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 740</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> National anthems, flags, and holidays are all symbols that promote</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. irredentism.</li><li>B. nationalism.</li><li>C. supranationalism.</li><li>D. regionalism.</li><li>E. war.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Nationalism is a strong identification with one's country and what it stands for. National anthems, flags, national holidays, memorials, and even national sports teams all cement one's loyalty to a sovereign state and are strong centripetal forces in a country. Irredentism (A) is the claim by a country's government that an ethnic minority living in another country belongs to the homeland country. Strong irredentist unrest led to a war when Serbia stirred the fires of irredentism in Croatia among the ethnic Serb minority living there in the 1980s and 1990s. Supranationalism (C) is the current global trend for many countries to join organizations for a common goal or good. The United Nations is a well-known supranational organization. Regionalism (D) often develops when a minority group forms a majority in one region of a country and identifies more closely with its group than with the country. War (E) is not promoted by a flag or national symbol. Such iconography may stir nationalism in times of war, but these items do not encourage or promote war in themselves.</p>
</div>

## Question 741

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 741</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> The birth rate of any country is greatly influenced by all the factors below EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. religious beliefs.</li><li>B. the age structure of population.</li><li>C. the government's population policies.</li><li>D. disease.</li><li>E. the sex structure of population.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—While disease is a factor in the general health of a country's population, it is not an important influence on the birth rate. Religious beliefs (A), the age and sex composition of its population (B and E), and the population policies of the country (C) are the strongest influences on a country's birth rate.</p>
</div>

## Question 742

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 742</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which one of the following does NOT correctly characterize agribusiness?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A system</li><li>B. A set of relationships to organize food production from seed to loaf of bread</li><li>C. A large corporate entity</li><li>D. A global enterprise</li><li>E. A business enterprise driven by the fast food industry</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Agribusiness is not a new or single corporate entity but rather a system (A) that involves a complex set of interrelationships to organize food production (B). It is a global enterprise (D) that is driven in large part by the global fast food industry (E), which requires low-priced farm products to be competitive and profitable.</p>
</div>

## Question 743

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 743</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Which of the following statements correctly describes world population distribution?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. World population is evenly distributed.</li><li>B. More than one-half the world's population lives between 60 degrees and 80 degrees north of the equator.</li><li>C. Less than half of the world's population lives north of the equator.</li><li>D. A large majority of the world's population lives on a small part of the world's surface.</li><li>E. The world's population increases sharply with an increase in surface elevation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—More than half of the world's population is concentrated on only 5 percent of the world's land area and two-thirds lives on only 10 percent of the land area. The world's population, in fact, is very unevenly distributed (A) with some parts of the world uninhabited and others very densely populated. The area between 60 degrees and 80 degrees north of the equator is sparsely inhabited because of a very cold climate (B). Over half the world's population lives north of the equator (C). The world's population drastically decreases in numbers with increases in elevation because of increasingly unfavorable living conditions (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 744

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 744</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> On which continent would you most likely find large statues of Christ (Cristo Rey) overlooking cities from hilltops such as the one shown in the photo below?</p><p><img src="https://img.crackap.com/ap/human-geography/a5/f0003-01.jpg"/></p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. North America</li><li>B. South America</li><li>C. Europe</li><li>D. Asia</li><li>E. Australia</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—There are a number of large Christ the Redeemer (Cristo Rey) statues in South America usually placed on hillsides above cities. There is one in the United States and another in Europe, but the majority are found in South America and are a testament to the widespread Roman Catholic faith on that continent.</p>
</div>

## Question 745

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 745</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> The almost continuous strip of urban centers that extends along the US Atlantic coast from north of Boston to southern Virginia is commonly called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. megalopolis.</li><li>B. megacity.</li><li>C. super city.</li><li>D. oligopolies.</li><li>E. triceratops.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—Megalopolis refers to an almost 600-mile-long conurbation stretching from southern Maine to southern Virginia. Several cities and their industrial and market-oriented businesses make up this conurbation. Megacity (B) is a term created in the 1970s to apply to very large cities with a population of 10 million or more that many thought would overwhelm the world's resources. Supercity (C) is the term given to Auckland, New Zealand, by its residents as the city boundaries continue to extend into the neighboring hinterlands, swallowing nearby towns and smaller cities. There is no such term as oligopolis (D), and a triceratops (E) is a species of extinct dinosaur.</p>
</div>

## Question 746

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 746</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Which of the following political state shapes would likely be the most efficient for transportation and communication?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Compact</li><li>B. Prorupt</li><li>C. Elongated</li><li>D. Fragmented</li><li>E. Perforated</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—A compact state would have lower transportation and communication costs within the state, leading to more efficient transportation and communication systems. This can lead to greater cohesion among its population. A prorupt state (B) is mainly compact with a narrow extension protruding out of it. An elongated state (C) is long and narrow like Chile or Norway. A fragmented state (D) is composed of more than one disconnected piece of territory. Examples include island states such as Indonesia and the Philippines, as well as states like Italy with regions on both the mainland and on islands. All these shapes of states can be expected to have less efficient transportation and communication systems than a compact state.</p>
</div>

## Question 747

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 747</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Graveyards and cemeteries are NOT used by</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Christians.</li><li>B. Jews.</li><li>C. Hindus.</li><li>D. Muslims.</li><li>E. Animists.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Both Hindu and Buddhist faiths cremate their dead and do not bury the deceased in graveyards or cemeteries. Christians (A), Jews (B), Muslims (D), and most animists (E) make use of graveyards and cemeteries for burial of their dead.</p>
</div>

## Question 748

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 748</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> A dress store, a shoe store, and a jewelry store located on the same block close to each other is an example of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. purchasing power parity.</li><li>B. agglomeration.</li><li>C. deglomeration.</li><li>D. an urban heat island.</li><li>E. concentric zone.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Agglomeration is process in which businesses cluster together to take advantage of infrastructure or markets. These three stores would likely locate near one another to attract shoppers who might also be interested in their goods. Deglomeration (C) refers to the spreading out of businesses because of crowding and other negatives. Purchasing power parity (A) refers to a formula used to compare the value of a product in various countries. Urban heat islands (D) refer to the increase in temperatures found in urban areas because of increased pavement, population density, and industrial activity. Concentric zones (E) are neighboring zones radiating outward in rings. The <em>concentric zone model</em> was developed to explain the urban housing patterns in American cities in the 1920s.</p>
</div>

## Question 749

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 749</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Which one of the following is NOT a common reason for state boundary disputes?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Resources</li><li>B. Territories</li><li>C. Linguistic differences</li><li>D. Documents defining boundaries</li><li>E. Exclusive economic zones (EEZs)</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Linguistic differences are not generally enough to stimulate a heated boundary dispute. Boundary disputes between countries are usually over resources (A), territories they both claim (B), the interpretation of the legal documents that define the boundary between the two (D), or exclusive economic zones (EEZs) offshore (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 750

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 750</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which of the following central place functions is most likely to have the highest range of goods and also the highest threshold population?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A dry cleaner</li><li>B. A Chinese restaurant</li><li>C. An elementary school</li><li>D. A cancer treatment clinic</li><li>E. A flower shop</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—A central place function with a high range and high threshold would need a specialized group of customers and workers for its services. A cancer treatment clinic provides a special service to certain sick patients who would be willing to travel a great distance to receive their treatment. The other answer choices list services that would have a lower threshold population since they do not require as large a population in order to support their supply of services in their local community.</p>
</div>

## Question 751

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 751</strong></p>
