<p><b>5.</b> The belief that people, not their surroundings, are the forces behind cultural development is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. environmental perception.</li><li>B. possibilism.</li><li>C. environmental determinism.</li><li>D. environmentalism.</li><li>E. a culture system.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Possibilism is the theory that humans have a choice in how they think, act, and live within a range of available possibilities given to them by their physical environment. Environmental perception (A) is the theory that people of different cultures look at their environments in different ways. Environmental determinism (C) is the belief that our environment influences and controls our actions, lifestyle, and culture. Environmentalism (D) is the movement to preserve and protect the physical environment from pollution and misuse by humans. A culture system (E) is a group of culture complexes that form the common identity of a group.</p>
</div>

## Question 752

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 752</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> The conflict in Kashmir is based on which type of boundary disagreement?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Fertile ground</li><li>B. Land use</li><li>C. Irredentism</li><li>D. Document interpretation</li><li>E. Immigration</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—The conflict in Kashmir is irredentist, therefore territorial in nature, as the Muslim majority in this Indian-controlled territory long to become part of Pakistan. Fertile ground (A) is a resource issue, land use (B), and immigration (E) are functional issues of contention on some borders, and document interpretation (D) is a boundary disagreement based on differing interpretations of how the boundary was defined in writing.</p>
</div>

## Question 753

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 753</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> Dishes, axes, knives, and toys are examples of</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. tools.</li><li>B. artifacts.</li><li>C. mentifacts.</li><li>D. sociofacts.</li><li>E. the built environment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Artifacts are the material elements of a culture, such as tools, dishes, knives, toys, etc. Tools (A) do not include all the artifacts of a culture, such as toys. Mentifacts (C) are the core elements of a culture and remain relatively constant, evolving only very slowly over time. These include language, religion, and traditions. Sociofacts (D) are the connections between people in a culture and include religious, political, and educational institutions, as well as family and community linkages. The built environment (E) is the material culture of a group, including buildings, roads, and whatever humans have constructed in their environment.</p>
</div>

## Question 754

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 754</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> Which one of the following is an example of a vernacular region?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. New Hampshire</li><li>B. Bible Belt</li><li>C. Urban zone of working and shopping for Pittsburgh</li><li>D. Little Italy</li><li>E. Texas</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Little Italy is an urban ethnic community whose residents define themselves as Italian. Answer choices A, B, and E are formal regions defined by a political boundary (New Hampshire and Texas) or a cultural feature (Christianity). The urban working and shopping zone of Pittsburgh (C) is a functional region with a core and a periphery.</p>
</div>

## Question 755

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 755</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Which urban model was developed to explain the patterns of American cities in the 1920s?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Concentric zone model</li><li>B. Central place model</li><li>C. Urban realms model</li><li>D. Sector model</li><li>E. Multiple-nuclei model</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—The <em>concentric zone model</em> depicts the city as a set of rings radiating out from the CBD and was developed to explain the social patterns of American cities in the 1920s. The central place model (B) was developed by German geographer Walter Christaller in 1933 to explain the patterns and distributions of settlements as they are interconnected with their surrounding hinterlands. The urban realms model (C) is an economic model that states an urban resident's life is mainly lived in one realm within the urban environment. The sector model (D) views urban housing like spokes radiating from a central hub. It states that new housing for the wealthy extends outward on its original axis from the city as it grows, middle-income housing extends in the same way next to higher-income sectors, and lower-income housing fills in the gaps. The <em>multiple-nuclei model</em> (E) states that large cities spread out from several nodes of growth, not just one.</p>
</div>

## Question 756

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 756</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> A suburb is</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. often characterized by sprawl.</li><li>B. the same thing as central city.</li><li>C. a conurbation.</li><li>D. exclusively residential.</li><li>E. separate and not integrated with urban areas nearby.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—Suburbs are often characterized by "sprawl" or a tendency to spread over time. Central city (B) refers to the central business district (CBD) that is found at the heart of every city. A conurbation (C) is a continuous urban area that has grown to consume what were once separate cities. Many suburbs contain shopping and other facilities as well as homes (D). Suburbs are generally on the outskirts of metropolitan areas and are well integrated with them (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 757

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 757</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which one of the following statements does NOT correctly describe truck farming?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. It is the main type of farming in Georgia and Florida.</li><li>B. Truck farm produce is shipped long distances.</li><li>C. Truck farming employs low-cost labor.</li><li>D. Mechanization is rarely used.</li><li>E. Highly perishable crops like lettuce and strawberries are common.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—The large-scale agribusinesses that dominate truck farming are highly mechanized. Machinery is used to plant, irrigate, and harvest the crop. Truck farming is big business in California, Florida, and in southeastern states such as Georgia (A). Produce grown on truck farms is often shipped to areas where these crops cannot be grown as easily, if at all (B). Large-scale commercialized farms employ migrant workers who are less costly (C). Perishable fruit and vegetable crops are common crops of truck farming (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 758

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 758</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> Which of the following national capitals is NOT a forward-thrust capital?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Brasilia, Brazil</li><li>B. Abuja, Nigeria</li><li>C. Islamabad, Pakistan</li><li>D. Paris, France</li><li>E. Astana, Kazakhstan</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Paris, France, is not a forward-thrust capital. All the other answer choices list forward-thrust capitals located on a frontier as a magnet for development or on a contested border as a stance of power.</p>
</div>

## Question 759

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 759</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> Which economic sector of the city furnishes goods and services to the larger economy outside the city?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Basic</li><li>B. Non-basic</li><li>C. White collar</li><li>D. Suburban</li><li>E. Blue collar</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—Basic jobs in a city's economy generate income for the city by producing goods or services for "export" out of the city. Non-basic jobs (B) provide services to the city's workers and do not usually generate "new" income for the city. White-collar jobs (C) are desk jobs or clerical jobs that require more mental and less physical activity than blue-collar (E), or physical jobs. Suburban (D) refers to the residential communities surrounding American cities and not to an economic sector.</p>
</div>

## Question 760

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 760</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> The attachments we have to a specific location and its characteristics is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. placelessness.</li><li>B. sense of place.</li><li>C. location.</li><li>D. cultural landscape.</li><li>E. connectivity.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—A sense of place is the feelings of attachment we have to a specific location. Placelessness (A) refers to the absence of distinct characteristics that might make a location special or unique. Location (C) is a description of where a place is. The cultural landscape (D) defines the Earth's surface as modified by human hands. Connectivity (E) refers to the tangible (highway systems) and intangible (radio waves) ways that places are connected.</p>
</div>

## Question 761

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 761</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> The charter group of Quebec, Canada, was the</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. British.</li><li>B. Germans.</li><li>C. French.</li><li>D. Irish.</li><li>E. Spanish.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—A charter group is the first ethnic group to arrive and start the first effective settlement in a new area. They establish the recognized cultural norms that groups arriving later must follow. The French came to Quebec, Canada, during the seventeenth century to establish a fur trade with the Native Americans and to spread the Catholic faith. Today 75 percent of Quebec's population is of French lineage. Quebec maintains a distinctive Francophone identity distinct from the rest of Canada.</p>
</div>

## Question 762

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 762</strong></p>
<p><b>1.</b> Which model below is based on the assumption that growth happens around several major foci, not just the CBD?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Central place model</li><li>B. Concentric zone model</li><li>C. Urban realms model</li><li>D. Sector model</li><li>E. Multiple-nuclei model</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—The <em>multiple-nuclei model</em> states that large cities spread out from several nodes of growth, not just one. The central place model (B) was developed by German geographer Walter Christaller in 1933 to explain the patterns and distributions of settlements as they are interconnected with their surrounding hinterlands. The <em>concentric zone model</em> (B) depicts the city as a set of rings radiating out from the CBD and was developed to explain the social patterns of American cities in the 1920s. The urban realms model (C) is an economic model that states an urban resident's life is mainly lived in one realm within the urban environment. The sector model (D) views urban housing like spokes radiating from a central hub (the CBD). It states that new housing for the wealthy extends outward on its original axis from the city as it grows, middle-income housing extends in the same way next to the higher-income sector, and lower-income housing fills in the gaps.</p>
</div>

## Question 763

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 763</strong></p>
<p><b>2.</b> Which one of the following economic activities is primary?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Pottery production</li><li>B. Electronic assembly</li><li>C. Hydroelectric production</li><li>D. Mining</li><li>E. Selling items on eBay</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—Primary activities such as mining, agriculture, fishing, forestry, and quarrying, involve humans harvesting crops or removing materials from the earth. Pottery production (A), electronic assembly (B), and hydroelectric production (C) are secondary activities that add value to the original material. Internet sales (E) and other retail and wholesale activities involving the business, financial, professional, or clerical sectors are tertiary activities.</p>
</div>

## Question 764

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 764</strong></p>
<p><b>3.</b> Population growth reflects all of the following factors EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. birth rates.</li><li>B. death rates.</li><li>C. migration.</li><li>D. age structure.</li><li>E. calculation of the doubling time.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> E</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>E</strong>—Doubling time is calculated by dividing the country's growth rate (as a percent) into 70. These calculations should never be relied on to accurately predict the future size of a population. Birth rates (A), death rates (B), migration (C), and age structure (D) are all important factors affecting the growth of a population.</p>
</div>

## Question 765

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 765</strong></p>
<p><b>4.</b> Which country below has the highest concentration of Buddhists?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. Brazil</li><li>B. Vietnam</li><li>C. France</li><li>D. Russia</li><li>E. Iran</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Vietnam practices the Mahayana, the most dominant form of Buddhism. Buddhism diffused to Vietnam during the second century <small>B.C.</small> from India, China, and Central Asia. The other answer choices list countries with only very small minorities of Buddhists. Brazil (A) is a Roman Catholic country. France (C) is nominally Roman Catholic, although in reality it is a very secular country (recent polls show most French seldom attend church). About 80 percent of the Russian population (D) belongs to the Russian Orthodox church, but the Muslim population is rapidly increasing and Islam is Russia's second largest religion. Iran (E) is a Shi'ite Muslim country.</p>
</div>

## Question 766

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 766</strong></p>
<p><b>5.</b> What type of land use would you expect to find near the railroad yards?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A Macy's department store</li><li>B. A Walmart</li><li>C. The Wells Fargo Bank headquarters</li><li>D. A steel mill</li><li>E. A penthouse apartment</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> D</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>D</strong>—You would expect to see a steel mill near a railroad yard for cargo reception and product transport. The other choices would not typically be found near a railroad yard.</p>
</div>

## Question 767

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 767</strong></p>
<p><b>6.</b> Which region of China marked on the map above has the highest population density?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A</li><li>B. B</li><li>C. C</li><li>D. D</li><li>E. E</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—The eastern coastal region of China has a population density of over 400 per square kilometer—twice the density of the second-highest which is the central region. The arid basins and deserts of western China (A) and the high, cold mountains of the Tibetan Plateau (E) have very low population densities of less than 10 people per kilometer. Regions B and D represent regions of intermediate population densities.</p>
</div>

## Question 768

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 768</strong></p>
<p><b>7.</b> In which region of China are the special economic zones (SEZ's) located?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. A</li><li>B. B</li><li>C. C</li><li>D. D</li><li>E. E</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—The Special Economic Zones (SEZs) of China's east coast enjoy relaxed trade laws that stimulate China's economy.</p>
</div>

## Question 769

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 769</strong></p>
<p><b>8.</b> The latitude and longitude coordinates of a place refer to its</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. absolute location.</li><li>B. relative location.</li><li>C. distance.</li><li>D. situation.</li><li>E. scale.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—Latitude and longitude are the exact location of a place on the Earth's surface in degrees, minutes, and seconds and represent its absolute location. Relative location (B) refers to where a place is in relation to other places. Distance (C) is the space between two points on the Earth's surface, and situation (D) is the relative location of a place in terms of its physical and cultural features. Scale (E) is the frame of reference for studying something. It is also the size of a unit on a map as a ratio to the same number of units on the Earth's surface.</p>
</div>

## Question 770

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 770</strong></p>
<p><b>9.</b> Total fertility rates</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. are increasing in most European countries.</li><li>B. are increasing in Asian countries.</li><li>C. slightly higher than two are at replacement level.</li><li>D. reflect biological constraints.</li><li>E. reflect the level of industrialization in a country.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Total fertility rates of 2.1 to 2.3 are required to replace a country's population and have been declining steadily in both European (A) and Asian (B) countries over the last decades. The total fertility rate reflects the cultural values of a country and the reproductive behaviors of its women. It does not directly reflect either biological constraints (D) or the level of industrialization (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 771

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 771</strong></p>
<p><b>10.</b> The worldwide trend towards using biofuels has caused all the following to occur EXCEPT</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a decrease in use of fossil fuels.</li><li>B. a rise in global food prices.</li><li>C. the conversion of small farms to large monoculture plantations.</li><li>D. violence.</li><li>E. the eviction of small farmers.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—The development of biofuels has not caused a decrease in the use of fossil fuels as hoped; worldwide consumption of fossil fuels continues to grow, although at a slower pace than it would if biofuels had not been developed. However, the development of biofuels has caused a rise in global food prices as some farmland that used to grow food now produces crops for biofuels (B). In some parts of the world, the transfer of farmland to the production of crops for biofuels has also resulted in the conversion of small farms to large monoculture plantations (C), violence (D), and the eviction of small farmers (E).</p>
</div>

## Question 772

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 772</strong></p>
<p><b>11.</b> Which one of the following factors has NOT contributed to the explosive spread of infectious disease?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. World trade expansion</li><li>B. Increased investment in sanitation and healthcare</li><li>C. Migration</li><li>D. Growing global tourism</li><li>E. Rapid population growth</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> B</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>B</strong>—Increased investment in sanitation and government healthcare programs and has worked to decrease the spread of infectious diseases like pneumonia and malaria. The other factors have all contributed to the global spread of infectious disease by increasing contact between people throughout the world.</p>
</div>

## Question 773

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 773</strong></p>
<p><b>12.</b> A group of people with a common culture and history who occupy an area are called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. a state.</li><li>B. a country.</li><li>C. a nation.</li><li>D. a political state.</li><li>E. a nation-state.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—A nation is a group of people with a common culture and history who occupy an area. A state (A) is a political entity that occupies a definite territory with borders and full sovereignty. A country (B) is synonymous with a state. A political state is another term for a state (D). A nation-state (E) is a state with only one nation of people within its borders.</p>
</div>

## Question 774

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 774</strong></p>
<p><b>13.</b> The outer boundary of a linguistic feature on a map is called</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. an isogloss.</li><li>B. a dialect.</li><li>C. a toponym.</li><li>D. a vernacular.</li><li>E. a creole.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> A</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>A</strong>—An isogloss is the geographic boundary limit for a linguistic trait. An example is the geographic boundary between the US region where the word "hoagie" is used and the word "grinder" is used. Dialects (B) are different spoken regional versions of the same language. They usually vary in pronunciation, rhythm, and speed. A toponym (C) is a place name such as Cropp's Corners or Oil City. Vernacular (D) refers to the local, nonstandard language spoken in a place. Creole (E) is a language that began as a pidgin language and graduated to a permanent language.</p>
</div>

## Question 775

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 775</strong></p>
<p><b>14.</b> The relationship between the size or length of a map attribute and the same attribute on Earth's surface is called a</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. mental map.</li><li>B. projection.</li><li>C. scale.</li><li>D. density.</li><li>E. model.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Scale is the relationship between the size of an element on the map and the same element on the Earth's surface. A mental map (A) refers to the images in one's mind about an area. A projection (B) is the method used to represent the Earth's curved surface on a flat piece of paper (map). Density (D) is defined as the quantity of something per unit on a map. A model (E) is a simplified representation of reality and is used often in human geography to study cause-and-effect relationships.</p>
</div>

## Question 776

<div class="mcontent">
<p><strong>Question: 776</strong></p>
<p><b>15.</b> Which of the following jobs would NOT be considered a quaternary economic activity?</p>
<ul class="qlist">
<li>A. IRS employee</li><li>B. College professor</li><li>C. Insurance salesman</li><li>D. Computer programmer</li><li>E. Research scientist</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Correct Answer:</strong> C</p>
<p><strong>Explanation:</strong></p>
<p><strong>C</strong>—Sales jobs are a tertiary economic activity. All the other answer choices list "white collar" and professional jobs in the quaternary sector.</p>
</div>
